1801 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Det. of Brock


No. 53881-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


126 Wn. App. 957; 110 P.3d 791; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 646



April 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Personal Restraint of Brock, 78 Wn. App. 1012, 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 878 (1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found to be a sexually violent predator under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09 and committed to a special commitment center. Years later, he filed a pro se petition for unconditional discharge. The Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) denied defendant's petition for unconditional discharge, concluding that the State presented proof that he continued to meet the requirement for commitment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.090(2)(b) violated due process by allowing the State to rely solely on the annual report to show that he continued to meet the definition of a sexually violent predator. The appellate court disagreed, holding that Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.090(2)(b) permitted the State to rely on annual reports without presenting additional evidence at the show cause hearing. The statute did not violate due process because existing show cause hearing procedures sufficiently minimized the risk of an erroneous deprivation of defendant's liberty interest, and the probable value of cross-examination at a show cause hearing was minimal. Defendant had sufficient avenues at his disposal to gather evidence to show that his condition had "so changed" that total commitment was no longer warranted. While cross-examination of the State's experts at a show cause hearing could conceivably have elicited information helpful to defendant, he could do the same thing by using the civil discovery rules.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1802 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Dagg v. Spokane Pub. Sch. Dist. No. 81


No. 22988-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 543



April 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Dagg v. Spokane Pub. Sch. Dist. No. 81, 126 Wn. App. 1055, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1404 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-2-04493-2. Judge signing: JEROME J. LEVEQUE. Date filed: April 8, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, granted respondent school district summary dismissal, holding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction in appellant tutors' action concerning their continuing contract rights with the school district. The trial court found that the tutors did not appeal the school district's decision on their contract rights within 30 days as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.645.010. The tutors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tutors claimed that Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.645.010 did not apply to them, but even if it did, they substantially complied with it. In the alternative, they argued that the 30-day statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court noted that if the tutors were categorized as employees, they were entitled to a continuing contract. Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.405.010 applied to actions styled as declaratory judgment suits in which the litigant sought a favorable construction of statutory terms involving their employment benefits. The tutors' filing on July 11, 2003 was untimely as the contracts were signed on June 9, 2003; the 30 days would expire on July 9. The statute did not treat district employees and non-employees differently. It was not unlike any appellate rule that limited the time for appeal. The tutors had no property interest at stake. The legislature did not provide a specific right to have notice of the appeal requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.645.010. The school district's failure to notify the tutors that they had to appeal its decision within the 30-day period required by the statute did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1803 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walton


No. 30215-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 568



April 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 01-1-00045-8. Date filed: 04/08/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Gary R. Tabor.
State v. Walton, 126 Wn. App. 1051, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1390 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of first degree incest. The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court previously remanded for the sentencing court to supplement the record with the presentence investigation (PSI) report and to determine whether defendant's unscored misdemeanor convictions warranted an exceptional sentence. Defendant argued that his exceptional sentence was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the sentencing court relied on an unproven fact to support the exceptional sentence. Neither Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090 nor Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.68A explicitly defined "immoral purposes" or "communicates," but case law held that "immoral purposes" referred to sexual misconduct and "communicates" included conduct as well as words. Because defendant's conduct leading to the prior conviction could have involved a broad range of conduct, the sentencing court's finding that he had sex with a minor was never proven nor admitted. The sentence court improperly relied on facts not necessarily proven at the prior adjudication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for resentencing within the standard range.

 

1804 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clarke


No. 52289-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 501



March 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Clarke, 126 Wn. App. 1038, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1279 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-1-02089-1. Judge signing: Hon. Robert H Alsdorf. Date filed: 04/04/2003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of child molestation in the first degree and sentenced him to life in prison with no parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.94A.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child molestation in the first degree and was sentenced to life in prison with no parole under the POAA. He had three prior convictions: two counts of indecent liberties and one count of assault in the second-degree with sexual motivation, all committed against boys. He alleged prosecutorial misconduct, ineffective assistance of counsel, and challenges the POAA on several constitutional bases, but the court affirmed on appeal. Assuming without deciding that the prosecutor's comments in question were improper, defendant failed to show that they likely affected the jury's verdict. In addition, he did not show that the comments about defense counsel "confusing" the child witness were so flagrant and ill-intentioned that a curative instruction would have been useless. Counsel was not ineffective pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. VI because the evidence sought to be admitted was properly excluded since it was irrelevant, improper, and beyond the scope of a detective's testimony. His sentence was neither cruel nor unusual because he was a repeat offender who had been convicted of indecent acts against four different young boys.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1805 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Bergen Indus. & Fishing Corp. v. Joint Stock Holding Co. Dalmoreproduct


No. 53351-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 509



March 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-2-35169-9. Judge signing: Hon. Michael J Fox. Date filed: 11/07/2003.
Bergen Indus. & Fishing Corp. v. Joint Stock Holding Co., 126 Wn. App. 1039, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1281 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent corporation, a judgment creditor, registered its foreign judgment and used procedures in Wash. Rev. Code ch. 6.27 to obtain several ex parte, post-judgment writs of garnishment. One of these was served on a Seattle bank that held funds for the judgment debtor in the name of a third party, appellant company. The Superior Court of King County, Washington, awarded half the frozen funds to the corporation. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the company contended, inter alia, that Wash. Rev. Code § 6.27.060 was unconstitutional and that the lower court impermissibly stayed an order and granted an injunction. The appellate court found that the company had no standing to make its constitutional challenge as it was not an aggrieved party. Although the trial court concluded that the company and the judgment debtor were not the same legal entity, it had the power to issue a stay of execution on its judgment. At the time the trial court granted the company's summary judgment motion, there was significant evidence in the record that some or all of the funds in the company's garnished accounts were actually the property of the judgment debtor. There was not "judgment" against the company in favor of the corporation as the corporation's claim was that the company was in possession of the judgment debtor's funds, and that the corporation was the judgment creditor. No alternative remedy of a suit at law was present because the corporation was not suing the company on the basis of the company's personal obligations to the corporation. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the injunction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1806 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kinlow


No. 22863-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 470



March 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-1-03028-8. Judge signing: NEAL Q. RIELLY. Date filed: March 18, 2004.
State v. Kinlow, 126 Wn. App. 1037, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1274 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant of second degree assault, first degree malicious mischief, and harassment. The trial court imposed exceptional sentences on his convictions except for the harassment conviction, wherein defendant received a standard range 12-month sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed solely the exceptional sentences. The appellate court noted that the trial court based the exceptional sentences on its findings of multiple uncharged victims, and the emotional impact the attack had on defendant's ex-wife. Because those facts were not admitted by defendant, nor found beyond a reasonable doubt by a jury, defendant's exceptional sentences violated the Sixth Amendment. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535 did not contain the necessary process due defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's exceptional sentence was vacated and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1807 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kinlow


No. 22863-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1347



March 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 8, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-1-03028-8. Judge signing: NEAL Q. RIELLY. Date filed: March 18, 2004.
State v. Kinlow, 126 Wn. App. 1037, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1274 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, imposing exceptional sentences for second degree assault and first degree malicious mischief.


OVERVIEW: The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence of 48 months for second degree assault, including 12 months for a weapons enhancement, and ordered an exceptional sentence of 36 months for first degree malicious mischief. Defendant received a standard range 12-month sentence for his harassment conviction. Because the facts increasing the penalties beyond the statutory maximums were not submitted to the jury, the parties agreed defendant's exceptional sentences were unconstitutional. The trial court based the exceptional sentence upon its findings of multiple uncharged victims, including defendant's former wife, and the emotional impact she suffered. Since these facts were not admitted by defendant nor found beyond a reasonable doubt by a jury, defendant's exceptional sentences violated the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The sentences were vacated, and the matter was remanded for further sentencing proceedings.

 

1808 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Knight v. State


No. 54129-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 483



March 21, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-2-27325-2. Date filed: 3/19/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Richard a Jones.
Knight v. Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs., 126 Wn. App. 1033, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1259 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which affirmed a decision of the Office of Administrative Hearings upholding the suspension of his driver's license for failure to comply with a child support order. Respondent, the Department of Social and Health Services, was also involved in the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The father was required to pay monthly child support. Following his accumulation of past-due child support debt of over $ 50,000, the Department of Social and Health Services Division of Child Support notified the father of his noncompliance and the resulting suspension of his driver's license under Wash. Rev. Code § 74.20A. An administrative law judge heard his challenge to the suspension and entered an order concluding that the father failed to comply with the child support order and upholding the license suspension. Recognizing that the father did not dispute that the license was properly suspended under state law, the trial court affirmed, holding that the father's constitutional claims were barred under collateral estoppel and res judicata. The trial court noted the father's claims would also fail on the merits. The father appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that each of his constitutional claims had been addressed on the merits by other courts and there was no authority that the court had to review the trial court and appellate records before applying res judicata or collateral estoppel. In addition, the court noted that § 74.20A provided procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1809 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pederson


No. 21863-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 433



March 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Pederson, 126 Wn. App. 1028, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1241 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: KLICKITAT. Docket No(s): 01-1-00139-8. Judge signing: E. THOMPSON REYNOLDS. Date filed: March 3, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Klickitat County (Washington), convicted defendant of four counts of first degree child rape and two counts of first degree child molestation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that defendant's trial only lasted about three days; the issues and his defense of general denial on all the counts were straightforward; and the trial court instructed the jury to decide each count separately. Therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's severance motions. The first child victim met all the factors for competency because she was able to (1) accurately testify as to her age, her living arrangements, and the city where she lived; (2) respond appropriately to a truth/lie example; and (3) understand her obligation to tell the truth; thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by finding her competent to testify. In addition, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of first degree child molestation of the second victim because she testified she was lying on the couch with her eyes closed when defendant put his hand under her shirt and touched her chest for a few seconds. Also, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for first degree child rape because the third victim testified at trial that she was six years old when he put his hands down her pants and felt around inside.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1810 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Monroe


No. 30239-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


126 Wn. App. 435; 109 P.3d 449; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 451



March 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at State v. Monroe, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 727 (Wash., Sept. 7, 2005)
Review granted by, Remanded by State v. Monroe, 157 Wn.2d 1016, 142 P.3d 172, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 625 (Wash., Sept. 6, 2006)
Appeal after remand at State v. Monroe, 135 Wn. App. 880, 146 P.3d 931, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2419 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 7, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) convicted defendant, upon his guilty pleas, of two counts of first degree rape, one count of first degree burglary with sexual motivation, five counts of first degree kidnapping, and one count of second degree assault. Based on the aggravating factors, the trial court sentenced him to serve a maximum term of life with a determinate minimum term of 651 months. Defendant appealed from his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that defendant waived his right to have a jury determine his guilt by knowingly and voluntarily pleading guilty to the crimes with which he had been charged. Defendant's convictions were based on his unchallenged and constitutionally valid plea and he was sentenced to life as Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712(3) specifically required. However, defendant was not otherwise eligible to receive a minimum sentence in excess of the standard range until a jury found the disputed aggravating facts on which the trial court relied beyond a reasonable doubt, specifically, deliberate cruelty, victim vulnerability, and criminal sophistication. Therefore, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712(3) did not give the trial court the authority to impose a minimum term in excess of the 384 to 511 month standard range without satisfying Blakely's jury trial requirement. Because the jury did not find those aggravating factors beyond a reasonable doubt and because defendant did not admit to those factors, under Blakely, the trial court's exceptional sentence imposing a minimum term sentence of 651 months on defendant had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's plea-based convictions, but remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1811 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kirk


No. 54030-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 438



March 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Kirk, 126 Wn. App. 1025, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1133 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Date filed: 11/21/2003. Docket No:03-1-02592-1. Judge signing: Hon. Richard F McDermott.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had been convicted in the Superior Court of King County, Washington, for third-degree domestic violence assault and the trial court entered a no-contact order pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.99.050. Thereafter, he was convicted for domestic violence fourth-degree assault and felony violation of the no-contact order and the trial court imposed another no-contact order. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the original no-contact order was based on a facially unconstitutional statute and that the second no-contact order based on a violation of that order was void. Specifically, he contended that the statute unconstitutionally allowed prohibition of direct and indirect contact between him and the victim, effectively cutting off his ability to have contact with his children. The appellate court noted that a statute was facially unconstitutional only if there was no set of circumstances in which it could be constitutionally applied. The appellate court found that the no-contact order did not restrict contact between defendant and his children, and that defendant did not maintain that there was no set of circumstances in which the statute could be constitutionally applied. The appellate court held that the prohibition of all other contact was reasonably related to the goal of preventing further harm to the victim and the original order on which the no-contact order was based was issued pursuant to a valid statute and was not void; therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing the no-contact order.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1812 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Pierce County v. Wash. Shellfish, Inc.


No. 31380-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 391



March 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Pierce County v. Wash. Shellfish, Inc., 126 Wn. App. 1020, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1114 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No:02-2-08561-5. Judge signing: Hon. Vicki Hogan.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, granting partial summary judgment in favor of respondent, Pierce County, Washington, concerning a lease agreement of tidelands.


OVERVIEW: The company contacted the Pierce County Department of Parks and Recreation concerning an interest in leasing tidelands the County owned. The company engaged in aquaculture and wanted to lease approximately 47 acres of submerged tidelands. The tidelands at issue were considered a public resource because they were one of a few places where the public could go to recreate and take shellfish for personal consumption. Eight months after the company began its operations on the leased property, the County began to question the validity of the lease and filed a complaint for declaratory relief declaring the lease null and void. The appellate court ruled that the lease was not ultra vires and the County could enter into such a contract for the first five-year period. However, the renewal clause that would have extended the contract for 30 years was prohibited by county ordinances requiring county council approval. Instead of invalidating the entire contract, the trial court should have severed the ultra vires portion. By exempting itself from Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.34, the County also exempted itself from Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.68, dealing with the management of county owned park lands.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part, striking the renewal clause, and the case was remanded for trial as to whether the lease for the five-year term was a gift of public funds.

 

1813 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Authier


No. 31436-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 392



March 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Authier, 126 Wn. App. 1021, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1116 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No:02-1-00164-4. Date filed: 02/06/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth Day Williams.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of Clallam County, Washington, revoking his Special Sexual Offender Sentencing Alternative (SSOSA).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of first degree child rape. Defendant was sentenced to 132 months, but the sentence was suspended and a SSOSA was imposed in accord with the plea agreement. Defendant was later convicted of second degree burglary and theft. Defendant's SSOSA was revoked, and confinement was imposed for the remainder of his 132-month sentence. Defendant argued that his guilty plea was invalid and should be withdrawn because the plea form and the trial court erroneously identified the standard sentencing range for his convictions. The State responded that defendant's challenge to his guilty plea was an untimely collateral attack that was procedurally barred under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1). Defendant's appeal was filed more than one year after the judgment and sentence became final, and challenged his plea's validity only after his SSOSA was revoked. The appellate court ruled that defendant's collateral attack was procedurally barred under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1) and not subject to any exception under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100. Defendant's judgment and sentence were facially valid, and accurately identified defendant's standard sentencing range.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1814 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. 53913-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 370



March 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Johnson, 126 Wn. App. 1015, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1093 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-02613-8. Date filed: 02/23/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Michael J Heavey.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the King County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted him of felony violation of a domestic violence no-contact order. The State cross-appealed the determination of defendant's offender score.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued for the first time on appeal that the order prohibiting his contact with the child's mother had a consequence of precluding contact with his child, thus impermissibly interfering with his fundamental right to parent. Defendant claimed the statute authorizing the order, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.99.050, was unconstitutional on its face and that the resulting order was invalid. The instant court concluded that the order did not prohibit defendant from having contact with his child; it only prohibited contact with the child's mother. Therefore, defendant could not show that the statute would interfere with his right to parent, at least as constitutionally recognized. While the order may have been an inconvenience, any interference was not substantial or beyond that which was justified by the need to protect the mother. There was no violation of defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial on whether the crime was a domestic violence offense. With respect to the State's cross-appeal, the sentencing court erred in determining that defendant's juvenile conviction for second degree assault "washed-out," thereby reducing his offender score from four to three.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. However, on the State's cross-appeal of the determination of defendant's offender score, the instant court reversed and remanded for resentencing.

 

1815 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fualaau


No. 52043-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 377



March 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Fualaau, 126 Wn. App. 1011, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1089 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-1-01336-4. Judge signing: Hon. Catherine D Shaffer. Date filed: 02/21/2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a firearm and imposed an exceptional sentence upward of 60 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the exceptional sentencing statute was facially unconstitutional, that his waiver of a jury trial was not knowing and voluntary, that the trial court erred by considering acts unrelated to the charged offense in setting the sentence, and that the State violated its plea agreement by changing its sentencing recommendation. The appellate court noted that any argument concerning provisions relating to exceptional sentences as facially unconstitutional had been rejected. The plea agreement entered by defendant did not restrict consideration of the stipulated facts only for purposes of a standard range sentence. The trial court did not err by imposing an exceptional sentence upward based on the severity of the victim's injuries. The language of the plea agreement pointed to four triggers for withdrawal of the sentencing recommendation. The second trigger advised the defendant that criminal conduct resulting in arrest would jeopardize the sentencing recommendation, even if charges were not filed or a conviction had not been entered. Defendant's alleged criminal conduct was sufficient to relieve the State of the obligation to recommend the agreed sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Webster

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Hon. Richard F McDermott.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant, pursuant to guilty pleas, of residential burglary, attempted residential burglary, first degree theft, and five counts of forgery. The trial court imposed exceptional sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the exceptional sentences imposed on two of the counts were invalid because the authorizing statutes were facially unconstitutional, and because the grounds for the sentences were not submitted to a jury. The appellate court noted that those arguments were defeated by its previous decisions in other cases. Defendant's argument that Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 and the portion of the sentences requiring him to provide a biological sample for DNA identification violated his Fourth Amendment right against unreasonable searches was rejected in, and was controlled by, the appellate court's prior decisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Christophe


NO. 53318-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 384



March 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Christophe, 126 Wn. App. 1013, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1064 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-00616-1. Judge signing: Hon. Harry J McCarthy. Judgment or order under review Date filed: 10/06/2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicting him of theft of rental property over $ 1,500.


OVERVIEW: Defendant rented a car and prepaid for a week. Although he paid for some additional rental time after that, he kept the car longer than he had paid for and did not return it by the agreed-upon time. He was tried for theft of rental property over $ 1,500. The "to convict" instruction given to the jury was not an accurate statement of the elements of the crime of theft of rental or leased property. On its face, it did not require that the jury find the conduct element of the crime: "wrongfully obtains, or exerts unauthorized control over, or by color or aid of deception gains control of." Although the instruction was technically incorrect, it did not relieve the State of its burden to prove each element beyond a reasonable doubt. Therefore, any error in the jury instructions was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1818 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Dell


No. 53329-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 395



March 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. O'Dell, 126 Wn. App. 1014, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1068 (2005)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at O'Dell v. Karlsson, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50146 (W.D. Wash., Apr. 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-1-02648-2. Date filed: 10/31/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Harry J McCarthy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County (Washington) convicted and sentenced defendant for his convictions for third degree child molestation, attempted third degree child molestation, and 15 counts of communication with a minor for immoral purposes. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because the victim testified to multiple incidents but the trial court ruled that only one incident merited submission to the jury for child molestation, defendant argued that the jury could have convicted him based on one of the incidents dismissed by the trial court. During closing argument, the State elected the acts on which it relied, leaving no doubt that the jury's unanimous verdict was based on incidents supported by the evidence. Also, although the jury asked a question that seemingly signaled confusion as to which incidents the State elected, the appellate court could not assume that the confusion was not cleared up during the remainder of the jury's deliberations. Thus, his molestation conviction was not reversed. The appellate court found that sexual gratification was not an essential element of third degree child molestation. Thus, the trial court did not omit any essential element from the "to convict" jury instructions. Also, given the quantity and subject matter of the victim's testimony conceding her difficulties with defendant, even if the trial court erred in not permitting defendant to further cross-examine her on that subject, it was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1819 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flowers-Roscoe


No. 30779-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 348



March 1, 2005, File


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Flowers-Roscoe, 126 Wn. App. 1008, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1077 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 03-1-01842-4. Date filed: 08/21/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Frederick Fleming.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant was convicted of unlawful manufacturing of methamphetamine in the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington. Defendant appealed, asserting that the evidence used in support of his conviction was illegally obtained in a pretextual traffic stop. In that respect, the arresting officer stopped his vehicle for a cracked windshield.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court cited numerous statutes which provided that operating a vehicle with faulty equipment was a traffic infraction. Further, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.021(2) provided, in part, that whenever any person was stopped for a traffic infraction, the officer could detain that person for a reasonable period of time necessary to identify the person, check for outstanding warrants, and check the status of the person's license. The appellate court found that the findings of fact and underlying testimony established that the officer saw a cracked windshield, believed that it posed a safety hazard and, thus, had an objective basis for stopping defendant to investigate. Once he learned that defendant was driving with a suspended license, he had probable cause for a custodial arrest and grounds to search incident to a valid arrest. Further, the officer testified that over the years he had stopped dozens of cars with cracked windshields, and would normally give either a warning or a citation. Thus, under those circumstances, the appellate court held the stop was not an unlawful pretextual stop with the intention of circumventing the warrant requirement.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1820 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Funk v. City of Duvall


No. 53967-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


126 Wn. App. 920; 109 P.3d 844; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 359



February 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Respondent's Motion to Publish April 4, 2005.
Reported at Funk v. City of Duvall, 126 Wn. App. 1007, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1071 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent city on appellant residents' claim that their payment of assessments to help finance construction of the city's sewage treatment plant and sewer system gave them a contractual right to be first in priority for the allocation of the limited capacity and that the city's allocation decisions impaired this right. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The residents argued that the trial court erred in granting the city's motion for summary judgment. They claimed that their payment of assessments guaranteed them the right to a sewer hookup when they developed their properties in the future. The appellate court determined that assuming that a contractual right to a sewer connection was the special benefit the residents obtained when they paid their assessments for the original Utility Local Improvement District (ULID), there was no basis for their claim that the city promised them priority in the event of a shortage. The city's ordinances did not require the residents to perform any additional act as a new condition to receiving sewer service. They were not being denied a right to a connection until they satisfied a new condition. The ordinance creating the original ULID did not promise to reserve capacity for the ULID properties. The ordinance did not anticipate shortages and did not provide a method for dealing with them. The residents did not demonstrate that the special benefit conferred by their payment of assessments included an ongoing right to priority over the non-ULID property owners who received the 850 units.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1822 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Brundage


No. 30390-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


126 Wn. App. 55; 107 P.3d 742; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 314



February 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at, Injunction denied by, Motion denied by State v. Brundage, 157 Wn.2d 1017, 142 P.3d 607, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 729 (Wash., Sept. 7, 2005)
Review denied by State v. Brundage, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 641 (Wash., Sept. 6, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) that convicted him of multiple crimes involving first-degree rape, kidnapping, and unlawful possession of a firearm stemming from an attack on his wife, and that imposed an exceptional sentence based on defendant's extensive criminal history and the existence of his current convictions as authorized by Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the exceptional sentences violated his Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial because they were imposed based on facts not submitted to the jury and must be vacated under the Apprendi/Blakely rule. The court noted that the trial court identified three aggravating factors: deliberate cruelty; domestic violence; and that the standard range sentence was clearly too lenient under the multiple offense policy. The court held that the question of whether defendant manifested deliberate cruelty and engaged in domestic violence were questions of fact, which required a jury determination, and thus were not valid under the Blakely rule. However the court found that the trial court's imposition of an exceptional sentence was justified under the "free crimes" doctrine because, without the additional time, defendant's second-degree rape conviction would have gone unpunished, which was an unjust result and clearly too lenient as provided in Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1823 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guzman-Balbuena


No. 30763-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 326



February 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Guzman-Balbuena, 126 Wn. App. 1002, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1045 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Mason County. Docket No: 03-1-00188-1. Date filed: 08/21/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Toni A Sheldon.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated and case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. He also received an exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed after he was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver arguing that the prosecutor committed misconduct in closing argument. The court disagreed and affirmed the conviction, stating that the prosecutor's remarks that defendant had been employed as a brush picker for only $400 a week were not flagrant or ill-intentioned. Defendant argued that the reference was made for the jury to determine that he was guilty by inferring that someone in his financial state would only purchase a lot of cocaine if he was acting as an agent for an unnamed financier and that his intent was to improve his financial condition. The court stated that the trial court instructed the jury that the prosecutor's argument was not evidence and that they were to rely only on the evidence produced at trial during their deliberations. Considering the other evidence suggesting that defendant was acting with or for others in the transaction and that he intended to deliver the cocaine either to the others participating in the deal or the public, the court could not say that the misstatement and the prosecutor's brief focus on defendant's economic status influenced the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the exceptional sentence and remanded for resentencing.

 

1824 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rice


No. 31025-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 330



February 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] As amended by the Court of Appeals January 18, 2006.  RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 02-1-01755-0. Date filed: 09/26/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Barbara D Johnson.
State v. Rice, 126 Wn. App. 1002, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1044 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to first degree theft in the Superior Court of Clark County, Washington. His crime regarded the embezzlement of money form his stepmother, for whom he had been appointed guardian of her person and estate. The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence, based on two aggravating factors. Defendant appealed as to his sentence because said aggravating factors were not submitted to a jury.


OVERVIEW: The uncontroverted evidence established that defendant took more than $ 200,000 from his stepmother's estate. That was 133 times greater than the minimum threshold for first degree theft. Thus, the trial court made the very common sense determination that an exceptional sentence was supported by the fact that defendant's crime was facilitated by a breach of fiduciary duty and was a "major economic offense." However, those facts did not suffice for the appellate court. It concluded that per the United States Supreme Court's holding in Blakely v. Washington, such findings could not support an exceptional sentence because they were not made by a jury or admitted by defendant. The appellate court also concluded that Blakely errors were not subject to a harmless error analysis. Thus, even though defendant did admit to loaning himself money from his stepmother while he was her guardian and using it for his own personal gain, because he did not actually admit to the precise amount, and because he did not technically admit that his action constituted a breach of fiduciary duty, the appellate court held he was entitled to resentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for resentencing within the standard range.

State v. Bruner


No. 31115-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 328



February 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

As Amended by Order of the Court of Appeals   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 00-1-01280-2. Date filed: 11/13/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Roger A Bennett.
State v. Bruner, 126 Wn. App. 1003, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1048 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Exceptional sentence vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which sentenced him on remand after he was convicted of second-degree rape of a child and second-degree molestation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his sentence on remand, arguing that (1) the court on remand was prohibited from considering a prior Oregon sex offense when determining his offender score; (2) the court on remand failed to properly classify the prior Oregon offense; and (3) his exceptional sentence was improper under Blakely. The court held that on remand, the trial court properly considered his prior Oregon sex offense. The trial court also rightfully relied on the initial classification of that offense and offender score calculation because the issues were not addressed in his prior appeal. But the court vacated the exceptional sentence and remanded for resentencing in accordance with Blakely. A complete reading of the court's opinion showed that it did not hold that the Oregon offense was no longer part of defendant's offender score. The trial court made the findings supporting the enhancement and defendant did not admit the facts supporting the exceptional sentence. Thus, the case clearly fell under Blakely.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the exceptional sentence and remanded for resentencing.

1827 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Ventenbergs v. City of Seattle


No. 53920-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 290



February 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-2-25260-3. Date filed: 02/23/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Douglas D McBroom.
Ventenbergs v. City of Seattle, 125 Wn. App. 1043, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 909 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The instant appeal challenged defendant city's approach to regulating commercial solid waste collection which required a city contract. Plaintiffs, two companies, sued defendant, and also defendant waste management company, alleging constitutional and statutory violations. The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. The companies sought review, alleging constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: The companies argued that the city's ordinances violated the privileges and immunities clause of the Washington Constitution because they made it illegal for anyone other than the waste management company it contracted to be in the business of hauling construction, demolition and land clearing waste (CDL). However, the appellate court noted that Washington courts had repeatedly held that the regulation of solid waste was a valid exercise of local police power. The city had articulated important public health objectives to maintain the environmental standards established in its long-haul disposal contract with the waste management company. Thus, there was no constitutional violation. Secondly, Wash. Rev. Code § 81.77.020 did not state, as the companies argued, that once a city contracted with one vender, other venders who wished to collect solid waste no longer needed a state certificate. Because the companies (a construction company and a waste hauling company), did not have a certificate, they did not have a valid contract between themselves for hauling such waste. Finally, the companies did not show that they were wrongfully excluded from bidding on a city contract per state law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Cook


No. 30705-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


125 Wn. App. 709; 106 P.3d 251; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 222



February 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by State v. Cook, 155 Wn.2d 1013, 122 P.3d 912, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 843 (Wash., Oct. 6, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought discretionary review of an order from the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss a second degree assault charge that arose from allegations of domestic violence.


OVERVIEW: The charge was filed more than three years after the alleged domestic violence occurred. Defendant, who was a police officer, argued that the statute of limitations had run. The State responded that under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.04.080(1)(b)(i), a ten-year statute of limitations applied when a public officer committed a felony in breach of duty or in violation of the oath of office. The trial court, in denying defendant's motion to dismiss, ruled that the statute of limitations was ten years because the alleged assault would be a violation of defendant's oath of office, which prohibited violation of any law. The court held that the extended statute of limitations for felonies for public officers was applicable to police officers even when they were off duty. Defendant was a public officer, as defined in Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.04.110(13), when he allegedly assaulted his wife, and he was thus subject to the extended statute of limitations regardless of whether he was acting in his official capacity. The court declined to consider a constitutional challenge to defendant's oath of office on religious freedom grounds, holding that defendant lacked standing to raise this argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss.

 

1829 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Heaton


No. 30123-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 236



February 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 02-1-00495-6. Date filed: 02/21/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Kathryn J Nelson.
State v. Heaton, 125 Wn. App. 1035, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 876 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicted defendant, a police officer, of official-misconduct under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.80.010, based on the allegation that he took money from a citizen during a traffic stop without legal justification. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the terms "unauthorized acts" and "duty imposed by law" in § 9A.80.010 failed to give notice and did not prevent arbitrary enforcement. The court disagreed because people of common intelligence could understand the meaning of the statute. The statute also was not vague within the context of the case because people of common intelligence could understand that taking money from a citizen during a traffic stop was conducting an "unauthorized act" and that an officer conducting a search had "duty imposed by law" to return any money to the owner of the wallet. The statute did not invite arbitrary enforcement. The court agreed with defendant, however, that the trial court committed reversible error by omitting the element of intention to commit an unauthorized act from the "to convict" instruction. The error was not harmless, even though the jury found that defendant intentionally obtained a benefit under color of law, because there was an argument that defendant found the citizen's money, rather than taking it. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant, in an official capacity, took the money from the wallet and kept it "under color of law."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Wallin


No. 52920-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


125 Wn. App. 648; 105 P.3d 1037; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 219



February 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by State v. Wallin, 155 Wn.2d 1012, 122 P.3d 186, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 831 (2005)
Related proceeding at State v. Wallin, 2009 Wash. App. LEXIS 1230 (Wash. Ct. App., May 18, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree rape of a child, first-degree child molestation, sexual exploitation of a minor, and possession of depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct.


OVERVIEW: A neighbor telephoned the police to complain that defendant had been taking pictures of her teenage nieces from his apartment window. The police reported the incident to defendant's CCO, who felt, that, given his history, the incident was a strong indication that defendant was violating the terms of his community placement. As a result, several CCOs visited defendant and searched his home and computer; they did not have a warrant. Based on what they found, they contacted the police and arrested defendant. Relying on information obtained from the CCOs, police officers obtained a warrant to search defendant's home, computer, and media storage devices. Code § 9.94A.120(10)(c) (1998). When his term expired in April 1999, he was no longer a probationer with a lessened expectation of privacy. The 1999 order was invalid and the initial search made pursuant to the order but without a warrant violated Wash. Const. art. I, § 7.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

In re Pers. Restraint of Johnston


No. 20549-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 209



February 3, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Pers. Restraint of Johnston, 125 Wn. App. 1032, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 866 (2005)
Reconsideration denied by In re Pers. Restraint of Johnston, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 473 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 97-1-01950-9. Judge signing: LINDA G. TOMPKINS. Date filed: October 20, 2000. Proceedings Originating in Court of Appeals: 10/9/01. Nature of Proceedings: PERSONAL RESTRAINT PETITION.
State v. Johnston, 100 Wn. App. 126, 996 P.2d 629, 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 534 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant of various crimes. Defendant sought relief from personal restraint imposed for his jury convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his second degree felony murder conviction had to be vacated in light of a supreme court holding that assault could not serve as the predicate crime for second degree felony murder under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.050(1)(b) (1976). The appellate court agreed, finding that the 2003 legislative amendment that included assault as a predicate crime for second degree felony murder was not retroactive because retroactive application would violate the ex post facto clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction as an accomplice to first degree robbery and for attempted second degree intentional murder where the jury was entitled to disbelieve defendant's testimony that he was unaware of the knife until he saw his accomplice throw it into the river ten minutes after the robbery, and that he thought the accomplice was merely punching the clerk in the back. The trial court gave the exact accomplice instruction proposed by defendant. Defendant's ineffective assistance claims all amounted to conclusory or unsupported allegations insufficient to command further review.


OUTCOME: Defendant's personal restraint petition was granted to the extent that his second degree felony murder conviction and sentence for that crime was vacated and the matter remanded to the superior court; defendant's personal restraint petition was otherwise denied.

 

1832 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Gausvik v. Abbey


No. 31054-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


126 Wn. App. 868; 107 P.3d 98; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 152



January 25, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Respondents' Motion to Publish February 23, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 01-2-00958-1. Date filed: 10/27/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Richard a Strophy.
Gausvik v. Abbey, 125 Wn. App. 1022, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 719 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accused father appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Thurston County (Washington) that denied his motion for reconsideration of the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants, Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS) and three social workers, on their statute of limitations and qualified immunity defenses in the father's action alleging violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and negligent investigation in a child abuse case.


OVERVIEW: The father claimed the trial court erred in finding that his claims were barred by the statute of limitations; that Wash. Rev. Code § 4.16.190 was constitutional; and that he was collaterally estopped from relitigating those issues because of his prior federal action against law enforcement officials. The father was convicted of child abuse in 1995, but the State dismissed the charges in 2000. The father claimed the statute of limitations began to run when his conviction was invalidated in 2000. The court noted that under § 4.16.190, the statute of limitations began to run when the factual basis for the action became known to the father, and that he admitted that he knew at the time of his sentencing in 1995 that the investigation techniques used could have led the children to allege abuse that never occurred. The court also noted that § 4.16.190 only tolled the statute of limitations during his incarceration before sentencing and that the federal court had already decided the constitutionality issue. The court held that the father's claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 failed because the DSHS workers did not make the decision to arrest and prosecute him and they had qualified immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1833 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Tapps Brewing Co., Inc. v. McClung


No. 31959-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 158



January 25, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County.
Tapps Brewing Co. v. McClung, 125 Wn. App. 1024, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 805 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent city and dismissed the developers' lawsuit challenging the city's imposition of a storm water general facilities charge (GFC) and an obligation to upgrade a storm water pipe in order to gain approval of commercial development plans for their property.


OVERVIEW: After a finding against them, the developers appealed. The court stated that given liberal notice pleading requirements, the developers' complaint had provided the city adequate notice of its challenge to the upgrade obligation's legality. Thus, the trial court erred in refusing to consider the claims. Further, given the substance of the summary judgment motion and hearing, and that all of the developers' claims were based on the same circumstances and very similar facts and evidence, the developers provided the city adequate notice of the constitutional claims. The trial court also abused its discretion in denying the developers' motion to amend the complaint to clarify the challenges to the constitutionality of the city's storm water pipe upgrade obligation. The trial court failed to evaluate whether the developers' amendments prejudiced the city. There was no evidence of prejudice to the city from the amendments when proposed by the developers and the amendment was not so untimely as to dictate denial on that basis alone. The law of the case doctrine precluded review of the developers' challenge to the GFC's legality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for trial only on the developers' challenge to the upgrade obligation's legality and to allow the developers to amend the complaint to clarify the constitutional claims. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1834 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lysikov


No. 53727-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 136



January 24, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Lysikov, 125 Wn. App. 1020, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 732 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 03-1-00903-7. Date filed: 01/12/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Linda C Krese.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with attempting to elude a pursuing police vehicle in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.024. Defendant unsuccessfully moved to suppress all evidence obtained following his detention by a police officer; namely, his admission. The Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, convicted defendant, sentenced him to 75 days confinement, and required him to submit a biological sample for DNA testing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to justify the warrantless seizure. The evidence established that another officer attempted to stop a vehicle because it had no rear license plate, but the vehicle drove off at a high rate of speed instead of stopping. The vehicle contained four individuals and was speeding north. The court found that these facts established reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. The officer was also informed that a vehicle was sighted. The officer made contact with the four individuals, who admitted they were associated with the vehicle. The officer had reasonable suspicion that defendant and his companions were involved in criminal activity. It was not error to deny defendant's motion to suppress. The late entry of Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.6 findings did not require reversal because the belated findings and conclusions were consistent with the oral ruling and there was no showing that defendant suffered any other prejudice. Finally, the argument that Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 authorized a warrantless search without probable cause, in violation of the Fourth Amendment and the Washington Constitution, was rejected.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

1835 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garcia


No. 22197-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 131



January 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 91-1-00060-7. Judge signing: CAROLYN A. BROWN. Date filed: April 18, 2003.
State v. Garcia, 125 Wn. App. 1017, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 741 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1991, defendant was convicted of first degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to 250 months of incarceration. Three months later, defendant's sentence was modified to add two years of community placement. The judgment and sentence were affirmed. Over eight years later, defendant filed pro se a Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b) motion for relief from judgment. The Superior Court Benton County, Washington, denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Over eight years passed between when the mandate was filed in defendant's first appeal and when he filed the Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b) motion. Consequently, the instant court found that his motion was untimely unless it qualified as an exception under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100. Defendant's motion was not "based solely" on the grounds specified in § 10.73.100. A "mixed" motion was subject to the one-year limit of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090. Consequently, the motion was properly dismissed. Defendant knew of the mandatory two-year community placement in his modified judgment and sentence before he argued his first appeal, decided in 1994. That first appeal also settled the issue of insufficiency of the evidence. The remaining issues raised in the motion involved a purported amended information charging defendant with second degree murder. However, the amended information was never filed and defendant was never charged with second degree murder. Equitable tolling of the time limit was not justified because defendant did not show material mistakes, prejudice, or that he did not know all the necessary facts within one year after his amended judgment became final.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1836 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reynolds


No. 30806-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 120



January 19, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Docket No: 03-1-00297-9. Date filed: 08/11/2003. Judge signing: Hon. David E Foscue.
State v. Reynolds, 125 Wn. App. 1015, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 815 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington), which convicted him of attempting to elude a pursuing police vehicle, second-degree assault with a deadly weapon in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021(1)(c), and two counts of first-degree malicious mischief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions, which stemmed from his fleeing from pursuing police vehicles. On appeal, the court affirmed, stating that under the apprehension of harm definition of assault, his intent to inflict the apprehended harm was clearly irrelevant. In defendant's statement to he police, he admitted that he intentionally struck one of the victim's car in an attempt to push through the stopped vehicles and elude the pursuing officers. The trial court could have reasonably concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's act of driving into the stopped vehicles was intended, at least in part, to scare the drivers of those vehicles into moving in order to avoid being harmed. Further, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021(1)(c) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied in his case because the court could not otherwise conclude that the statute failed to provide adequate notice and standards to prevent arbitrary enforcement. However, prior convictions could not alone support an exceptional sentence. Because they were the only basis for defendant's exceptional consecutive sentence, resentencing was required.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction, but vacated the exceptional sentence and remanded for resentencing within the standard range.

World Wide Video v. Spokane


No. 22092-3-III (consolidated with No. 22093-1-III)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


125 Wn. App. 289; 103 P.3d 1265; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 51



January 11, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Worldwide Video of Wash., Inc. v. City of Spokane, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 303 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 15, 2005)
Review denied by World Wide Video of Wash. v. City of Spokane, 155 Wn.2d 1014, 122 P.3d 186, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 829 (Wash., Oct. 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
World Wide Video of Wash., Inc. v. City of Spokane, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 18927 (9th Cir. Wash., July 12, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a video company and a property manager, challenged a decision of the Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington), which affirmed decisions of the city hearing examiner who upheld extensions for relocation of an adult video store upon enactment of former Spokane, Wash. Mun. Code § 11.19.143(D), which provided an amortization period of one year for nonconforming adult stores to relocate or change the nature of their businesses.


OVERVIEW: The video company operated adult stores in buildings leased from the property manager. The issues were whether regulating the location of adult stores violated constitutional rights and whether the administrative hearings followed proper procedures. The court affirmed and held that Wash. Const. art. I, § 5 did not justify extending greater state constitutional protection to adult stores. Nothing in Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.080 prevented the city from raising a collateral estoppel defense regarding the ordinances' constitutionality in its response brief to the land use petition. The state constitutional issue was resolved in the video company's federal action; thus, the manager was estopped from raising that issue. The manager was also collaterally estopped from arguing additional prior restraint, and the ordinance did not qualify as a bill of attainder. As the parties entered into the leases subject to further regulation by ordinance, former Spokane, Wash. Mun. Code § 11.19.143(D) did not unconstitutionally impair the leases. The record supported the hearing examiner's conclusion that extension of the amortization period was not necessary beyond what was granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the superior court.

City of Bremerton v. Tucker


No. 31206-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


126 Wn. App. 26; 103 P.3d 1285; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 79



January 11, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, imposing a mandatory, 24-month, statutory minimum sentence enhancement for driving-under-the-influence (DUI), based on a prior deferred DUI prosecution.


OVERVIEW: In 1996, defendant requested and received a deferred prosecution for DUI. In 1999, after finding that defendant had successfully completed the deferred prosecution conditions, the DUI charge was dismissed, entering a no conviction on his record. In 2002, defendant was charged with another DUI, and defendant pled guilty as charged. The trial court imposed the mandatory minimum sentence for a DUI offender with one "prior offense," based on defendant's previous deferred DUI prosecution. The appellate court ruled that defendant failed to show lack of notice or any due process violation when the trial court used his prior deferred DUI prosecution to enhance his sentence under former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(vii) (2002). Former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(vii) did not violate due process by increasing the penalty for a second DUI where defendant had previously admitted to having committed a prior DUI under a deferred prosecution. Defendant knew that if he drove again while under the influence, his penalty for the new DUI would be more severe than it would have been had the new DUI been his first offense.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

 

1839 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Luther


No. 52391-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


125 Wn. App. 176; 105 P.3d 56; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 30



January 10, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Luther, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 308 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 22, 2005)
Review granted by State v. Luther, 155 Wn.2d 1014, 124 P.3d 304, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 885 (2005)
Affirmed by, En banc State v. Luther, 157 Wn.2d 63, 134 P.3d 205, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 428 (Wash., May 18, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court in King County (Washington), which convicted him of the attempted possession of child pornography.


OVERVIEW: Police received a tip that defendant was receiving child pornography over the internet. After he was convicted, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the State was unable to show the age of the persons involved. However, the not guilty verdict on some of the charges did not bar his conviction for the attempted possession of constitutionally unprotected materials under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.010(1). The court noted that impossibility was not a defense to attempt; therefore, it was irrelevant that the pictures possessed by defendant did not depict actual minors. Next, the court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.070 was not constitutionally overbroad. The crime was not expanded to images that appeared to depict minors because minor was defined under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.011(4) as someone under the age of 18. Further, the State was required to make a showing that defendant was aware of the nature and content of the materials possessed. Finally, the court determined that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction because the record showed that defendant intended to obtain the materials and took a substantial step towards obtaining them.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

1840 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Manro


No. 52013-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


125 Wn. App. 165; 104 P.3d 708; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 31



January 10, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant juvenile of fourth degree assault on two counts and sentenced him to eight months confinement. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by not granting his motion to extend juvenile jurisdiction under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.300, in anticipation that he might be acquitted of the first degree assault charge. The appellate court noted that defendant's arguments concerning § 13.40.300 were based on his assumption that jurisdiction was defeated under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.030 when the jury acquitted him of first degree assault. The statutory criteria for original jurisdiction under § 13.04.030(1)(e)(v) were met. The State did not amend the charges against defendant. He was found not guilty of assault in the first degree. Use of the word "alleged" indicated that the legislature intended the charge, not the final outcome, to dictate the proper jurisdiction. The silence regarding alternative procedures upon acquittal of all automatic-transfer charges also indicated that the outcome of the prosecution had no affect on jurisdiction. Jurisdiction attached when certain enumerated offenses were charged. Because defendant was properly tried in adult court under § 13.04.030(1)(e)(v), he was not entitled to a declination hearing under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.110.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
