Properties Four, Inc. v. State


No. 31006-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


125 Wn. App. 108; 105 P.3d 416; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 10



January 4, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] As amended by order of the Court of Appeals February 8, 2005.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Properties Four, Inc. v. State, 155 Wn.2d 1003, 122 P.3d 185, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 753 (Wash., Sept. 7, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property company appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which granted summary judgment in favor defendant State in the company's action against the State for damages the company allegedly sustained when the State failed to complete a property purchase.


OVERVIEW: Representatives of the State's General Administration (GA) and the company entered into an option to purchase agreement that was conditioned on the approval of any government agency. While the State representatives assured the company representatives that there would be no problem obtaining the legislative appropriation, it was never approved. The court held that, because the GA never had legislative authority to bind the State to the purchase, the legislature did not render an agreement void; the agreements were unenforceable without necessary agency approval. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 43.88.110(6), because the option to purchase set a price in excess of $ 9,000,000, the Office of Financial Management was obligated to review and approve the purchase. Because the GA never obtained the necessary approvals, which were set out in the option agreement, the documents did not bind the State. Further, the company's arguments that the State should be bound, even though the GA never obtained legislative funding or required governmental agency approvals, ignored the ultra vires mandate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the State.

State v. Bunn


No. 21866-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3106



December 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

State v. Bunn, 124 Wn. App. 1054, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3703 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Benton County (Washington), which convicted him of two counts of first degree robbery, one count of first degree burglary, and one count of first degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was one of three men who invaded the victims' apartment looking for someone who was not there. Defendant and his companions beat the boyfriend of one victim until he was unconscious, sexually assaulted the victims, and took money and a victim's car. An informant met with defendant and obtained a confession. Evidence of the crime was found in defendant's car. Amunrud v. Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs.


No. 52910-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


124 Wn. App. 884; 103 P.3d 257; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3083



December 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by Amunrud v. Bd. of Appeals, 155 Wn.2d 1001, 122 P.3d 185, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 721 (2005)
Affirmed by Amunrud v. Bd. of Appeals, 158 Wn.2d 208, 143 P.3d 571, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 725 (Wash., Sept. 21, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, father, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, affirming the decision to revoke his driver's license for delinquency in child support payments, pursuant to the petition filed by respondent, Washington Department of Social and Health Services.


OVERVIEW: The father fell at least six months behind in his child support payments, owing $ 16,255. The prosecutor filed a petition for modification of child support on the father's behalf, requesting a reduction in his monthly obligation. The request was rejected and the father's obligation was increased. Soon after, a license suspension action was initiated. The father argued that revocation of his driver's license was a violation of his Fourteenth Amendment substantive right to a livelihood. The appellate court ruled that the father failed to prove that any of his rights were violated. The sanction and the underlying conduct need not be directly related, but instead must only be rationally related. The State had satisfied this burden by providing evidence that license suspension, or the threat of license suspension, had proven an effective support enforcement tool. Because the threat of license suspension was an effective tool, it was rationally related to the problem of delinquent obligors. Also, since the father did not claim a personal infringement of his privacy, he did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 74.20A.360 and 26.23.120.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1844 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Clarke


No. 53003-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


124 Wn. App. 893; 103 P.3d 262; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3084



December 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

As corrected by 130 Wn. App. errata.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by State v. Clarke, 154 Wn.2d 1020, 116 P.3d 398, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 563 (2005)
Affirmed by, En banc State v. Clarke, 156 Wn.2d 880, 134 P.3d 188, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 425 (Wash., May 11, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, King County (Washington) convicted defendant of two counts of second degree rape and imposed indeterminate sentences under the nonpersistent offender statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the indeterminate sentences imposed under the nonpersistent offender statute violated the Sixth Amendment. The presumptive range for a minimum term was between 102 and 136 months pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.20.021(1)(a). Defendant argued the sentence imposed was not an indeterminate sentence but a determinate sentence under the Sentencing Reform Act (SRA) that was invalid under Blakely. Sentences under the nonpersistent offender statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712, were not determinate sentences, and the focus of Blakely was on the maximum sentence a judge could impose solely on the basis of the facts reflected in the jury verdict or admitted by the defendant. The jury verdict for the crime of second degree rape mandated a maximum term of life as part of the indeterminate sentence. Thus, Blakely was not implicated to the extent of the maximum term of the sentences the court imposed. The maximum term of the sentences was life. The minimum term imposed was 204 months. The verdicts authorized the maximum term, and the minimum term did not exceed that maximum. There is no violation of the Sixth Amendment under Blakely.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Custody of A.C.


No. 30016-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


124 Wn. App. 846; 103 P.3d 226; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3074



December 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by, Remanded by Cumming v. Cumming (In re Custody of A.C), 155 Wn.2d 1011, 120 P.3d 928, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 808 (2005)
On remand at, Remanded by Cumming v. Cumming, 130 Wn. App. 157, 123 P.3d 121, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2790 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, amended a parenting plan to give limited visitation rights to respondent grandmother. Appellant father sought review.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court unconstitutionally interfered with his right to parent his children. The court disagreed, explaining that until the time of trial, the grandmother, at the father's request, had custody of and parented the children for four years, over half of each child's life. Thus, she had essentially become a de facto or psychological parent. The court rejected the assertion that, as a matter of law, a nonparent could not bring a third party visitation action. United States Supreme Court precedent, although limiting court interference with parental decisions, did not preclude court-ordered visitation where the nonparent seeking visitation brought a petition during the pendency of marriage dissolution proceedings between the children's parents, the nonparent had had legal custody of the children for a significant portion of their lives, and the parent objecting to visitation had failed to show a likelihood that such visitation would be detrimental to the children. The court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.240 did not have the problems that had been discussed by the United States Supreme Court with regard to former Wash. Rev. Code § 26.10.160.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Bercier v. Kiga


No. 31052-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


127 Wn. App. 809; 103 P.3d 232; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3077



December 21, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals August 3, 2005.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Modified by Bercier v. Kiga, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1944 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 3, 2005)
Review denied by, Motion to strike granted by Bercier v. Kiga, 155 Wn.2d 1015, 124 P.3d 304, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 876 (Wash., Nov. 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff American Indian appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which dismissed his declaratory action claiming that he should be exempt from all Washington excise taxes and regulation contending that he was an Indian doing business on Indian trust land, entitled to exemptions under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 82.24.260, 82.24.900, and 82.26.040.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sold tobacco products at a smokeshop on a tribe reservation where he was not a tribal member. The trial court granted the State's Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 12(b)(6) motion to dismiss the majority of plaintiff's claims. The court held that the relevant law provided the tax exemption only for Indians who were members of the tribe on whose land they were operating. Wash. Admin. Code 458-20-192(5) included only those persons who were enrolled with the tribe upon whose territory the activity took place and did not include members of other tribes. The court also noted that the definition of "Indian" in 25 U.S.C.S. § 1301 pertained solely to criminal jurisdiction. Also, the existence of a consensual business relationship with the tribe did not give plaintiff the same benefits as a member of the tribe. As to plaintiff's claim that a compact existed, the claim involved no justiciable controversy because he is concerned only with a hypothetical compact between the State and the tribe. He did not show that such a compact currently existed or is under consideration such that it would adversely affect him. Therefore, plaintiff failed to present a justiciable controversy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Friend & Friend Enters. v. Thurston County


No. 31343-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3078



December 21, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Mason County. Docket No: 02-2-00993-3. Judgment or order under review Date filed: 01/12/2004. Judge signing: Hon. James B II Sawyer.
Friend & Friend Enters., Inc. v. Thurston County, 124 Wn. App. 1043, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3656 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington) affirming an administrative finding that his subdivision proposal was incomplete for noncompliance with Thurston County's Critical Areas Ordinance (CAO) and other environmental regulations.


OVERVIEW: The individual owned property. The county permitted the individual to operate a road across the property for logging purposes only. The individual then proposed a subdivision of the property. The county rejected the proposal contending that it was incomplete for noncompliance with the Critical Areas Ordinance (CAO) and other environmental regulations. The individual sought judicial review of the decision contending that the county misinterpreted the CAO, substantial evidence did not support the decision, the decision was clearly erroneous, and the CAO was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court affirmed the county's decision, and the individual appealed. The court noted that the county was vested with discretion to interpret the provisions of the CAO, and the interpretation it gave the particular provisions was supported by substantial evidence, was not clearly erroneous, and thus was proper. Furthermore, the CAO was not vague or unambiguous and did not tread upon an individual's constitutional rights. Therefore, since the individual failed to show entitlement to relief under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.130(1), the affirmation of the county's order was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

1849 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hosier


No. 51972-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


124 Wn. App. 696; 103 P.3d 217; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3047



December 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by State v. Hosier, 155 Wn.2d 1011, 122 P.3d 186, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 821 (2005)
Affirmed by, En banc State v. Hosier, 157 Wn.2d 1, 133 P.3d 936, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 424 (Wash., May 11, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court, Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of two counts of communication with a minor for immoral purposes (CMIP) under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090, one count of attempted CMIP, and two counts of harassment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant placed sexually explicit notes on a fence at a day care where it was likely that children would see them and at various places where it was likely that young women would find the notes. The court affirmed and held that the fact that defendant placed notes on his neighbor's lawn that described the neighbor's daughter, even though the daughter did not read the notes, was sufficient to fulfill the communication element of CMIP. As to the day care notes, the court stated that it would be absurd to require that a minor understand the prurient nature of the communication. Further, the attempted CMIP was supported by defendant's act of placing a pair of underwear in the day care parking lot because it was a substantial step toward the commission of the crime. The court also upheld the harassment conviction because it was not required that the speaker actually intended to carry out the threat. Finally, the court held that notwithstanding an expert's conclusion that defendant authored the notes, the court had probable cause to issue an affidavit to obtain samples of defendant's handwriting from his residence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Lanphar


No. 30518-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


124 Wn. App. 669; 102 P.3d 864; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2994



December 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which convicted defendant of bail jumping in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.170.


OVERVIEW: After posting bail, defendant failed to report to a supervised release officer and failed to appear in court as he had been ordered. Defendant argued that § 9A.76.170 violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 19, because 2001 Wash. Laws ch. 264, § 3, which amended the bail jumping statute by removing a knowledge element, expanded beyond the bill's title, "escaping from custody." Defendant contended that the unamended version of the bail jumping statute applied to his case and, therefore, that his conviction should be reversed because the State did not prove that he knowingly failed to appear. Construing the title broadly, the court on appeal held that the general title was constitutional, as bail jumping was a form of escape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1851 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Davis


NO. 53043-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


125 Wn. App. 59; 104 P.3d 11; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2979



December 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Respondent's and Appellant's Motion to Publish January 5, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Davis, 124 Wn. App. 1035, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3451 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which refused to consider his motion to withdraw his guilty plea to one count of delivery of cocaine. He also appealed the order compelling a DNA sample pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the court was required to consider the motion to withdraw his guilty plea because judgment had not yet occurred under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 4.2(f). Although the precise meaning of judgment under Rule 4.2 had not been decided, Washington courts had considered whether oral pronouncements of sentences were final in other contexts. Concluding that "judgment" under Rule 4.2(f) meant the date the judgment and sentence were filed with the clerk, the court held that the trial court erred by not considering the merits of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. Because the determination of whether defendant's plea of guilty was voluntary and intelligent was a question of fact peculiarly within the province of the trial court, the court remanded the issue and defendant was entitled to representation by counsel on the motion because it was an essential stage of his prosecution. The court also held that Wash. Rev. Code § Wash. Rev. Code Ann. § 43.43.754 is constitutional and cheek swabbing was a lawful means of collecting DNA samples under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the superior court for a decision on the merits on defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea.

Fria v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 53653-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


125 Wn. App. 531; 105 P.3d 33; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2981



December 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 20, 2005.
Reported at Fria v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 124 Wn. App. 1035, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3454 (2004)
Reconsideration denied by, Ordered published by, 01/20/2005
Review denied by, Motion granted by Fria v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 154 Wn.2d 1018, 113 P.3d 1039, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 516 (Wash., June 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-2-01780-1. Date filed: 11/15/2002. Judge signing: Hon. John Erlick.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, claimant, received workers' compensation payments and funds from a third party tort claim. Respondent, Washington Department of Labor and Industries, entered a final order requiring the claimant to reimburse it for workers' compensation payments the claimant had received. The order was affirmed by the Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals, and the King County Superior Court, Washington, dismissed the case. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant injured himself while working. The claimant applied for and received workers compensation, and also filed a third party lawsuit. The claimant informed the Department that he had recovered $ 37,000 in settlement, and upon being informed of the settlement, the Department closed the claim and issued the final order. The claimant sought to invalidate the portion of Wash. Rev. Code § 51.24.060 that required the offset. The claimant argued that the Department should not be permitted to reimburse itself from any funds recovered in the tort action for noneconomic injuries such as pain and suffering for which industrial insurance did not compensate. The appellate court ruled that the claimant had not shown how the constitutional principles he asserted related to the workers' compensation statute. The claimant provided no authority to support his claim of a fundamental right to a tort remedy, did not adequately rebut the Department's authority to the contrary, and he provided only a theoretical discussion of each constitutional protection he argued the statute violated, without tethering his theory to case law or the facts of his case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1853 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Responsible Wildlife Mgmt. v. State


No. 30940-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


124 Wn. App. 566; 103 P.3d 203; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2960



December 7, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Citizens for Responsible Wildlife Mgmt. v. State, 149 Wn.2d 622, 71 P.3d 644, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 452 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit organizations challenged initiatives prohibiting various hunting and trapping practices, arguing the initiatives violated respondent State's duty to control and manage wildlife for the public's benefit (public trust doctrine). The Superior Court, Thurston County (Washington), entered summary judgment in favor of the State. The nonprofits appealed.


OVERVIEW: Washington voters approved initiative 655, codified at Wash. Rev. Code § 77.15.245, which made it unlawful to hunt black bear with the aid of bait or to hunt black bear, cougar, bobcat, or lynx with the aid of dogs. Washington voters approved initiative 713, codified at Wash. Rev. Code §§ 77.15.192, .194, .196, and .198, which prohibited the use of body-gripping traps and other devices to capture animals and banned the use of two poisons, sodium fluoroacetate and sodium cyanide. At issue was the jus publicum, or public authority interest. The initiatives' bans were also subject to important exceptions. The initiatives did not interfere with a State grant of authority to a local government. In passing the initiatives, Washington voters did not give up control over the State's natural resources in violation of the public trust doctrine. Rather, the initiatives as implemented provided specific restrictions on techniques for hunting and trapping certain wild animals. If anything, this was an assumption of greater rather than lesser control. The nonprofits' challenge failed, because the State did not relinquish control over the public's interest in the State's natural resources.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of the State was affirmed.

 

1854 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hale


No. 30517-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2963



December 7, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 03-1-00620-3. Date filed: 06/13/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Barbara D Johnson.
State v. Hale, 124 Wn. App. 1031, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3436 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) convicted defendant of first degree burglary and first degree assault under an accomplice liability theory. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.08.020(3), to show accomplice liability, the State had to prove defendant knew about the crimes the principal committed. There was no abuse of discretion in allowing a qualified expert to explain the slang term "tax." No evidence supported a finding that defendant acted as a principal. The only way the jury could find him guilty was if they found accomplice liability. The jury instructions properly stated the law and required the jury to find defendant, whether as accomplice or principal, committed each element of the crimes. The jury instructions correctly informed the jury that when one accomplice was deemed armed, other accomplices could be considered armed. It was harmless error to include the word "possession" in the special verdict form, as the verdict would have been the same. The prosecutor's comments in closing argument did not warrant reversal. As the record supported the State's reference in closing argument to defendant's knowledge that the principal was armed, counsel's failure to object during closing argument did not fall below an objective standard of performance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1855 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Routt


No. 30935-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2967



December 7, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Lewis County. Docket No: 03-1-00284-9. Date filed: 10/08/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Richard Lynn Brosey.
State v. Routt, 124 Wn. App. 1032, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3440 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of methamphetamine and use of drug paraphernalia in the Superior Court of Lewis County, Washington. Defendant appealed, asserted the trial court erred in denying her motion to suppress the evidence seized without a warrant. She argued that the officer's reason for the initial traffic stop, obstructing the roadway, was invalid. She also asserted that the statute authorizing a strip search was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The record established that the officer observed defendant's car in a cul-de-sac. The officer testified that he found the dome light suspicious. The officer asserted he was not sure whether a large vehicle would have been able to pass the car. The evidence was contradictory as to whether the car was one foot or two feet away from the curb. Even though neither the officer or the trial court could determine what if any law was being violated, the trial court concluded that some law must have been violated. The appellate court concluded that defendant must have violated Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.575, which required a car to be parked within 12 inches of the curb. The appellate court also concluded that the officer had an objective, reasonable suspicion that the car was improperly parked on a public street. Consequently, where defendant's passenger was arrested on an outstanding warrant, and a search of the car was done incident to his arrest, the methamphetamine found was admissible. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.130, allowing for a strip search, was unconstitutional, where there was reasonable suspicion that defendant had contraband.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence, and her conviction, were affirmed.

 

1856 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Paradise, Inc. v. Pierce County


No. 51098-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


124 Wn. App. 759; 102 P.3d 173; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2944



December 6, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Paradise, Inc. v. Pierce County, 154 Wn.2d 1027, 120 P.3d 73, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 608 (Wash., July 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 01-2-21035-1.KNT. Date filed in Superior Court: Final Judgment - August 27, 2002; Judgment on Jury Verdict - September 9, 2002. Superior Court Judge Signing: Dean S. Lum.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff casino commenced this action seeking damages as well as declaratory and injunctive relief, claiming respondent County passed an invalid ordinance that violated equal protection and substantive and procedural due process, and constituted a taking. The Superior Court, King County (Washington), found for the casino. The County appealed.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether a county ordinance banning social card rooms constituted either a taking or a denial of due process, whether the County was estopped from enforcing the ordinance, and whether it either violated equal protection or was in conflict with and thus preempted by state statute. The threshold questions were whether it destroyed or derogated any fundamental attribute of property ownership. If the property owner claimed less than a total taking and if a fundamental attribute of ownership was not otherwise implicated, then the second threshold question was whether the challenged regulation safeguarded the public interest in health, safety, the environment, or the fiscal integrity of an area. Because the answer to both threshold questions was no, there was no taking. There was no destruction or derogation of any fundamental attribute of ownership - no total taking or denial of due process, the County was not estopped from enforcing the ordinance, and the ordinance did not violate equal protection and was not in conflict with and thus preempted by state statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1857 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Wash. State Geoduck Harvest Ass'n v. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 31004-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


124 Wn. App. 441; 101 P.3d 891; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2919



November 30, 2004, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant geoduck harvest association filed suit, seeking to have Wash. Rev. Code § 79.96.080 declared invalid under the public trust doctrine and equal protection principles, and generally challenged the department of natural resources' right to manage resources on aquatic lands. The Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, granted summary judgment in favor of the department. The association appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the association argued that the department had no authority to regulate geoduck harvesting and that its regulations for auctioning geoduck harvesting rights: (1) violated the public trust doctrine; (2) violated equal protection safeguards; and (3) were inconsistent with Wash. Rev. Code § 77.04.012. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the department could manage and sell geoducks on public lands, which included state-owned aquatic lands, under Wash. Rev. Code chs. 79.02, 79.90. Further, the department had a continuing obligation under the public trust doctrine to manage the use of the resources on the land for the public interest, and shellfish embedded on public property were resources that invoked a public right under the public trust doctrine. The department's procedures and regulation of commercial geoduck harvesting served the public, satisfied the public trust doctrine's requirements, and was not an unconstitutional infringement on the public's rights. The challenged statute applied only to geoduck harvesting, did not create classes of harvesters, and, thus, did not trigger equal protection principles.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1858 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Olympic Pipe Line Co. v. Thoeny


No. 31613-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


124 Wn. App. 381; 101 P.3d 430; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2840



November 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Olympic Pipe Line Co. v. Thoeny, 154 Wn.2d 1026, 120 P.3d 577, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 605 (Wash., July 13, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington), which entered judgment in favor of respondent pipe company in a condemnation action.


OVERVIEW: The company had pipes underneath the owner's land. When the owners sought to revoke their permission to use the property, the company filed a condemnation action. The trial court condemned a portion of the property and dismissed an inverse condemnation and trespass claim. The owners then sought review. In affirming, the court determined that it was entitled to review whether or not the company's statutory authority was constitutional. However, the challenge under Wash. Rev. Code § 8.20.160 was meritless since damages were favored over an injunction after a taking under Washington law. Further, the dismissal of the inverse condemnation claim was proper because the damages were the same as those in condemnation cases. However, the owners were not precluded from bringing their claims for an additional trespass in a separate tort action. The owners were entitled to interest under Wash. Rev. Code § 19.52.010(1) from the date that the company's possession became non-permissive until compensation was paid into the trial court. But, the owners failed to satisfy the necessary criteria for attorney fees under Wash. Rev. Code § 8.25.070(1) on appeal or at trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for a determination of interest, but affirmed in all other respects.

State v. Jackson


No. 30510-1-II

He moved for relief from judgment on October 17, 2002, well after the one-year time limit in § 10.73.090. Further, his motion was not based solely on one or more of the grounds listed in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Citizens for Safety & Envt v. Wash. DOT

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant organization sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the Department of Transportation (department), and granted its motion for summary judgment in the organization's action seeking to invalidate a permit issued by the department to an Indian tribe.


OVERVIEW: The organization sought to invalidate a permit issued by the department to an Indian tribe. The permit allowed the tribe to access its property and an amphitheater from a state route. State v. Chiofar


No. 52386-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2836



November 22, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Chiofar, 124 Wn. App. 1018, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3384 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-1-10218-9. Date filed: 05/09/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Carol a Schapira.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of intimidation of a judge in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.72.160 and 9A.04.110(25)(a), (e), and (j).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had filed a civil lawsuit concerning the value of coins that he owned. Opposing counsel filed interrogatories for which defendant provided answers. When opposing counsel asked for more in-depth answers, defendant stated that he could not provide them. Counsel then filed a motion to compel and defendant filed a motion for reconsideration, which was denied. Soon after, defendant called and left the judge's bailiff six telephone messages. Code § 9A.72.160, relating to threats defined by Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.04.110(25)(e) and (j) were not overbroad. Further, the admissions in defendant's brief and his testimony at trial were both sufficient to satisfy two elements of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.72.160(1), that the threats be directed to a judge because of a ruling or decision of the judge in an official proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1862 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Moses Lake v. Salinas


No. 22159-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2807



November 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at City of Moses Lake v. Salinas, 124 Wn. App. 1017, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3378 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: GRANT. Docket No(s): 02-2-00655-4. Judge signing: JOHN M. ANTOSZ. Date filed: May 16, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Grant County Disability Board, determined that cross-appellant firefighter was no longer disabled and could return to work. The firefighter wanted to return to work. However, appellant City claimed the firefighter could not return to work because he was over the age of 50 when his disability ceased. The Grant County Superior Court, Washington, entered summary judgment in favor of the firefighter. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board determined on July 11, 2001, the firefighter's 50th birthday, that he was no longer disabled. Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.130(3) provided that, if at the time that a disability ceased, the member was over the age of 50, he or she would then receive either disability retirement allowance or retirement for service allowance, whichever was greater. The City claimed the firefighter could not return to work because he was over 50 on the date of the Board's decision. Thus, the issue was whether the firefighter could be reinstated given the provisions of § 41.26.130(3). The appellate court held that, as the Board's findings of fact stated its decision was based upon medical opinions from May 2001, indicating the firefighter could return to work without restrictions, the latter date was the relevant date. Thus, at the time his disability ceased, the firefighter was not over the age of 50. Finally, no law prohibited the Board from determining the firefighter's reinstatement was effective July 11, 2001. The City's argument that the Board exceeded its authority by reinstating the firefighter as of July 11, 2001, when it did not enter its order until September 2001, was rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Statutory attorney fees were awarded to the employee on appeal.

 

1863 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Alkire


No. 52500-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


124 Wn. App. 169; 100 P.3d 837; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2795



November 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by, in part, Remanded by State v. Alkire, 154 Wn.2d 1032, 119 P.3d 852, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 706 (Wash., Aug. 24, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, convicted defendant of second degree possession of stolen property and one count of attempting to elude a pursuing police vehicle. The trial court ruled that the presumptive sentence was too lenient and imposed an exceptional sentence of 29 months on each count, to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the United States Supreme Court had declared Washington's exceptional sentence provisions facially unconstitutional. The court noted that the only relevant fact was defendant's offender score, which was based exclusively on the jury's finding that he committed the current offenses and on his prior convictions, to which he stipulated and which were expressly excluded from the prohibition against improper judicial fact-finding. Based solely on defendant's undisputed criminal history, the offender scores were extremely high. A standard range concurrent sentence would have meant he received no punishment for one of his crimes. A judge could, consistent with the Sixth Amendment and due process, impose an enhanced sentence based on the fact of a prior conviction. Defendant's exceptional sentence fell squarely within the narrow exception for prior convictions. Prior convictions did not need be proved to a jury. The trial court merely fixed the punishment within the authorized range. Exercising judicial discretion within the range authorized by law was not fact-finding. The exercise of sentencing jurisdiction was not a fact that had to be submitted to a jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Day v. McKinney


No. 30648-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2706



November 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Docket No: 94-3-00109-4. Date filed: 06/09/2003. Judge signing: Hon. F. Mark McCauley.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the modification of his child support obligation by a Washington trial court.


OVERVIEW: The father argued, inter alia, that the trial court should have held a hearing before modifying the support order because there had been a substantial change in the circumstances of the parties. The court of appeals disagreed. The record showed that the trial court did hold a hearing before modifying the child support order. The trial court ordered extensive discovery of financial documentation from all parties, including documentation from other adults residing with the respective parents. The trial court held a hearing that included argument from the father's attorney, the mother's attorney, and the prosecutor. Those procedures comported with the requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.175. The record did not show that the father requested a hearing with oral testimony as required by the statute. Nor did he claim to have made such a request of the trial court. Moreover, the record showed no extraordinary features of the case warranting oral testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Amezcua


No. 22239-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2419

NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Amezcua, 123 Wn. App. 1056, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3292 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: STEVENS. Docket No(s): 02-1-00243-3. Judge signing: LARRY M. KRISTIANSON. Date filed: July 2, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stevens County (Washington) that convicted him of child rape, child molestation, and possession of depictions of minors engaged in sexually explicit conduct. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the warrant affidavit and evidence, jury instructions, the effectiveness of his counsel, the victim's hearsay statements, and the scope of the search.


OVERVIEW: The mother of an eight-year-old victim notified police after discovering that her son had been sexually molested and raped by defendant and shown pornographic images on the Internet. Police obtained a warrant and seized defendant's computer. Defendant appealed his conviction, claiming there was no probable cause for the warrant as the affidavit contained no corroboration of the victim's statements. The court held that probable cause for the warrant was not based on an informant's tip but on the direct report of the crime victim's mother and the police investigation. Unlike a third party informant, a victim was presumed to be reliable. The court held there was no need for an unanimity jury instruction on the counts alleging a single act of rape because a general verdict reflected unanimous agreement that the one violation occurred, and that the lack of the unanimity instruction on counts involving multiple acts was harmless. The court held that the required evidence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.835(2) of defendant's sexual motivations in possessing child pornography was sufficient, and it rejected defendant's claim that sexual motivation could be proved solely by direct evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of child rape, child molestation, and possession of depictions of minors engaged in sexually explicit conduct.

 

1867 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


North Div. Complex, L.L.C. v. Spokane County


No. 22545-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2411



October 26, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at N. Div. Complex, L.L.C. v. Spokane County, 123 Wn. App. 1057, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3295 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-2-03603-4. Judge signing: LINDA G. TOMPKINS. Date filed: October 22, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county enacted ordinances regarding storm water control. Plaintiff corporations filed a complaint for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief from the ordinances. The corporations moved for summary judgment, claiming the ordinances were for land use control and the county did not follow the statutory procedure for enacting them. The Superior Court for Spokane County, Washington, agreed and granted the motion. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county argued that the corporations' assertion that they did not comply with Washington Growth Management Act (GMA) procedure when it enacted the ordinances brought the issue under the jurisdiction of Washington Growth Management Hearings Board (GMHB). The corporations countered that GMHB did not have jurisdiction because neither ordinance was a developmental regulation. The court held that pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70A.280(1)(a), a developmental regulation had to be adopted under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70A.040 in order for the GMHB to have jurisdiction. Because that requirement was not met, the GMHB did not have jurisdiction. Consequently, the corporations were neither required to bring the action to the GMHB, nor did they have any administrative remedies to exhaust. Finally, the court noted that storm water drainage ordinances were land use control ordinances. Because the ordinances were "official controls," the county had to follow Wash. Rev. Code §§ 36.70.570 to 36.70.650 when adopting them. The latter statutes required specific procedures and a public hearing, which the county did not follow. Thus, the trial court properly declared the ordinances invalid.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Harris


No. 52548-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


123 Wn. App. 906; 99 P.3d 902; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2405



October 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals November 15, 2004.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Reconsideration denied by State v. Harris, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3005 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 8, 2004)
Review granted by, in part, Remanded by State v. Harris, 154 Wn.2d 1032, 119 P.3d 852, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 703 (Wash., Aug. 24, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree child molestation and imposed an exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: After convicting defendant of first-degree child molestation on stipulated facts, the superior court sua sponte imposed an exceptional sentence above the standard range based on findings it made at sentencing. Defendant appealed and the court reversed the sentence, stating that the exceptional sentence statutes were not facially invalid, but that defendant's stipulation at trial did not admit the facts the superior court relied on to support the exceptional sentence. On remand, the superior court had authority to empanel a jury to consider aggravating factors. The superior court made no findings following the bench trial that would have supported aggravating factors. The aggravating factors it relied on for the exceptional sentence were based on facts found outside the trial record. Defendant's trial stipulation could not be used to support the aggravating factors for that reason as well. Accordingly, his exceptional sentence violated U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court further stated that double jeopardy principles did not apply to his sentencing and that the invalid procedures were severable from the remainder of the exceptional sentence provisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the sentence and remanded for further proceedings.

Thatcher v. Thatcher


No. 22493-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2361



October 19, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Thatcher v. Thatcher, 123 Wn. App. 1052, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3275 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-2-05772-4. Judge signing: DAVID M. THORN, COURT COMMISSIONER. Date filed: September 29, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, granted appellee wife a protection order against appellant husband, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 26.50.030. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband pointed out apparent inconsistencies between the trial court's oral ruling and its written ruling, where it appeared to have made contradictory statements in its oral ruling indicating that the husband could be present at church or a child's sporting event at the same time as the wife. The appellate court found that the husband's attorney did not seek revision of the written order under Wash. Rev. Code § 2.24.050. The appellate court had to rely on the written ruling and had to assume that the court modified its oral decision before entering its protection order. The trial court had the authority to grant a second protection order, as it had been informed of the earlier temporary order of protection. The husband's rights were properly restricted, when his presence interfered with the wife's right to be free of invasive, oppressive, and harmful behavior. The wife failed to file an affidavit of financial need and, in any event, the order was entered under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.50; therefore, the wife's request for attorney fees was denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Van Buren


No. 30237-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


123 Wn. App. 634; 98 P.3d 1235; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2295



October 5, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by, in part, Remanded by State v. Van Buren, 154 Wn.2d 1032, 119 P.3d 852, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 708 (2005)
Remanded by State v. Van Buren, 136 Wn. App. 577, 150 P.3d 597, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 35 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Van Buren, 121 Wn. App. 1056, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3511 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which imposed an exceptional sentence after defendant entered an Alford pled to two counts of third-degree rape of a child, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.079, and to one count of third-degree rape, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.060.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an Alford plea to charges of third-degree rape and third-degree rape of a child. The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence, and, on appeal, the court affirmed, stating that the 120-month sentence was supported by defendant's high offender score and the fact that imposition of a standard range sentence would have resulted in "free crimes." His offender score calculation was in excess of nine, which would have resulted in free crimes if the trial court had imposed a sentence within the standard range. Those factors were calculations based on defendant's criminal history and were not findings of disputed fact that required jury resolution. Moreover, the sentence imposed was not excessive as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Pederson v. County of Skagit


No. 53554-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2291



October 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Pederson v. Skagit County, 123 Wn. App. 1037, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3215 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Skagit County. Docket No: 03-2-01192-7. Judge signing: Hon. Michael E Rickert. Judgment or order under review Date filed: 11/21/2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent public utility district's (PUD) application for a shoreline substantial development/variance/conditional use permit was granted and it formed a local utility district (LUD). Appellant property owner's motion to reconsider the permit approvals was denied, and respondent county board of commissioners affirmed. The Superior Court of Skagit County, Washington, dismissed the owner's appeal. The owner sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the property owner raised several issues challenging the dismissal of his claim for failure to comply with the procedural requirements of the Washington Land Use Petition Act (LUPA), Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.005 et seq., arguing that the LUPA did not apply to his action. The appellate court found that because the owner's challenge to the LUD formation issue was not a land use decision, it could not be brought as part of a LUPA appeal. Further, the trial court had no authority to review the owner's growth management claims regardless of his compliance with LUPA procedures; thus, any of the owner's that were subject to review by the growth management hearings board would have been dismissed in any event. Because the owner failed to comply with LUPA's procedural requirements, it was impossible for him to succeed on his LUPA appeal, and therefore impossible to succeed in a claim for monetary damages or compensation. Although some of the owner's arguments were excluded from LUPA review, this action was brought as a LUPA petition, and those issues not properly included in a LUPA appeal should have been brought in separate actions or before different tribunals.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1872 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Des Moines Marina Ass'n v. City of Des Moines


No. 52757-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


124 Wn. App. 282; 100 P.3d 310; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2210



September 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Appellant's Motion to Publish October 25, 2004.
Reported at Des Moines Marina Ass'n v. City of Des Moines, 123 Wn. App. 1029, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3186 (2004)
Review denied by Des Moines Marina Ass'n v. City of Des Moines, 154 Wn.2d 1018, 113 P.3d 1040, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 510 (Wash., June 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a marina association, two nonresident tenants, and an association officer, sued appellant city for adopting an ordinance to increase moorage rates. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) decided the ordinance violated the federal Equal Protection Clause, the association did not have standing to sue, and the city had authority to increase moorage rates. The association and the tenants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance increasing moorage rates did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The imposition of the leasehold excise tax (LET) was justified as an effort to compensate municipalities for services to lessees of publicly owned property. As it was paid for by both residents and nonresidents, it did not provide a basis to differentiate between the two regarding the amount paid for city services. It did not undermine the rational basis that justified the city's decision to charge nonresidents higher moorage rates, and the trial court erred in holding the city violated the Equal Protection Clause. Because there was no evidence that any association members were nonresidents, the association did not show it had standing to sue on behalf of its members. Wash. Rev. Code §§ 35.22.280 and 35.23.440 allowed the city to set rates for the use of its marina. Neither statute limited the city's authority to increase moorage rates for marina tenants. The trial court's dismissal of the two nonresident tenants' Wash. Const. art. I, § 12 claim was not error as they presented no argument regarding whether residents could be treated differently than nonresidents.


OUTCOME: The decisions to dismiss the association for lack of standing, that the city had authority to charge market rates for moorage, and the dismissal of the state constitutional claim were affirmed. The decision that charging nonresidents a higher moorage rate than residents violated the Equal Protection Clause was reversed. The judgment was reversed and entered in favor of the nonresident tenants.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, father, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, denying his motion to vacate the order modifying his child support, challenging the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.19, in the underlying action with respondent, mother.


OVERVIEW: The parties were married in 1987, and had two children before their marriage was dissolved in 2000. The father did not appeal from the underlying support modification order. The father argued that the trial court erred in imputing income to him because it made no finding that he was voluntarily unemployed. The appellate court ruled that the father failed to satisfy his burden of demonstrating that the statute was unconstitutional. Furthermore, the mother's request for attorney fees on appeal was denied, because the mother presented no authority for the proposition that a non-attorney appearing pro se could be awarded attorney fees.

No. 53198-1-I

2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2226



September 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County; Docket No: 99-2-02194-8. Date filed: 11/21/2002. Judge signing: Hon. Richard D Hicks.
Havsy v. Dep't of Health, 123 Wn. App. 1030, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3190 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which affirmed an order by the presiding officer (PO) of respondent Washington State Department of Health Board of Osteopathic Medicine and Surgery, imposing sanctions against the doctor for engaging in unprofessional conduct. The sanctions required the doctor to receive psychological evaluation and to provide his patients with written estimates.


OVERVIEW: The doctor argued that the PO's findings of fact did not support the conclusion that his conduct constituted moral turpitude. The court held that there was clear and convincing evidence that the doctor's conduct rose to the level of acts indicating his unfitness to practice the profession and undermined the purposes of the Washington Uniform Discipline Act, Wash. The doctor's conduct also constituted negligence under Wash. Rev. Code § 18.130.180(4). Patients experienced psychological distress as a result of his screaming, yelling, and name-calling. The sanctions imposed directly related to the PO's duty to protect the public and were supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court denied the doctor's request for attorney fees and costs.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County, Washington, convicting him for obstruction of justice.

Golden v. Fisher (In re L.B.F.)


No. 30396-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2109



September 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Golden v. Fisher (In re Custody of L.B.F.), 123 Wn. App. 1017, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2891 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 00-3-00194-5. Date filed: 04/11/2003. Judge signing: Hon. James E Warme.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandfather motioned to intervene for visitation with his granddaughter, where appellee grandmother had legal custody of the child. The Superior Court of Cowlitz County, Washington, ruled that the grandmother's court-ordered legal custody conferred on her the constitutional rights of a fit parent and denied the grandfather visitation. The grandfather appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grandfather argued the trial judge at the hearing lacked the authority to reverse the first judge's order allowing him to intervene. The appellate court noted that the grandfather was a necessary party to the visitation issue in the original custody action pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 19(a). The order restraining the child's parents and grandmother from allowing the child to have contact with the grandfather was improper and the first judge correctly provided the grandfather a remedy by granting his motion to intervene. Accordingly, the hearing judge's post-trial denial of the grandfather's intervention motion was error. The appellate court held that the trial court erred by concluding as a matter of law that a non-parent cannot bring a third party visitation action under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.240. Court-appointed custodians, such as the grandmother, did not have the right to control visitation of their wards. Absent legislative action, non-parents, e.g., legal guardians, grandparents, and persons acting in an in loco parentis capacity, did not have the same constitutional rights as a parent.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

1878 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Fredrick


No. 30605-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


123 Wn. App. 347; 97 P.3d 47; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2029



September 8, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:  PUBLISHED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with crimes related to possession of drugs and drug paraphernalia. However, the instant action concerned only defendant's conviction for bail jumping, for her failure to appear for court dates in the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, in relation to events which occurred after her arrest and during the course of the aforementioned criminal proceedings on drug charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted the State was relieved of its burden to disprove the statutory defense to bail jumping because the defense of "uncontrollable circumstances," "negated" the knowledge element. That argument failed, however, because there was no law supporting the contention that the State had to disprove the affirmative defense to bail jumping. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that she presented sufficient evidence to show uncontrollable circumstances. The testimony of her friends, that she was sick, did not meet the statutory definition of "uncontrollable circumstances." She presented no evidence that she was in the hospital because of illness or any other similar barrier to her attendance. The appellate court held that because the knowledge element of bail jumping did not implicate the statutory affirmative defenses to bail jumping, the defenses did not unconstitutionally shift the burden to defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

In re Det. of Jones


No. 44442-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE

Holmes Harbor Sewer Dist. v. Frontier Bank


No. 52650-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


123 Wn. App. 45; 96 P.3d 442; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1915



August 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Holmes Harbor Sewer Dist. v. Holmes Harbor Home Bldg. LLC, 154 Wn.2d 1001, 113 P.3d 481, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 397 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Holmes Harbor Sewer Dist. v. Holmes Harbor Home Bldg. LLC, 155 Wn.2d 858, 123 P.3d 823, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 923 (Wash., Nov. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court County: Island. Superior Court Cause No: 02-2-00294-8. Date filed in Superior Court: February 27, 2003. Superior Court Judge Signing: Alan Hancock.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sewer district challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Island County (Washington), which granted respondent owner's motion for summary judgment and determined that the district's utility charges on unimproved lots amounted to a tax rather than a regulatory fee. The owner appealed the portion of the decision that determined that the district would have been able to charge a fee to unimproved lots.


OVERVIEW: The owner held title to unimproved lots. The district sent bills to the owner for sewer services. When the owner refused to pay, the district instituted foreclosure proceedings. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted the owner's motion, determined that the charge was an unconstitutional tax, but also held that the district was allowed to charge the fee to unimproved lots. Both parties then sought review. In reversing, the court held that the district was permitted to charge rates to vacant lots where service was available, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 57.08.081(1). An actual connection to the sewer was not required. Next, the court applied a three-part test to determine whether the district was taxing the lots or merely charging a regulatory fee. The primary purpose of the district was to collect revenue to finance the public improvement. Further, the money collected was allocated exclusively to the operation of the sewer system. Finally, there was a direct relationship between the rate charged and the service received. Each lot had a right to use the sewer system. Based on the three-part test, the charge was not a tax.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that the charge was a tax was reversed. The court remanded the case for entry of judgment in favor of the district. The issue raised by the owner on appeal was affirmed.

Sound Mind & Body, Inc. v. City of Seattle


No. 53320-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1875



August 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-2-27890-6. Date filed: 10/09/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Gregory P Canova.
Sound Mind & Body, Inc. v. City of Seattle, 122 Wn. App. 1074, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2570 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondents, the city and a market's owners, dismissed the corporation's action, and found that the corporation failed to show that it was injured by closure of a street for a Sunday market.


OVERVIEW: Every Sunday, vendors of crafts, collectibles, produce, and other foodstuff sold their wares at the market. The corporation owned and ran two fitness clubs and filed an action against the city and market's owners, stating in part that the market constituted a nuisance in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 7.48.010 and 7.48.120, and that the city took the corporation's property in violation of Wash. Const. art. I, § 16 for the benefit of private persons. The trial court dismissed the action and the court affirmed, stating that the trial court did not err in dismissing the claim of nuisance per se because the corporation did not show that the market was a use of property that was not permissible under any circumstances. Further, the street use permits were all that was required to make the market lawful for purposes of nuisance analysis. The takings claim failed because the corporation was not denied access to its property and there was no tortious interference with a business expectancy because there was no evidence that the market affected the corporation's business relationships, either current or prospective, or caused it any other injury or damage.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Det. of Scott


No. 50631-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1876



August 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

In re Det. of Scott, 122 Wn. App. 1071, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2561 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which granted the State's petition and committed defendant under the sexually violent predator act (SVPA), Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. The jury found that defendant was an SVP and that a less restrictive alternative (LRA) to total confinement would not be in his best interests or would be inadequate to protect the community.


OVERVIEW: The jury found that defendant was an SVP and that a less restrictive alternative (LRA) to total confinement would not be in his best interests or would not adequately protect the community. The court stayed defendant's appeal pending the decision of the Washington Supreme Court in another case, which held that the statutory prohibition in Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.090 against considering LRAs during commitment hearings and delaying consideration until the first annual review did not violate equal protection principles, as protection of the public and the treatment of SVPs were rational bases for the restriction. The court found that, because at the point of the annual review, the trial court did have authority to order conditions of release, there was no further need for the instruction which informed the jury that the trial court had no authority to order a defendant into an LRA or to undergo treatment in an LRA. That instruction was given in defendant's trial, therefore the court vacated the verdict in the LRA phase of his trial, and held his arguments concerning it were moot. The court rejected defendant's other claims of error and affirmed his commitment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that committed defendant as an SVP and vacated the verdict in the LRA proceeding.

In re Pers. Restraint of Kiet Hoang Le


No. 30101-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


122 Wn. App. 816; 95 P.3d 1254; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1864



August 10, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Affirmed by, Sub nomine at In re Pers. Restraint of Domingo, 155 Wn.2d 356, 119 P.3d 816, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 788 (Wash., Sept. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Clark County. Superior Court Docket No. 95-1-01659-6. Date Filed In Superior Court: March 5, 2003. Superior Court Judge Signing: John F. Nichols.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for two counts of first-degree kidnapping, two counts of first-degree robbery, one count of first-degree burglary, and one count of first-degree possession of stolen property. He filed a personal restraint petition, asserting that his due process rights were violated when the jury received erroneous accomplice liability instructions. The Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, denied his petition, and he sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted the instructions used in his trial were found erroneous by a Washington Appellate Court, and that the two Washington Supreme Court cases that appellate court relied on were significant changes in the law, exempting him from the one-year limit for filing personal restraint petitions under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1). However, as to one of the subject cases, the subject appellate court had relied on a dissenting opinion. In the second case, the Washington Supreme Court had not announced a significant change in the law with respect to accomplice liability, but had merely stated, "in part," that knowledge by the accomplice that a principal intended to commit "a crime" did not impose strict liability for any and all offenses that followed. Because the aforementioned cases did not set forth a significant change in the law, defendant's petition for personal restraint was untimely. Finally, the evidence established beyond a reasonable doubt that the trial court's accomplice liability instruction did not contribute to the jury's verdict and any error was harmless. The evidence showed defendant was a willing participant in the crimes and did not withdraw.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court, denying defendant's personal restraint petition as untimely, was affirmed.

State v. Pacificar


No. 51955-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1849



August 9, 2004, Filed

State v. Pacificar, 122 Wn. App. 1057, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2503 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of felony murder in the first degree and ordered him to pay restitution to the parents of the victim. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the superior court erred in denying his motion to strike the restitution order based on the limitation period in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090. He argued that the statute did not apply, as the restitution order was not entered within 60 days, and, therefore, was facially invalid. The appellate court noted that it had rejected a similar argument in a prior case and that the restitution order appeared valid on its face. Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1) barred collateral attacks brought more than one year after the judgment and sentence became final. Motions like the one brought by defendant under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 were subject to the statutory limitations period. There was no showing that the judgment and sentence was invalid on its face. Defendant did not show that any exceptions to the statute of limitations applied. Nothing indicated that defendant was ever affirmatively misinformed regarding his eligibility for good time credit. Defendant did not establish a violation of his constitutional right to appeal under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.585(1). Defendant's other claims were without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, for bail-jumping and sentenced to 43 months in prison. Defendant appealed.

In re Det. of Frisina


No. 46035-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1487



July 19, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 98-2-26085-8. Judgment or order under review Date filed: 01/10/2000.
In re Det. of Frisina, 122 Wn. App. 1032, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2590 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which committed him as a "sexually violent predator" (SVP) under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. Appellant claimed the trial court violated his due process rights by considering the likelihood that he would re-offend over his entire lifetime rather than in the foreseeable future. Appellant also challenged the admission of hearsay and actuarial assessment evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the trial court's decision committing him as an SVP. The court held that it did not need to address the hypothetical constitutional due process question, as appellant's argument that the trial court's decision was based on an improper time frame was contrary to the record. The court held that there was no reversible error regarding the admission of evidence. The court found that the alleged hearsay evidence were statements from appellant's counselors, supervisors, and corrections officers that were not admitted for the truth of the matter, but were admitted to show that appellant needed particular supervision or that he had been warned that certain behaviors were inappropriate. The court also found that the prison warning log testimony was admissible under the business records exception in Wash. R. Evid. 803(a)(6), because the entries were not based on the observation of others, but were based on the observation of the recording officer. The court also held that the actuarial assessment evidence was admissible under Wash. R. Evid. 702, 703, and 403 and that appellant's claims went to the weight of the evidence rather than its admissibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that committed appellant as a "sexually violent predator."

1888 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Carrillo v. City of Ocean Shores


No. 29735-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


122 Wn. App. 592; 94 P.3d 961; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1451



July 13, 2004, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city required appellee owners of vacant lots within the city limits to pay water and sewer "availability charges," although their properties were not connected to the water and sewer systems. The owners sued the city, claiming that the charges were unconstitutional property taxes and not permissible regulatory fees. The Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington) granted the owners' summary judgment motion. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city imposed a per lot charge for each lot that could be, but was not, connected to the municipal services. The city contended that the trial court erred in determining as a matter of law that the water and sewer availability charges were constitutionally invalid taxes rather than valid regulatory fees. The city admitted that its purpose in imposing the challenged user fee was to raise revenue because charging rates only to the property owners who chose to connect to the city's water and sewer systems would not generate sufficient revenue. The appellate court found that there was no direct benefit or identified regulatory use of the funds collected from the owners who were required to pay the charges. Instead, the city used the money raised by the charges to operate a free public recreational vehicles (RV) dump for use by all RVs in the area and to reduce the water and sewer charges paid by permanent residents of the developed land. Thus, the appellate court found that the charges were a revenue-generating method that was illegal, and the owners who paid the unauthorized availability charges were entitled to recover with interest the charges paid after April 8, 1996.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
