State v. McFadden


No. 52758-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1436



 July 12, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. McFadden, 122 Wn. App. 1026, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2258 (Wash. Ct. App., July 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No:03-1-00520-1. Judge signing: Hon. Gerald L Knight.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress, the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, found defendant guilty on one count of possession of a controlled substance (cocaine). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the State failed to prove that the officers had probable cause to stop him and, even assuming that the officers had probable cause to believe a traffic infraction had occurred, the stop was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the officers stopped defendant's car because the left brake light was not adequately illuminated; as the brake light was barely visible right behind the car, it was logical to infer that the light was not visible from 300 feet away, as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 46.37.200. Thus, the officers had probable cause to make a warrantless arrest. Contrary to defendant's assertion, nothing in the record indicated that the officers were suspicious of defendant and were looking for an excuse to stop him. Therefore, the trial court did not err in ruling that the evidence seized in the search incident to arrest was admissible. As evidence that defendant was arrested just after leaving a mobile home park where he purchased cocaine was not relevant to whether the defective brake light was a pretext for a warrantless search, defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to offer that evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Parentage of R.F.R.


No. 30452-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


122 Wn. App. 324; 93 P.3d 951; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1340



July 7, 2004, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, permitted appellee mother to relocate to Indiana with the parties' child, under the parental relocation statutes, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.09. Appellant father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court abused its discretion in determining that the mother was the parent entitled to the presumption in favor of relocation. The appellate court noted that the trial court carefully addressed the Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.520 factors on the record. But the father disputed the court's finding that the mother was the parent entitled to the presumption of relocation under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.430. Sufficient evidence supported the finding that the child resided a majority of the time with the mother. Based on the mother's trial testimony, there was evidence supporting the finding that she was the primary caregiver in California. The father had not met his burden of showing that Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.520 violated his substantive due process rights. He cited no authority directly supporting his claim. The State's ability to prevent the relocation of the custodial parent was limited by the right of the relocating parent to care for the child in the manner in which he or she saw fit. The trial court was required to intervene and necessarily choose between the parents' competing interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Willman v. WUTC


No. 22411-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


122 Wn. App. 194; 93 P.3d 909; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1308



July 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at Willman v. Wash. Utils. & Transp. Comm'n, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 258 (Wash., Mar. 1, 2005)
Review granted by Willman v. Wash. Utils. & Transp. Comm'n, 153 Wn.2d 1031, 110 P.3d 757, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 289 (2005)
Affirmed by Willman v. Wash. Utils. & Transp. Comm'n, 154 Wn.2d 801, 117 P.3d 343, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 670 (Wash., Aug. 11, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Yakima County, Washington, granted judgment in favor of appellees, Washington Utilities and Transportation Commission (WUTC) and utilities corporations, by affirming an ordinance adopted by a tribal council imposing a franchise fee from utilities operating within the boundaries of its reservation. The cost of the fees was passed on to all customers within the reservation. Appellant citizens' group appealed.


OVERVIEW: The group argued that the fee was presumptively invalid and discriminatory against nonmembers. They also argued that the WUTC erroneously concluded that the fee should be recovered only from customers within the reservation rather than from the utilities' customers statewide. The appellate court noted that, because the WUTC lacked the authority to determine whether the franchise fee was valid, the additional declarations were not material to either the agency or the superior court proceedings. The group provided no authority suggesting the WUTC had the jurisdiction to determine the validity of any tax. The tribe's franchise ordinance resolved disputes over the utilities' alleged trespasses on tribal land; the utilities thus may have chosen to pay the fee rather than to challenge its validity and still face the tribe's trespassing allegations. The group established that the validity of the franchise fee was questionable; however, it was not possible to conclude that the fee was clearly invalid. The revised tariffs did not violate Wash. Rev. Code § 80.280.090. The portion of the ordinance exacting a tax was a unilateral exaction; the utilities received nothing in return.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Peacock


No. 29910-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1297



June 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 01-1-03877-1. Date filed: 01/24/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Thomas P Larkin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicting him of unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(a)(1)(ii), and unlawful possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine, former Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.440 (2000).


OVERVIEW: The motor home defendant was driving had been reported stolen and was stopped by police. Following standard operating procedure with stolen vehicles, the officer looked inside the motor home and noticed the disabled ignition replaced with a toggle switch to start the vehicle, and a strong odor that he recognized as toluene, a solvent used in manufacturing methamphetamine. The appellate court ruled that the jury could have reasonably inferred that defendant had been engaged in the manufacturing of methamphetamine, and there was substantial evidence to support the jury's conclusion that defendant was in possession of pseudoephedrine. An officer found evidence of all three stages of methamphetamine manufacturing, and testified that he could "absolutely" say that methamphetamine had been manufactured using the items in the motor home. Defendant had been the sole driver and the sole occupant of the motor home containing the meth lab. The bottle containing pseudoephedrine and the pill bottles containing pseudoephedrine were located in the motor home and were in defendant's exclusive control.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Teitzel


No. 30112-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1305



June 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Teitzel, 122 Wn. App. 1014, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2083 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 99-1-04251-6. Date filed: 03/12/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Vicki Hogan.
State v. Teitzel, 109 Wn. App. 791, 37 P.3d 1236, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 46 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to vehicular homicide in the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington. The trial court sentenced defendant to 113 months in prison. The trial court imposed a standard 41 month sentence, plus an additional 72 months based on three consecutive 24 month sentence enhancements for each of his three prior offenses of driving while under the influence of intoxicants (DUI). Defendant appealed in regard to his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to modify his sentence. On appeal, defendant specifically attacked only one of his prior DUIs that was used to enhance his sentence. For that prior DUI, he had received a deferred prosecution. In State v. Shaffer, the court of appeals had held that former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(v) (1999) was unconstitutional. Former § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(v) violated due process because it allowed the trial court to impose a sentence enhancement based entirely on an unproven DUI charge. However, defendant's sentence enhancement for a prior DUI deferred prosecution involved former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(vii) (1999). Consequently, Shaffer's holding did not apply to defendant's sentence. Finally, pursuant to precedent, defendant's sentence could be enhanced for a prior DUI deferred prosecution under former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(vii). It was the "granting" of the prior deferred prosecution that triggered its treatment as a prior offense under former § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(vii). Thus, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to modify his sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1894 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Legrone


No. 51387-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1288



June 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Legrone, 122 Wn. App. 1009, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2065 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-1-01152-5. Date filed: 11/12/2002. Judge signing: Hon. Douglass North.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree kidnapping in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.40.020(1)(d).


OVERVIEW: A police officer noticed a vehicle parked without its lights on the side of road. The vehicle's lights then illuminated and it pulled away from the curb. He thought that the driver could potentially be a prowler and stopped the vehicle. The officer noticed that a young woman in the vehicle was crying and she told him that the men in the vehicle had kidnapped her and would have killed her but for the officer's intervention. Defendant was subsequently convicted of first-degree kidnapping and the court affirmed. The officer's suspicion, based on the late hour, the recent presence of car prowlers in the neighborhood, and the odd movement of the vehicle, became sufficiently reasonable and individualized to justify the stop when he discovered the vehicle's connection to a rental agency with a known history of irregular transactions. Also, the fact that the car had been rented in another city suggested that its occupants were not residents of the neighborhood, and intensified the officer's suspicion that he may have interrupted a car prowler or burglar. Thus, the officer was justified in making the investigative stop. Further, Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9A.46.020 was neither vague nor overbroad.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1895 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Heckel


No. 51204-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


122 Wn. App. 60; 93 P.3d 189; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1306



June 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by State v. Heckel, 153 Wn.2d 1021, 108 P.3d 1229, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 243 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Heckel v. Wash., 126 S. Ct. 387, 163 L. Ed. 2d 172, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5821 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Heckel, 143 Wn.2d 824, 24 P.3d 404, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 388 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted summary judgment in favor of appellant State, by entering a judgment and decree imposing permanent injunctions and a civil penalty on respondent, an Oregon citizen, for violations of Washington's Commercial Electronic Mail Act (Act), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 19.190. The trial court also awarded attorney fees and costs to the State. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen argued that the State failed to show that he knew or had reason to know that his spam had been sent to a particular e-mail address held by a Washington resident, that the Act as applied to him violated the Commerce Clauses, and that there was a factual issue for trial regarding whether his subject lines were "misleading" under the First Amendment analysis of commercial speech. The appellate court noted that the Act did not state that proof that the residency information was available from the Internet domain registrant was the exclusive means of proving knowledge under Wash. Rev. Code § 19.190.020(2). There was nothing in the record to indicate that the State intended to rely on the statute to show the citizen's knowledge. He failed to take any action to determine whether any of his intended bulk mail e-mail recipients were Washington residents or to change his practices to comply with the Act. The citizen had reason to know that his spam would be directed to Washington residents. The Act, as applied to him, did not violate the Commerce Clause. The resident's subject lines were deceptive and misleading and were not entitled to First Amendment protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1896 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dravis


No. 29960-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1218



June 15, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Dravis, 122 Wn. App. 1001, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2032 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 01-1-03466-1. Date filed: 01/14/2003. Judge signing: Hon. John A McCarthy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pleaded guilty to first- and second-degree child molestation so he could receive a special sex offender sentencing alternative, he obtained new counsel and filed a motion to withdraw his plea. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, denied defendant's motion and imposed a sentence prohibition forbidding contact with the victim and defendant's minor children. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court should have granted his motion to withdraw his guilty plea, because he received ineffective assistance of counsel and his plea was involuntary. Defendant also challenged the sentencing prohibition forbidding contact with all minors as unconstitutional. The appellate court found that defendant's counsel's tactical advice to seek a special sex offender sentencing alternative (SSOSA) was objectively reasonable, because the SSOSA sentence shortened defendant's sentence and imprisonment. Counsel's other decisions demonstrated effective assistance of counsel, as a fourth count against defendant was dropped and counsel successfully requested a competency evaluation for defendant. Counsel's failure to interview the victim was a reasonable strategy decision. The appellate court also found that defendant's plea was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary. However, the appellate court agreed that the sentencing prohibition was error, as there was no evidence that defendant ever molested his biological children or that he violated the pretrial release condition allowing only supervised contact with them.


OUTCOME: The trial court's refusal to allow withdrawal of defendant's guilty plea was affirmed, and the case was remanded for a hearing to determine the necessity and scope of the sentencing provision prohibiting defendant's contact with his minor biological children.

 

1897 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Levy


No. 52074-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1206



June 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 02-1-02453-4. Date filed: 02/27/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald X Castleberry.
State v. Levy, 121 Wn. App. 1079, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1972 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a firearm in the second degree, first-degree burglary with a deadly weapon allegation, and first-degree robbery with deadly weapon allegations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction on the grounds that the trial court erred in instructing the jury. Defendant claimed that the instructions amounted to unconstitutional comments on the evidence, as the challenged instructions contained "to wit" language that had been condemned by prior case law as constituting a comment on the evidence in violation of Wash. Const. art. IV, § 16. The court held that, under the unique circumstances presented by the case, the instructions either did not amount to a comment on the evidence, or the improper instructions were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court noted that, although it found the erroneous jury instructions harmless, the use of "to wit" language in jury instructions often amounted to an improper comment on the evidence and advised counsel to avoid the use of "to wit" language in future "to convict" instructions. The court rejected defendant's ineffective assistance claims, because he had not shown deficient performance or resulting prejudice. The court also rejected defendant's claim that it was improper for a co-defendant's attorney to assert his client's Fifth Amendment rights on her behalf.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1898 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Trummel v. Mitchell (In re Trummel)


No. 48662-4-I (Consolidated with no. 50830-0-I and NO. 50135-6-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1208



June 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Trummel v. Mitchell (In re Trummel), 121 Wn. App. 1078, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1966 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-2-04698-5. Date filed: 05/09/2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondents, corporation, residents, and administrator, and held that the neighbor was in contempt of court for persistently posting the residents' and administrator's names and addresses on the Internet. The administrator sought attorney fees on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued an order restraining the neighbor from harassing his neighbors in a high rise apartment building for senior citizens, and then jailed him for contempt of court when he persistently posted their names and addresses on the Internet. Although the neighbor vigorously put forth the First Amendment as a shield, the trial court focused on his conduct rather than his speech. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, stating that the trial court appropriately used the civil anti-harassment statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.14.010 et seq., to protect the residents from having to endure aggressive and hostile personal confrontations and surveillance while in the privacy of home. The trial court also appropriately concluded that the public posting of personal information violated the no-surveillance provision of the order. Because the anti-harassment orders were not void as a prior restraint, they could not be collaterally attacked and did not furnish a basis for vacating the contempt findings. Since the court affirmed the contempt findings and orders, there was no basis upon which to grant the neighbor's request to reverse the trial court's award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and fees were awarded to the administrator on appeal in connection with the contempt proceedings.

 

1899 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Det. of Bergen


No. 49587-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1213



June 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Bergen, 121 Wn. App. 1078, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1968 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 01-2-04135-3. Date filed: 11/02/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Richard J Thorpe.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the State's petition, a jury determined that appellant prisoner: (1) had been convicted of a crime of sexual violence; (2) suffered from a mental abnormality or personality disorder; and (3) the mental abnormality or personality disorder made him likely to engage in predatory acts of sexual violence. The Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, then ordered the prisoner's commitment. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner argued that the trial court violated his right to due process when it declined to instruct the jury that the State had to prove he lacked volitional control over his behavior pursuant to Kansas v. Crane. However, the Washington Supreme Court had not read Crane as requiring a specific lack of control determination by the jury. Thus, the trial court properly declined to instruct separately on the volitional element. The prisoner was 74 years old. He contended that the actuarial instruments used by the expert in his case lacked proper foundation under Wash. R. Evid. 703, because they were not cross-validated on men 60 years or older. The appellate court noted that the assessment of such actuarial instruments went to the weight the jury would give such instruments and not their admissibility. The expert testified that he used four actuarial instruments to assess the prisoner's risk to re-offend. Even though the expert testified that he did not know whether the actuarial instruments had been cross-validated on men over age 60, the appellate court held their admission was not improper, where those actuarial instruments were generally accepted in the scientific community.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order for the prisoner's commitment.

 

1900 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nordlund


No. 30592-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1180



June 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 99-1-02886-6. Date filed: 06/13/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Bruce W Cohoe.
State v. Nordlund, 121 Wn. App. 1076, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1962 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of indecent liberties with forcible compulsion, unlawful imprisonment, and second-degree attempted rape. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, found that defendant was a persistent offender and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. He appealed, and the case was remanded. The trial court resentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. He appealed again.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.560 (2000) (now codified at Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.570). Defendant contended that the POAA violated the state and federal constitutions, because it did not require a jury determination of the fact of defendant's prior convictions. The Court of Appeals of Washington held that, where a prior conviction was used to increase a sentence, the fact of the prior conviction did not need not to be submitted to a jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant's sole point of error was rejected.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole was affirmed.

 

1901 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grisby


No. 50875-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1135



June 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court. Date filed: 11/03/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Joan E Dubuque.
State v. Grisby, 121 Wn. App. 1059, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3525 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a superior court (Washington), which resentenced him to 300 months for each of three counts together with 60-month firearm enhancements, all to run consecutively, on his convictions for five counts of first-degree murder and one count of first-degree assault. His previous sentence was overturned by a federal court on the ground that the sentencing scheme of former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.040 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the resentencing court abused its discretion in declining to revisit the original trial judge's determination that the sentences should run consecutively. He also claimed that the federal court mandate for resentencing did not have any language of limitation and that he was entitled to a full resentencing on every issue. In affirming, the court held that the resentencing court had the discretion not to revisit the consecutive sentence issue, because the issue was never a part of any of defendant's reviews or requests for collateral relief. The resentencing court was not required to consider issues never raised on appeal. The resentencing court applied the most current ranges under the Washington Sentencing Reform Act of 1981 to resentence defendant, and, under the law in effect at the time of his resentencing, the crimes for which he was convicted were not the same criminal conduct. The resentencing court was not required to apply pre-1986 law. The court concluded that the jury instructions and verdicts were sufficient to impose firearm enhancements and that the resentencing court did not err in imposing firearm enhancements and running them consecutively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the resentencing court's judgment.

 

1902 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Suleiman


No. 52557-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1147



June 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-00339-1. Date filed: 5/23/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Robert H Alsdorf.
State v. Suleiman, 121 Wn. App. 1067, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3554 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant of three counts of vehicular assault. Defendant appealed from the convictions and the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in imposing an exceptional sentence greater than the standard range. He contended that former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.390(2)(b) was unconstitutionally vague, and the Washington sentencing scheme violated due process. The appellate court noted that the part of the finding regarding the timing of the blood draw and the inference of a higher blood alcohol level (BAC) was erroneous, but the finding that defendant's BAC was one and one-half times the legal limit was supported by the evidence. The record supported the trial court's other findings. Basing the exceptional sentence on the victim's particular vulnerability was proper where the victim could not take evasive action. Defendant ignored her pleas to slow down and drove faster and more recklessly increasing her vulnerability. No constitutional right to sentencing guidelines existed. Defendant's vagueness challenge was not well taken. Finding aggravating factors neither increased the maximum sentence nor defined a separate offense. The trial court did not err in imposing the exceptional sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1903 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



City of Seattle v. Yes for Seattle


No. 53662-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


122 Wn. App. 382; 93 P.3d 176; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1151



June 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at City of Seattle v. Yes for Seattle, 121 Wn. App. 1070, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3566 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-2-28774-1. Date filed: 08/01/2003. Judge signing: Hon. James a Doerty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant group sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondents, the city and others, and struck an initiative entitled "Save Seattle Creeks Initiative" from the ballot.


OVERVIEW: The group submitted an initiative to the city and the city, along with the other respondents, filed an action to enjoin placement of the initiative on the ballot. The city moved for a declaratory judgment stating that the initiative exceeded the initiative power and the trial court granted the city's motion. The group sought direct review with the supreme court, which denied direct review and transferred the case to the court, which affirmed the decision. The trial court's review of the initiative was not premature because there would not have been time after the election for the trial court to review the initiative before it took effect. Under those circumstances, pre-election review, limited to whether the initiative was beyond the initiative power, was appropriate. Further, because citizens could not use the initiative process to enact development regulations under the Growth Management Act (GMA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.70A, the issue was whether the initiative was a GMA development regulation, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70A.030(7). The court concluded that because the initiative placed control on development and land use, the initiative, as a whole, was a development regulation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1904 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. DiLuzio


No. 22027-3-III, 22028-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


121 Wn. App. 822; 90 P.3d 1141; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1103



May 27, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SUPERIOR COURT, SPOKANE COUNTY. Date filed in Superior Court: 4/14/03 (22027-3-III); 4/22/03 (22028-1-III). Superior Court No: 02-1-02502-2 (22027-3-III); 02-1-03336-0 (22028-1-III). Superior Court Judge signing: JEROME J. LEVEQUE (22027-3-III); TARI S. EITZEN (22028-1-III).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant of possessing heroin, second degree theft, and making a false statement, Without the prosecutor's referral, defendant unsuccessfully petitioned for admission to drug court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in ruling that the prosecutor retained the power to decide whether a defendant should be referred to drug court. Defendant contended that the trial court's ruling that the prosecutor retained the power to decide drug court referrals violated the separation of powers doctrine. The appellate court found that while defendant met the eligibility requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 2.28.170(3)(b), the prosecutor denied referral to drug court on his possession and theft charges because the Department of Corrections had a hold on him and he did not demonstrate that he had a Spokane area residence; both justifiable reasons from the drug court manual. The drug statute did not create a "court" to which all state citizens had a right of access. Drug court referrals had been treated in Spokane County as part of the plea bargaining process. Plea bargaining was contractual in nature. The trial court did not engage in the plea bargain process, and was not bound by the parties' negotiations or agreements. Drug court was not analogous to deferred prosecution. The drug manual was used for guidance and was not officially adopted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1905 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Golden


No. 21339-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1104



May 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Judge signing: NEAL Q. RIELLY.
State v. Golden, 121 Wn. App. 1059, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3608 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington) convicted defendant of attempted second degree rape and unlawful imprisonment. Substitute counsel moved for a new trial, arguing a previous juvenile determination of incompetence raised a rebuttable presumption of incompetence that required a hearing before trial. The trial court found defendant competent to stand trial and sentencing and denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with and convicted of one count of attempted second degree rape (Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.050(1)(a)) and one count of unlawful imprisonment (Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.40.040). Defendant contended the trial court failed to comply with the competency statute, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 10.77, that there were errors in the court's jury instructions, and that that his trial counsel failed by not seeking an intoxication defense. The appellate court held that all proper competency procedures were followed, and there was no abuse of discretion. As defense counsel raised the issue of incompetence, defendant's argument that he was ineffective for failing to do so failed. Also, the competency commission's report supported the trial judge's determination of defendant's competence to assist counsel at sentencing. The appellate court also held that defendant's proposed instruction on fourth degree assault with sexual motivation was properly excluded. Finally, because the trial court's reasonable doubt instruction was judicially recognized as helpful to the jury and did not reduce the State's burden of proof, the instruction was not constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1906 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Superior Asphalt v. Labor & Indus.


No. 22166-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


121 Wn. App. 601; 89 P.3d 316; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 941



May 6, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Superior Asphalt & Concrete Co. v. Wash. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 153 Wn.2d 1005, 103 P.3d 1248, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 53 (Wash., Jan. 4, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a corporation and its subsidiary, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Yakima County (Washington), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, the Department of Labor and Industries (Department), in the corporation and subsidiary's declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Wash. Admin. Code § 296-155-305(2).


OVERVIEW: The corporation and subsidiary were contractors that performed road and highway construction all over the State. While working on a road project, the subsidiary was cited for violating Wash. Admin. Code § 296-155-305(2), the flagger safety regulation. The Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals determined that the Department could not prove that a violation had occurred and the corporation and subsidiary then filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against the Department, claiming that § 296-155-305(2) was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the Department, stating that the challenge was not yet ripe because the corporation had not been cited for a violation of § 296-155-305 and because the subsidiary had not requested that the reviewing court consider the facts surrounding the issuance of its citation, which had already been vacated. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the corporation lacked standing to challenge the regulation and that the facts surrounding the issuance of the original citation were not contested; thus, no justiciable controversy existed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1907 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Aase


No. 28584-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


121 Wn. App. 558; 89 P.3d 721; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 924



May 4, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress, the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, convicted him of possession of methamphetamine and sentenced him to 30 days in jail. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court should have suppressed the evidence, because police did not serve the search warrant at the "outset" of the search. The appellate court disagreed, finding that substantial evidence supported the finding that an officer provided a copy of the warrant to defendant only minutes into the search. Even assuming the officers "deliberately" violated Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 2.3(d), defendant did not argue that he was prejudiced by the several-minute delay or that the search would have somehow been less intrusive had he been able to immediately see the warrant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1908 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Parentage of L.B.


No. 52151-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


121 Wn. App. 460; 89 P.3d 271; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 833



May 3, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by, Motion denied by Carvin v. Britain (In re L.B.), 152 Wn.2d 1013, 101 P.3d 107, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 663 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Carvin v. Britain (In re L.B.), 155 Wn. 2d 679, 122 P.2d 161, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 861 (Wash., Nov. 3, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant woman challenged a decision of the Superior Court, King County (Washington), which dismissed her petition against respondent biological mother that sought to establish either (1) the woman's co-parentage of the mother's child under the Washington Uniform Parentage Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.26 (2002), or (2) the woman's right to visitation. The mother requested the court to adjudicate her husband as the child's biological father.


OVERVIEW: The woman sought to establish her co-parentage of or at least secure visitation to the mother's child, who was conceived by artificial insemination during the parties' 12-year intimate domestic relationship. The trial court dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed in part. The court agreed that the plain language of the Act did not give the woman a cause of action. While the previous Act might have provided a cause of action for a same sex unmarried individual to pursue parentage based on artificial insemination, the court concluded that the current Act clearly did not. However, the court held that a common law claim of de facto or psychological parentage existed in Washington. The court concluded that the woman had stated an action for recognition as a de facto or psychological parent under the common law, and the court reversed the trial court's decision to the contrary. The court further concluded that the action for visitation under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.10.160(3) was not barred by case law. The court refused to direct that the husband be declared the child's legal father. On remand, a guardian ad litem was to be appointed for the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that the woman had no cause of action under the Act. However, the court recognized a common law claim of de facto or psychological parentage existed in the state, and the court reversed the ruling to the contrary, as well as the ruling that the visitation claim was barred. The court declined to grant the mother's request to name her husband as the biological father. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1909 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hoisington


No. 20405-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FIVE


123 Wn. App. 138; 94 P.3d 318; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 823



April 29, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 13, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appellant inmate's scheduled release date from imprisonment for second degree rape, respondent State petitioned to commit him as a sexually violent predator (SVP). The Superior Court, Asotin County (Washington) found the inmate to be a SVP, and committed him to a special commitment center. The inmate then appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the inmate argued that recent Washington Supreme Court precedent mandated remand for consideration of less restrictive alternatives (LRAs). Further, he claimed that Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.030 was unconstitutional as it allowed the State to file a SVP petition shortly before his release, and that the State violated his right to substantive due process by delaying the filing of the petition and by denying him treatment during his imprisonment. The inmate also contended that there was a lack of sufficient evidence showing he was a risk to re-offend, and that the trial court erred in admitting certain evidence. In affirming, the court found that LRAs were not considered until the first annual review after commitment. Also, Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.030 did not violate due process and was not unconstitutional because it provided for filing of the SVP petition near the time of release. The inmate failed to show he was prejudiced by the filing of the petition as he was about to be released. Moreover, the evidence was sufficient to show defendant was likely to re-offend. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting a psychologist's expert testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1910 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hessler


No. 29424-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 808



April 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County Docket. No: 97-1-05066-1. Date filed: 09/06/2002. Judge signing: Hon. Marywave Van Deren.
State v. Hessler, 121 Wn. App. 1020, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 1525 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, denied defendant's motion to correct or modify his sentence, after defendant was convicted of robbery and assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(4) (1997), which the Department of Corrections (DOC) was relying on to deny him the right to earn early release credits, violated the single subject rule as applied to non-persistent offenders and, thus, was unconstitutional. The State argued that defendant's claim was time barred, because he did not make the motion to modify his sentence at the superior court until two years after the appellate court decided the original appeal. The appellate court noted that DOC's application of former § 9.94A.120(4) did not affect the validity of defendant's judgment and sentence. Therefore, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090 did not apply to bar defendant's appeal. Defendant claimed that his judgment was void under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b)(4); however, the appellate court found that he pointed to nothing in the judgment and sentence that was void or otherwise incorrect. The appellate court declined to sua sponte convert defendant's appeal to a personal restraint petition and substitute DOC as the proper party.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1911 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Martini v. State


No. 28894-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


121 Wn. App. 150; 89 P.3d 250; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 634



April 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at Martini v. State, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 138 (Wash., Feb. 1, 2005)
Review denied by Martini v. State, 153 Wn.2d 1023, 108 P.3d 133, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 207 (Wash., Mar. 3, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant corporation, and otherwise found in favor of defendants, State and contractor, in the driver's action for injuries sustained in a vehicle accident.


OVERVIEW: The driver sued defendants for injuries sustained when his car rear-ended the corporation's truck near a construction zone. The trial court found in favor of defendants, but the appellate court reversed, stating that a rational trier of fact could have found that the corporation's driver breached his duty of ordinary care. A jury could rationally have found that a reasonable person in the corporation's driver's shoes would have activated his four-way flashers while slowing, and that the corporation's driver was negligent when he did not do that. Thus, the trial court erred by granting the corporation's motion for summary judgment. To apply the principles of statutory construction was to give Wash. Rev. Code § 4.44.180(2) (2002) its plain meaning, and to give the statute its plain meaning was to conclude that the driver had the right to challenge a juror for cause. Under § 4.44.180(2), the employee of an adverse party, including the State, could be challenged for cause in a civil case. The evidence was sufficient to support a finding that the driver was following the corporation's driver, and the trial court did not err by giving the following-driver instruction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a trial involving all three defendants.

 

1912 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Fire Prot. Dist. v. Boundary Review Bd.


No. 49629-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


121 Wn. App. 73; 87 P.3d 1187; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 587



April 5, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part Snohomish County Fire Prot. Dist. No. 1 v. Wash. State Boundary Review Bd., 152 Wn.2d 1036, 103 P.3d 201, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 907 (2004)
Affirmed by Snohomish County Fire Prot. Dist. No. 1 v. Wash. State Boundary Review Bd., 155 Wn.2d 70, 117 P.3d 348, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 669 (Wash., Aug. 11, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Snohomish County Superior Court, Washington, affirmed the decision of appellee Washington State Boundary Review Board for Snohomish County (BRB) approving the annexation by appellee city of certain property. Appellant county fire protection district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district challenged the constitutionality of the property owner petition method of annexation and the timeliness of the city's notice to the BRB. The first step of annexation required a petition signed by owners of at least 10 percent of the assessed value of the property. If accepted, the next step was to circulate the annexation petition, which required the signatures of at least 75 percent of the owners. The appellate court found that this did not violate Wash. Const. art. I, § 12. Although the exact filing date of the 75 percent petition was unclear from the record, it was stamped "received" by the city on November 3, 1999, and was submitted to the county assessor on the same date. Even assuming a filing date of October 31, 1999, the notice of intention, which was filed 116 days later, was timely filed under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.93.090. Compliance with the 180-day filing deadline was a jurisdictional prerequisite. The district's argument that the petition did not comply with Wash. Rev. Code § 35.13.130 had to be raised before the BRB in order to be preserved for appeal because it was within the scope of the BRB's authority and was not jurisdictional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1913 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peters


No. 49282-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 331



March 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 00-1-10284-1. Date filed: 08/31/2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicted defendant of first-degree robbery for robbing a children's clothing store of $ 13 at knifepoint. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.570.


OVERVIEW: The court held that evidence of a prior crime was properly admitted under Wash. R. Evid. 404(b), because similarities in the prior crime were relevant to identity a common scheme or plan. The prior robbery took place within an hour and eight miles of the robbery for which defendant was convicted, and another robbery that was charged occurred four days later in the same general geographic area. All were committed with a knife and all of the victims gave similar descriptions. All three robberies were also relevant to a common scheme or plan of robbing small businesses unprotected by security, staffed by one or two female employees, towards the close of business day. The court also held that: (1) time that defendant was in custody was properly excluded from the speedy trial and arraignment calculation; (2) the State's late decision to use evidence of an uncharged robbery did not constitute mismanagement requiring dismissal; (3) a ruling denying defendant's Batson challenge was proper as to jurors who refused to state that they would convict a person based on the testimony of only one eyewitness; and (4) the life sentence was supported under the POAA and was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1914 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Weiss v. Thompson


No. 53018-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


120 Wn. App. 402; 85 P.3d 944; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 333



March 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Weiss v. Thompson, 152 Wn.2d 1033, 103 P.3d 202, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 917 (Wash., Nov. 30, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was detained for 15 days at the county jail before receiving treatment, for lack of bed space at a mental health facility (the hospital). The patient petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. The Superior Court King County (Washington) denied his petition because he had not yet pursued an appeal in his criminal case. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with criminal trespass. He was found incompetent to stand trial and ordered placed for mental competency restoration treatment at the hospital. Because the hospital lacked bed space, he was not transported from the jail to the hospital until 15 days after treatment was ordered. Defense counsel's motion to dismiss for failure to comply with Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.090(1)(d)(i)(C) was denied. Defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking immediate release and dismissal of the charges was denied. Fourteen days after he was admitted to the hospital he was returned to jail. He renewed his motion to dismiss the criminal charges for violation of § 10.77.090(1)(d)(i)(C). It was again denied. He was convicted. The issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred in denying his application for a writ of habeas corpus. Because defendant's detention at the hospital did not exceed 14 days, there was no violation of § 10.77.090(1)(d)(i)(C). Time spent in jail waiting for open bed space did not qualify as placement in a secure mental health facility. Defendant's detention was not unconstitutional and he was not entitled to habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the petition, although on alternate grounds than relied upon by the trial court.

 

1915 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dukes


No. 51180-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 280



March 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No:00-1-08533-4. Date filed: 09/27/2002.
State v. Dukes, 120 Wn. App. 1028, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 900 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of second-degree robbery. The Superior Court of King Count, Washington, sentenced him as a persistent offender based upon a 1994 Washington conviction and a 1992 California conviction. He appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a fast food restaurant, told the clerk that he had a gun, and stole approximately $ 150. He confessed to the crime. The maximum sentence for second-degree robbery was 10 years, but the trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.555 et seq. The trial court based the sentence on two of defendant's previous convictions: a 1992 no contest plea to second-degree robbery in California and a 1994 guilty plea to first-degree attempted assault in Pierce County, Washington. The appellate court reviewed his sentencing and upheld the use of defendant's prior Washington conviction as a sentencing consideration. However, because the relevant California and Washington statutes differed, the appellate court remanded to allow the trial court to determine whether defendant's California conduct constituted a "most serious offense" in Washington.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but his sentence was reversed, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1916 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Appel v. Norton (In re C.A.M.A.)


No. 51001-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


120 Wn. App. 199; 84 P.3d 1253; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 230



February 17, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Parentage of Appel, 152 Wn.2d 1002, 101 P.3d 865, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 587 (2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Parentage of C.A.M.A. v. Appel, 154 Wn.2d 52, 109 P.3d 405, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 356 (Wash., Apr. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
In re Parentage of C.A.M.A., 103 Wn. App. 1032, 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2736 (2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother petitioned for visitation before the Superior Court County of Snohomish, Washington. Respondent father moved to dismiss the petition. The trial court specifically found that the child's parents were not unfit and that under these facts there was no basis to grant visitation to the grandparents. The trial court granted the father's motion to dismiss the petition. The grandmother sought review.


OVERVIEW: The child moved to Germany with her father, where she lived for over two years. She was cared for by her paternal grandparents while her father worked. The father returned to the United States, but the child remained in Germany to live with her grandparents. When the child visited Washington to attend her father's wedding, the father filed a parentage action. Here, the grandmother functioned as the primary caregiver for five years and had a significant relationship with the child. In fact, the trial court order dismissing her custody action found her relationship with the child to be beneficial and significant. Thus, the state had an interest in providing a continuing relationship between a child's primary caregiver and the child. The appellate court held that Troxel did not invalidate Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.240, and that the statute was constitutional. But although the statute applied in this case, it was impossible for the appellate court to determine its specific application to the facts of this case.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded to allow the trial court to hear all facts relevant to visitation.

 

1917 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Young v. Pierce County


No. 29257-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


120 Wn. App. 175; 84 P.3d 927; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 239



February 17, 2004, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, purchasers, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent county and gave the county a reasonable period of time to conduct a wetland determination.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers appealed the county's ruling that applied wetland regulations to an "area" of their property and denied them an agricultural exemption. The superior court found no evidence of an actual Pierce County Code Title 18E violation by the purchasers, because the county had not yet verified the wetland areas. The superior court then gave the county a reasonable period of time to conduct a wetland determination, stating that it would vacate the cease and desist orders if the county did not act. On appeal, the court affirmed, stating that, based on the intent of Title 18E and the substantial weight given to an agency's interpretation of regulations within its area of expertise, the court could not say that the examiner made an erroneous interpretation of the law. Nor did the purchasers show that the word "area," as the ordinance used that word and as the hearing examiner applied it, was so vague as to have denied them fair warning that they could lose the agricultural exemption on a portion of their land if they allowed that portion to lie idle for five years.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1918 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Custody of Shields


No. 21741-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


120 Wn. App. 108; 84 P.3d 905; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 215



February 12, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at In re Custody Of Shields, 136 P.3d 117, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 816 (Wash., Nov. 3, 2004)
Review pending at In re Shields, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 637 (Wash., July 13, 2005)
Review granted by, En banc In re Custody of Shields, 155 Wn.2d 1007, 122 P.3d 728, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 734 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Custody of Shields, 157 Wn.2d 126, 136 P.3d 117, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 495 (Wash., June 8, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Lincoln County (Washington), which granted custody of the mother's child to his stepmother, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 26.10.100, after the child's father died. The trial court reinstated the mother's visitation rights under the parenting plan that was set up after the mother and father's divorce.


OVERVIEW: The child's parents divorced when he was three years old, and the child was placed with his father. The mother was granted liberal visitation rights. When the child was five years old, his mother moved to Oregon, and his father remarried. The father later adopted the stepmother's daughter, and the couple had a child of their own. The day after the father's funeral, when the child was 11 years old, the mother, accompanied by a sheriff's deputy, took the child from the stepmother's home. The court held that, where placing the child with an otherwise fit parent would be detrimental to the child, the parent's right to custody was outweighed by the state's interest in the child's welfare. The trial court's finding that the mother was not "unfit" did not deprive the stepmother of standing to bring the action. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by awarding custody of the child to the stepmother. The trial court's finding of detriment to the child if he was placed with his mother was supported by evidence of actual detriment, including the showing that the stepmother was the child's psychological parent and that the child was integrated into her family.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1919 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bulleri-Tilford


No. 29293-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 202



February 10, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 01-1-05604-4. Date filed: 08/09/2002.
State v. Bulleri-Tilford, 120 Wn. App. 1014, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 737 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) convicted defendant of three counts of first degree assault for steering the car his girlfriend was driving into oncoming traffic and injuring three people in the car that they struck. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued the trial court erred in (1) failing to give a unanimity instruction on alternative means of committing first degree assault; (2) allowing testimony about his past drug use; (3) failing to give an inferior degree instruction; (4) admitting prejudicial evidence; and (5) improperly commenting on the evidence. His failure to object to the testimony below regarding his drug use precluded him from raising it for the first time on appeal. The court admitted a letter he had written his girlfriend advising her how to testify at trial. It was relevant to her credibility and her possible motive to recant. The trial court did not impermissibly comment on the evidence. The trial court instructed the jury on alternative means of committing first and second degree assault. It did not, however, instruct the jury that it must be unanimous. The instruction was not necessary because the State presented sufficient evidence supporting each of the alternative means. Because there was no evidence that defendant acted merely negligently or recklessly, the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on the inferior degree offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1920 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morley


No. 21357-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 104



January 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 01-1-01587-8. Judge signing: RICHARD SCHROEDER. Date filed: August 15, 2002.
State v. Morley, 119 Wn. App. 1088, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 599 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree unlawful possession of a firearm in the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington. Defendant appealed, asserting that due process precluded prosecution for the offenses, because the sentencing court, in a 1995 underlying predicate conviction, failed to give him statutorily-required notice under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.047(1)(a) (1994), that he was ineligible to possess any firearm.


OVERVIEW: Upon his prison release in 1989, defendant was instructed that, under the version of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040 in effect at that time, that he could not possess "pistols or short firearms." The statute was expanded in 1994 to prohibit persons previously convicted of a serious offense from possessing "any firearm." Former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040 (1994). A notification requirement was also added pursuant to former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.047(1) (1994). In 1995, defendant pled guilty to second-degree burglary. It was undisputed that the sentencing court at that time did not comply with the notification requirement of former § 9.41.047(1). Then, in 2001, the State charged defendant with the instant crimes. On appeal, defendant asserted he was unaware of the 1994 change in the law and that he reasonably believed he could own or possess "rifles." However, the appellate court held defendant was on notice of the 1994 change in the law and that due process did not require any court to tell him that he had lost all firearm privileges. Defendant's reliance on State v. Leavitt was misplaced, because, in that case, a defendant was affirmatively misled about the firearm prohibition.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1921 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Chiawana, Inc. v. State


No. 21559-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 78



January 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Chiawana, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue, 119 Wn. App. 1085, 119 Wn. App. 1085, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 547 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: YAKIMA. Docket No(s): 01-2-01694-5. Judge signing: JAMES HUTTON. Date filed: October 11, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, State of Washington, Department of Revenue (department), sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Yakima County (Washington), which found in favor of respondents, taxpayers, reversed the decision of the Board of Tax Appeals (board), and held that it was in error to deny the taxpayers' applications for sales and use tax deferrals.


OVERVIEW: In 1998, the taxpayers applied for sales and use tax deferrals and business and occupation (B&O) tax credits for projects from 1994 through 1997. Finding the requests untimely, the department denied the applications. The department's appeals division and the board upheld the denials. The taxpayers sought judicial review and the superior court reversed the decision. The department appealed and one of the taxpayer's cross-appealed the denial of its request for credit for B&O taxes paid. The court reversed and reinstated the decision of the board. Because the taxpayers did not meet the statutory requirements, the department properly denied their requests for a refund for the overpayment of taxes; they were not entitled to the deferrals or credits, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 82.60.03, 82.62.020. Applications for deferrals and credits must have been met before the qualified project began. The court further stated that this was not the rare situation where the futility exception should have been applied and that the department's position that the taxpayers were not entitled to the tax benefits could not have been the basis for the claim of equitable estoppel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and reinstated the decision of the board.

 

1922 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



City of Olympia v. Drebick


No. 29018-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


119 Wn. App. 774; 83 P.3d 443; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 75



January 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Amending Opinion February 18, 2004.
Review granted by City of Olympia v. Drebick, 152 Wn.2d 1020, 101 P.3d 107, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 781 (2004)
Reversed by City of Olympia v. Drebick, 156 Wn.2d 289, 126 P.3d 802, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 112 (Wash., Jan. 19, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city imposed an impact fee on appellant permittee as a condition for issuance of a building permit. The permittee appealed the fee amount to the city's hearing examiner, which reversed as to whether the fee complied with Wash. Rev. Code § 82.02.050(3). On the city's appeal, the trial court reversed the hearing examiner. The permittee appealed to the Supreme Court of Washington, which transferred the case to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: Under Wash. Rev. Code § 82.02.050(3) of the Growth Management Act, 1990 Wash. Laws ch. 17, the city imposed an impact fee on the permittee to address the traffic impact of the permittee's new building, calculating the fee by averaging the cumulative traffic-related impacts of all new office buildings. The permittee paid the fee under protest and appealed. The court construed § 82.02.050(3) and held that it required impact fees to be reasonably related to the individualized impacts of the particular project. A review of the legislative history of the statute supported the court's interpretation, as did the wording of the statute. The use of "the" before "new development" in the statute indicated a particular new development, not all new development. The court further noted that such a construction assured the constitutionality of the statute, because the exaction of an impact fee had to be reasonably related to the public problem, increased traffic, that was expected to result from the new building. Therefore, § 82.02.050(3) capped the impact fee based on the impact of the permittee's particular project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court and remanded the case for the city to impose an impact fee using any of the methods provided by statute, provided that such fee was not to exceed the individualized impacts of the permittee's specific project.

 

1923 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Casper v. Esteb Enters.


No. 29078-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


119 Wn. App. 759; 82 P.3d 1223; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 70



January 21, 2004, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff home buyers filed suit against defendants, a building corporation, its principals, and its surety, alleging breach of contract and violation of the Consumer Protection Act. After a jury trial the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) entered judgment for the buyers on the contract claim and for defendants on the Act claim and dismissed the corporation's counterclaim. The corporation appealed, and the buyers cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before trial one of the principals gave deposition testimony on behalf of the corporation pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 30(b)(6). The principal did not prepare extensively for the deposition and failed to bring the requested documentation. The corporation subsequently failed to produce such documentation as ordered so the trial court bound the corporation to the deposition non-answers at trial on the issues raised by the documentation that was not produced. On appeal the court affirmed the discovery sanction. Based on the court's refusal to dismiss the counterclaims as requested by the buyers, its binding of the corporation to the deposition answers, and its comment that such was the best sanction for the corporation's failure to comply with the discovery requests, the court found that the trial court properly considered lesser sanctions. The trial court's comments that the principal's actions made discovery useless and its frustrations with his failure to comply with discovery orders showed that the trial court found the failure to comply was willful and that the buyers were substantially prejudiced by the failure. Therefore, the sanction was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1924 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barquet


No. 50068-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3081



December 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Barquet, 119 Wn. App. 1063, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3533 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-1-04544-6. Date filed: 01/29/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of delivery of cocaine in the Superior Court of King County, Washington. Defendant, a disabled person, appealed, challenging his standard range Washington Drug Offender Sentencing Alternative (DOSA) sentence as violative of the Americans With Disabilities Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq. Defendant also argued that his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment under Wash. Const. art. I, § 14.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was deaf, and did not speak, read, write, or even generally communicate by way of American Sign Language. Defendant pled guilty per a plea agreement. The trial court denied defendant's request for a sentence below the standard range, and sentenced defendant to a standard range DOSA sentence of 50.75 months of total confinement, and 50.75 months in community custody. The trial court also provided in its judgment and sentence that the department of corrections (DOC) would have to provide defendant with effective drug treatment, and interpretation and educational services. The appellate court noted that as a general rule, a defendant could not appeal a standard range sentence. Moreover, a DOSA sentence was always within the standard range because it was always based on the midpoint of the standard range. Secondly, defendant failed to demonstrate that the ADA applied in the context of his sentencing. If, in time, defendant believed the DOC violated the special conditions of his sentence, his remedy was to file a civil claim, file for an injunction, or file a personal restraint petition. Finally, defendant made no showing that his sentence was cruel and unusual.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1925 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


No. 48038-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3075



December 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Clark, 119 Wn. App. 1063, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3530 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-09431-6. Date filed: 05/19/2000.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) for second-degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted there was insufficient evidence for the State to prove he took money from bank tellers by the use or threatened use of immediate force, violence, or fear of injury, as he carried no weapon and made no verbal threats. The instant court, however, concluded that defendant's actions were sufficient to prove that he obtained property through use of or threatened use of immediate force, violence, or fear of injury. In both instances, defendant approached bank tellers and gave them a note communicating that he intended a robbery. One teller was alone, and defendant leaned over him, prevented him from pressing the alarm, motioned into his jacket, and asked for more money. The teller stated that he was fearful. With respect to the second incident, the note also informed the teller not to engage in any action that would draw attention to her and not to make a scene. The teller testified that she feared he would hurt someone. Further, defendant was not entitled to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of first-degree theft, as the evidence did not affirmatively establish defendant's theory that he did not threaten either teller. His remaining claims also failed.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

1926 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Evergreen Freedom Found. v. NEA


No. 29350-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


119 Wn. App. 445; 81 P.3d 911; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3055



December 23, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foundation challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which dismissed its citizen's action lawsuit against respondent education association that alleged violations of the Public Disclosure Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 42.17. The trial court found that dismissal was required under prior case law interpreting Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.400(4).


OVERVIEW: Proceeding under the Act, the foundation sent a notice to the attorney general and county prosecutors alleging that the association violated the Act. The attorney general referred the notice to a particular commission for a review and investigation. Later, the foundation sent another letter to the attorney general and county prosecutors stating that it intended to commence a citizen's action lawsuit in ten days if they did not initiate an action against the association. The trial court dismissed the action based on case law interpreting Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.400(4), which case appeared to hold that a referral from the attorney general's office tolled the ten-day deadline. On appeal, the court reversed. The court clarified its holding in State ex rel. Evergreen Freedom Found. v. Washington Educ. Ass'n, 111 Wash. App. 586 (2002), and held that it intended only to restate the statute's clear intent that the commencement of an action by an attorney general or county prosecutor within the proscribed time period precluded a citizen's action. The court did not intend to imply that the attorney general's customary referral for a review and investigation precluded a citizen's action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.
