Wash. Cedar & Supply Co. v. State


No. 29666-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3089; 20 OSHC (BNA) 1489



December 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.    [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Wash. Cedar & Supply Co. v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 119 Wn. App. 1062, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3527 (2003)
Opinion withdrawn by Wash. Cedar & Supply Co. v. State Dep't of Labor & Industries, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 97 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 28, 2004)
Substituted opinion at Wash. Cedar & Supply Co. v. State Dep't of Labor & Industries, 119 Wn. App. 906, 83 P.3d 1012, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 96 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which affirmed a decision by respondent state department of labor and industries (L&I) citing the business for failing to ensure that its employees were wearing fall restraints when they delivered materials onto the roof of a construction site.


OVERVIEW: The L&I cited the business for failing to ensure its employees' safety on a construction site. The L&I's board of appeals upheld the citation, the superior court affirmed that decision, and the business appealed. The business argued a partial panel of the board could not review the citation, the board improperly declined to apply the unpreventable employee misconduct defense under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.17.120(5), and the offense was improperly designated as a repeat serious violation. The court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 49.17.140 permitted partial panel review. The court also found that the unpreventable misconduct defense was inapplicable, because the business had been cited for prior similar misconduct and had not met the requirements under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.17.120(5)(iv) of effective enforcement of corrective procedures. Also, L&I made a prima facie showing of a repeat serious violation as required under Wash. Admin. Code § 296-155-24510. Finally, the court determined that there were no evidentiary errors by the board that required reversal of the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision affirming the citations against the business.

 

1928 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lincoln


No. 51525-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2992



December 22, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Lincoln, 119 Wn. App. 1055, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3500 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 99-1-00135-7. Date filed: 11/04/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington) denied defendant's Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 motion to vacate his plea of guilty to two counts of robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed two financial institutions. He was charged with one count of first-degree robbery while armed with a firearm and one count of second-degree robbery while armed with a firearm. He pled guilty to both counts. His total sentence was 140 months. The judgment and sentence informed defendant that any collateral attack would be subject to Wash. Rev. Code §§ 10.73.090 and 10.73.100. Defendant filed a pro se motion to vacate his judgment and sentence and withdraw his guilty plea pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 and Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 4.2. He acknowledged in his motion that it was not timely, but argued that it could be considered under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100(5) or (6) because the trial court either exceeded its jurisdiction in sentencing him or there had been a substantial change in the law. He also alleged that his attorney gave him erroneous advice that rendered his plea involuntary. The motion was denied. The State contended for the first time on appeal that the motion was time barred. The appellate court agreed with the State. Defendant's ineffective assistance claim was time barred at the outset by Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1929 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wright


No. 21285-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2935



December 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Wright, 119 Wn. App. 1052, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3486 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 01-1-00772-7. Judge signing: PAUL BASTINE. Date filed: June 27, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington), for first degree murder, first degree attempted murder, and first degree assault, all with the use of a firearm. Defendant asserted several errors including, inter alia, the trial court's admission of gang affiliation evidence, its excusal of a juror, and its denial of a manslaughter instruction. Finally, he challenged his sentence on double jeopardy grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed a child and injured one of seven other occupants when he fired into a home which housed a man who had recently robbed defendant in regard to a drug deal. The appellate court held gang evidence was admissible to prove ongoing gang rivalry between the victims and defendant and the fact that perceived disrespect was accepted as grounds for retaliatory murder. As a juror stopped showing up, and a doctor advised against his continuing, the circumstances justified his replacement. There was no basis for a manslaughter instruction as the actions could not be found to be reckless. Nothing in the record suggested a prosecutor's remark was flagrant and ill intentioned and the error was easily curable. There was sufficient evidence to support a finding that defendant was present at the scene. That was enough to establish premeditation. The trial court did not abuse its discretion refusing to dismiss the case based on a search of defendant's prison cell as the State's security concerns were acute. Absent a showing that the State would not likely have discovered a witness independently, the trial court correctly rejected the new trial motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Robtoy


No. 28338-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2890



December 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 79-1-00050-5. Date filed: 01/04/2002.
State v. Robtoy, 119 Wn. App. 1043, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3453 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to death for murder. Upon remand, the Kitsap County Superior Court, Washington, ordered that defendant's sentence run consecutive to a separate conviction for murder in a different county and recommended a minimum term of 600 months. The Washington Sentence Review Board set a 600 month minimum term. The trial court denied defendant's Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 motion and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After being convicted of murder and sentenced to death in the instant case, defendant pleaded guilty and was sentenced to life in a different murder case. The federal court of appeals ruled that defendant's life sentence without parole was unconstitutional; thus, in 1991, the trial court recommended a minimum sentence of 600 months, and also ordered that the sentence run consecutive to a sentence for a murder defendant had committed in the other county. In 1993, the sentencing board ordered that defendant's minimum sentence be 600 months. Defendant filed a Rule 7.8 motion in 2001 challenging the 1991 and the 1993 rulings. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling that the Rule 7.8 motion was untimely as defendant filed it many years after the challenged sentences and the exceptions in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100(3), (5) did not apply. Also, the trial court had power to set the minimum sentence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.95.011. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ordering that the sentences be served consecutively as under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.92.080(3), the sentences were to run consecutively unless specifically ordered to run concurrently.


OUTCOME: The consecutive sentences and the minimum term of the sentence imposed were affirmed.

 

1931 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hansen


No. 28544-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2894



December 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Hansen, 119 Wn. App. 1044, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3454 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Docket No: 01-1-00584-0. Date filed: 3/04/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington) entered judgment on a verdict that convicted defendant of stalking and found him not guilty of unlawful imprisonment. By special verdict, the jury found that defendant had violated a domestic violence protection order, thereby making his offense a class C felony under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.110(5). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46-110 for stalking his former girlfriend. On appeal the court rejected defendant's claim that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction. Defendant intentionally and repeatedly harassed his former girlfriend by contacting her numerous times after he learned of the restraining order she had obtained against him. The girlfriend stated that she was afraid of defendant, and defendant knew she did not want contact with him based on the restraining order and the girlfriend's statements to him to leave her alone. Such evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The court also found no abuse of discretion in the limited admission of opinion testimony about the cycle of domestic violence. After the State's witness was qualified as an expert on domestic violence and before the witness testified about the meaning of his wagon wheel on domestic violence or on whether the girlfriend was a victim of domestic violence, the trial court sustained defendant's objection because the witness had not been identified as an expert before trial. A limiting instruction to the jury sufficed to prevent any prejudice to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1932 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Henry


No. 51427-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2772



December 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Henry, 119 Wn. App. 1035, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3422 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-1-09282-7. Date filed: 11/04/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of a violation of the Uniformed Controlled Substances Act (Act), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 69.50 after he pled guilty to violating the Act. He was sentenced to 63 months.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed for the first time that the information to which he pleaded guilty lacked an essential element of the offense. He asserted that the information should have included an element related to his prior felony drug offenses. The existence of prior felony drug offenses led to a doubling of his maximum penalty, altering the standard range and thus changing his time of incarceration from 57 months to 63 months. The court affirmed however, stating that sentencing enhancements imposed by a court based on the fact of prior convictions were not unconstitutional. They did not pose a due process problem under the United States Constitution. Further, the federal constitution did not require that prior convictions be proved to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. In the face of that clear precedent, defendant's challenge failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1935 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Ettenhofer


No. 28545-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


119 Wn. App. 300; 79 P.3d 478; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2717



November 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 10, 2003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which, after denying a motion to suppress, convicted defendant of manufacture of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: An officer, after noticing an odor of marijuana coming from a building on defendant's property, contacted a judge by telephone to obtain a search warrant for defendant's property. The officer was placed under oath and gave a telephonic statement of grounds for the search. The judge found probable cause and authorized a search, but neither the judge nor the officer executed a written warrant. Marijuana was found growing inside the building. The trial court denied a suppression motion, reasoning that defendant failed to show actual prejudice resulting from the failure to prepare a written warrant as required by Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 2.3(c). The court reversed, holding that a telephonic procedure without the issuance of a written warrant violated defendant's rights under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7 and rendered the search warrantless. Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.040, which made warrantless searches unlawful, implemented both Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 2.3 and Wash. Const. art. I, § 7. The court noted that the procedure also violated Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 2.3(d), which contemplated a written, signed warrant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

State v. Avington


No. 21344-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2720



November 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Avington, 119 Wn. App. 1021, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3349 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: DOUGLAS. Docket No(s): 01-1-00123-3. Judge signing: JOHN HOTCHKISS. Date filed: July 15, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Douglas County (Washington) convicted defendant of first degree burglary and fourth degree assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim told the deputy she had been assaulted. The victim was hit in the face with a rock by the assailant and blacked out. Witnesses testified that defendant and the victim had prior incidents with each other and that he had accompanied the assailant to the house when the victim was assaulted. On appeal, defendant alleged that the trial court abused its discretion in admitting evidence that he threatened a witness because the evidence was inadmissible character evidence. However, because defendant's attempt to induce the witness to avoid testifying at the trial was analogous to concealing evidence, which was admissible as circumstantial evidence of guilty knowledge, the evidence was relevant and admissible. Additionally, the prejudicial effect of the evidence did not substantially outweigh its probative value. Because the trial court's jury instruction regarding a burglary inference was unconstitutional and the error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, the remedy was reversal of the burglary conviction. Finally, in the event of a future sentencing hearing, the appellate court instructed that defendant's juvenile offenses should not be counted in his offender score.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's assault conviction, but reversed defendant's conviction for burglary and remanded that cause of action for a new trial.

 

1937 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Osborne v. Osborne (In re Osborne)


No. 50956-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


119 Wn. App. 133; 79 P.3d 465; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2683



November 17, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother (with whom the child was living) appealed the judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which granted appellee mother's petition to relocate and modified a parenting plan.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother argued that the trial court erred by denying her a hearing and by overruling her objection to the relocation of the child. The court of appeals agreed. Rather than contravening the traditional presumption that a fit parent would act in the best interests of the child, Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.520 established a rebuttable presumption that the relocation of the child would be allowed. Thus, § 26.09.520 both incorporated and gave substantial weight to the traditional presumption that a fit parent would act in the best interests of her child. The burden of overcoming that presumption was on the objecting party, who could only prevail by demonstrating that the detrimental effect of the relocation upon the child outweighed the benefit of the change. Section 26.09.520 contained 11 specific factors for the trial court to consider at a hearing to determine whether relocation of the child would be permitted. Because the grandmother met the requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.540, the trial court should have held a hearing to determine whether or not the mother was permitted to remove the child over the grandmother's objection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Spiers


No. 28507-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


119 Wn. App. 85; 79 P.3d 30; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2669



November 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) of unlawful manufacturing of a controlled substance, eight counts of second degree unlawful firearm possession, unlawful possession of a short-barreled shotgun, and bail jumping. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a search of defendant's home, police found numerous weapons, drugs, and evidence of drug manufacturing. He was convicted of numerous charges. On appeal, the court reversed in part. The information charging defendant with bail jumping in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.170 informed defendant of the elements of the crime and the penalty. Thus, while the information arguably did not track the track the penalty portion of the statute, it was sufficient. The court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(b)(iv) unconstitutionally infringed on one's right to bear arms under Wash. Const. art. 1, § 24 by criminalizing firearm ownership for persons merely charged with a serious offense regardless of whether they had relinquished possession. Because the statute's prohibition against ownership was unconstitutional, the court reversed defendant's unlawful firearm possession convictions in which there was evidence of ownership.


OUTCOME: The court reversed three convictions for unlawful firearm possession and affirmed the bail-jumping conviction.

City of Tukwila v. Belec


No. 50322-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2608



November 10, 2003, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No:01-1-03699-4. Date filed: 03/19/2002.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, affirming his conviction of telephone harassment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a licensed private investigator and process server employed by a legal messenger service, was granted discretionary review of a superior court decision to affirm his municipal court conviction for telephone harassment under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230(2). Defendant argued his conviction violated his constitutional right to protected speech. In the alternative, defendant argued that the telephone harassment statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, his conviction should be reversed and remanded for adequate findings, and his lawyer was ineffective. The court of appeals held the municipal court did not use the correct legal standard to determine whether defendant had the requisite criminal intent; therefore, substantial evidence did not support his conviction for telephone harassment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was dismissed.

State v. Roberts


No. 20404-9-III CONSOLIDATED WITH 20736-6-III and 20811-7-111


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2584



November 6, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: GRANT. Docket No(s): 96-1-00223-5. Judge signing: EVAN SPERLINE. Date filed: July 31, 2001. Proceedings Originating in Court of Appeals: 12/26/01 and 1/31/02. Nature of Proceedings: PERSONAL RESTRAINT PETITIONS.
State v. Roberts, 119 Wn. App. 1003, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3276 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was prosecuted on 11 counts of sex-related crimes; 10 of the counts, which related to separate incidents involving two teenage girls, were reversed on appeal. On remand, the Grant County Superior Court, Washington, convicted defendant of third-degree child molestation, third-degree child rape, first-degree kidnapping, first-degree rape, and attempted second-degree rape, among others. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several issues on appeal. The appellate court found that the first-degree rape and the attempted second-degree rape convictions did not violate the prohibition against double jeopardy, as defendant's penetration of the victim's vagina with his penis was one unit of prosecution, and his attempt to contact her mouth with his penis was a separate unit of prosecution, independent of the other. Although the acts involved the same victim, were committed at the same place, and occurred only a few minutes apart, they were not continuous and uninterrupted, and defendant's pattern of conduct changed from one act to the next. Thus, the evidence supported the trial court's determination that the two acts did not encompass the same criminal conduct. As the evidence of defendant's prior crimes showed that at least three of the acts occurred in different places, the trial court did not abuse its discretion during sentencing by failing to find that the prior crimes encompassed the same criminal conduct. As defendant opened the door for the State to articulate a doctor's opinion that the victim had been sexually assaulted, defendant waived any objection to the opinion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1941 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Schuchman v. Hoehn


No. 21060-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


119 Wn. App. 61; 79 P.3d 6; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2586



November 6, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the department of labor and industries determined that appellant minor worker was a covered employee, appellant mother of the worker sued defendants, the husband and wife employers and their company, for damages. The Superior Court of Okanogan County, Washington, granted the employers' motion for summary judgment dismissal on the basis of employer immunity. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought suit against the employers for damages allegedly caused by knowing failure to use due care, failure to supervise her daughter, and knowingly allowing her daughter to operate dangerous machinery with certainty of injury. The trial court dismissed, finding that the daughter was limited to recovery under workers' compensation and did not meet the requirements for the "deliberate intent" exception of Wash. Rev. Code § 51.24.020. On review, the mother contended § 51.24.020 was unconstitutional as applied to injured minor workers. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the statute satisfied all three prongs of the rational relationship test. Summary judgment in the employers' favor was proper, as they presented evidence that they had a license to employ children as ice baggers, their machine containing the ice auger exhibited numerous warning signs, and nothing in the record indicated that the machine had injured anyone else. Nothing in the record supported the mother's allegation that the employers knew the daughter was certain to injure herself.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1942 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Niemann v. Vaughn Cmty. Church


No. 29049-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


118 Wn. App. 824; 77 P.3d 1208; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2371



October 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by Niemann v. Vaughn Cmty. Church, 151 Wn.2d 1031, 95 P.3d 351, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 499 (2004)
Affirmed by Niemann v. Vaughn Cmty. Church, 154 Wn.2d 365, 113 P.3d 463, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 530 (Wash., June 9, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When plaintiff citizen sought to enforce a trust's language prohibiting the sale of property, the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) ruled that the language in the deed that respondent, a non-profit corporation, was to hold the property in question for the perpetual use of certain churches was an unreasonable and discriminatory restraint on alienation and void under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.60.224. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The non-profit owned the property on which its church building sat and wanted to sell the property and build new facilities. The trial court found that the non-profit held the property in a charitable trust in accordance with the deed. The non-profit was the trust's primary beneficiary but not the only one. The deed containing the language at issue was a written instrument, related to real property, and seemed to filter sales by creed. Wash. Rev. Code § 49.60.224 passed constitutional muster as not being a burden on freedom of religion. The non-profit persuasively concluded that the deed language forbade sale to many different people, even many who fell within the classes protected by Wash. Rev. Code § 49.60.224; therefore, the statute applied and mandated that the restrictive deed language be void. The trial court did not err in making its conclusions regarding the application of Wash. Rev. Code § 49.60.224 to the charitable trust and that the non-profit could sell the property to any person or entity without regard to the restrictions in the deed. The trial court's findings supported the intent of the trust and the application of cy pres and equitable deviation doctrines.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Sanford v. Clallam County


No. 29656-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2342



October 14, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended November 18, 2003.
Reported at Sanford v. Clallam County, 118 Wn. App. 1071, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2988 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No:00-2-00794-1. Date filed: 06/12/2002.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Clallam County (Washington), which granted respondent county's motion for summary judgment in an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40.020. The owners also challenged the denial of their petition under the Washington Land Use Petition Act (LUPA), Wash. Rev. Code 36.70C.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought final plat application for a subdivision. They were required to meet certain conditions before getting final approval. Instead, they chose to submit a bond. However, the bond was never forwarded to the proper authorities. The owners were not given notice of the hearing on their application. After the application was denied, the owners filed a petition to set the decision aside under LUPA. They also filed claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40.020. After the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the county, the owners sought review. On appeal, the court determined that summary judgment was improper. The owners were entitled to actual notice of the hearing. Published notice of the hearing was inadequate because the evidence showed that the county had the owners' address. Therefore, the owners' due process rights had been violated. Further, the plat application had not expired. Former Clallam County, Wash., Code § 29.19.300 (1996) improperly conflicted with Wash. Rev. Code § 58.17.140, which gave the owners five years from the date of the preliminary plat approval.


OUTCOME: The court determined that summary judgment was improperly granted. The case was remanded with directions to rehear the owners' final plat application. The trial court was also ordered to determine whether the owners were entitled to any relief on their statutory claims.

State v. Owens


No. 29002-2-II, No. 29192-4-II (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2248



September 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County Docket. No: 98-1-04060-4. Date filed: 05/24/2002.
State v. Owens, 118 Wn. App. 1056, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2855 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, denying his motion for attorney fees and vacating the order of restitution.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was convicted of burglary and assault, and ordered to pay restitution. On appeal, the claimant's conviction was reversed and the restitution order was vacated. The claimant moved in the trial court for an award of attorney fees. The trial court denied the motion, vacated the restitution order, and ordered the clerk's office to refund the restitution the claimant had already paid. Later, when it learned that the clerk's office no longer had the claimant's money, the trial court modified the order by deleting the refund order. The appellate court ruled that the trial court had no grounds to award the claimant attorney fees and did not err in denying them. The claimant prevailed because of a procedural defect in the State's case, not because a jury found that he acted in self-defense, and the one-day delay in bringing the case to trial did not demonstrate frivolous or malicious action; there simply were no courtrooms available. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in vacating the restitution order and allowing the claimant to seek reimbursement from the county risk management office.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Farhood v. Asher


No. 28811-7-II Consolidated with: No. 29408-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2116



September 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 01-2-03179-5. Date filed: 04/12/2002.
Farhood v. Asher, 118 Wn. App. 1050, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2830 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchaser sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which confirmed the sale of property in a wrongful death suit brought by respondent judgment creditor against respondent judgment debtor, who sold the property to the purchaser. The purchaser also appealed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the creditor in the purchaser's action to quiet title.


OVERVIEW: In a wrongful death action, the creditor attached the debtor's property by an ex parte process based on an allegation of injuries arising from felonious conduct. After the debtor was acquitted, the purchaser sought to intervene in the wrongful death suit and, after being denied, instituted a quiet title action to remove the attachment. Meanwhile, the creditor received a judgment from the wrongful death suit and forced a sale of the property. The court held that the purchaser had standing because he suffered harm in the violation of his right to due process in the ex parte proceeding and he stood in the shoes of the debtor. Moreover, as a third party, the purchaser could bring an outside action to challenge an attachment because he did not have an opportunity in the tort suit. The ex parte attachment procedure of Wash. Rev. Code § 6.25.070(2) violated due process. The property owner had significant interest in keeping clear title; there was a relatively high risk of an erroneous decision based on an unrebutted, low burden; the claimant's prejudgment interest in the property was minimal (without showing exigent circumstances); and the government's interest could not be any greater.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ex parte attachment and remanded to quiet title to the property, free and clear of the creditor's interest.

 

1946 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pink


No. 25327-5-II (consolidated with No. 27573-2-II)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2128



September 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Pink, 118 Wn. App. 1049, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2828 (2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Superior Court Docket No. 99-1-00060-1. Superior Court Judge Signing: David Foscue.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree assault while armed with a deadly weapon and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: The victim noticed a beer bottle on top of a box and a shopping bag containing smashed beer cans between his truck and his boat. When he picked up the box, it exploded. Defendant was subsequently convicted and sentenced for first-degree assault while armed with a deadly weapon and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder with a deadly weapon, and the court affirmed. The court stated that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained from his car, as the officers' reasonable belief that the car's contents posed a danger to the public, in addition to the vehicle's potential mobility, met the exigent circumstances factors. Further, defendant was not entitled to assert a marital privilege, because defendant and his alleged wife married each other while she was married to another. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of second-degree assault, because the evidence did not establish that defendant committed only second-degree assault. The exceptional sentence was vacated because it was improper under the Blakely analysis.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, the exceptional sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1947 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Howell


No. 51006-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


119 Wn. App. 644; 79 P.3d 451; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2097



September 22, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish and Changing Opinion November 14, 2003.
Reported at State v. Howell, 118 Wn. App. 1047, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2819 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of unlawful possession of a firearm in the first degree in the Superior Court of King County, Washington. He appealed, arguing, among other things, a violation of his speedy trial rights, that the jury instruction on constructive possession was erroneous, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Two days before a second speedy-trial expiration date, the trial court granted a four-day continuance to allow the state crime lab to test-fire the gun. Defendant cited a case under which foreseeable administrative congestion was an insufficient basis for a continuance. The court found that rule inapplicable, however, because the lab's congestion was caused by an unusual circumstance that required extraordinary resources. There was no problem the State could be induced to remedy, and defendant's speedy trial right was not violated. The court also held that defendant was not entitled to a constructive possession instruction requiring that dominion and control could be immediately exercised. That instruction applied to sentence enhancement, but was not accurate for unlawful possession of a firearm under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a). The failure to object to a detective's testimony was not ineffective assistance of counsel because the failure to object could have been sound trial strategy. The defense that the police were biased was arguably strengthened by the testimony that the detective would have referred the case to the prosecutor even in the face of exculpatory evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1948 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. D.R.


NO. 50789-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2111



September 22, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. D.R., 118 Wn. App. 1046, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2815 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court. Date filed: 06/28/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile was convicted in the Superior Court (Washington) of criminal trespass in the second degree. Appellant challenged his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his friends were involved in an altercation at a mall with another group. A police officer requested the groups to either shop or move along. Appellant began using profane language against the officer. Ultimately the officer escorted appellant to the mall's north entrance and told him he was prohibited from returning to the mall for the rest of the day. The officer informed appellant that he would be arrested if he returned. Shortly thereafter, the officer saw appellant approaching the mall's south entrance. Appellant was arrested, charged, and convicted of criminal trespass. The court affirmed on appeal. The evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction. There was sufficient evidence, under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.08.010(1)(b)(I), 9A.52.010(3), to show that appellant knowingly remained on mall property. The court rejected appellant's public premises defense under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.090(2) and his claim that the mall's policy unlawfully restricted his access to mall property based on his profane speech. Appellant's use of vulgar language lacked constitutional protection, and this served as a proper basis to deny appellant mall access.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1949 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gaff


No. 47279-8-I (Consolidated with No. 47778-1-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2056



September 15, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County Docket No: 94-2-07248-8. Date filed: 08/18/2000.
In re Det. of Gaff, 118 Wn. App. 1035, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2561 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was committed as a sexually violent predator. Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) that he remain in custody at the special commitment center (SCC) based on an adverse jury verdict following an evidentiary hearing on his petition for conditional release.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion for judgment as a matter of law. The court of appeals disagreed. The State introduced evidence, through an expert witness, that defendant suffered from a mental abnormality, including five paraphilias: rape, sexual sadism, exhibitionism, voyeurism, and telephone scatalogia. He also had antisocial personality disorder traits. The expert testified that past behavior was the single best predictor of future sexual behavior. Defendant had admitted to at least eight rapes, and several attempted rapes. Despite treatment for alcohol and drug abuse, defendant used marijuana six to 10 times in 1997 and 1998, even though he was confined in the SCC at that time. Another risk factor for defendant was rejection by the community. If defendant was unable to find work, that would be another risk factor. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1950 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Heesan Corp. v. City of Lakewood


No. 28171-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


118 Wn. App. 341; 75 P.3d 1003; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1940



September 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Heesan Corp. v. City of Lakewood, 151 Wn.2d 1029, 94 P.3d 960, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 382 (Wash., June 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 00-2-08546-5. Date filed: 11/29/2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which awarded summary judgment to appellee city and upheld an order revoking the corporation's adult cabaret license on the ground that a club it operated was a public nuisance.


OVERVIEW: The corporation owned an adult cabaret club that featured erotic dancing and a variety of private booths. A county sheriff's department conducted numerous undercover investigations at the club. During their investigations, the officers saw dancers engage in various types of sexual conduct in exchange for money, perform at a distance of fewer than four feet from the audience, and make improper physical contact with customers. The city gave the corporation notice of its intent to revoke its business and adult cabaret license and to declare the club a public nuisance. The trial court upheld the revocation of the license on the ground that it was a public nuisance. On appeal, the court found that the city's restrictions were not a prior restraint triggering greater state constitutional protection. Revoking the club's license was not an impermissible public restraint. The court further found that the city's adult cabaret code provisions, read as a whole, did not sweep any protected expressions within their prohibitions. They were not overbroad or vague. Finally, the court determined that state law did not preempt the city's adult cabaret code provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1951 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Vine St. Commer. P'ship v. City of Marysville


No. 50009-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1893



September 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 95-2-07655-4. Date filed: 02/08/2002.
Vine St. Commer. P'ship v. City of Marysville, 118 Wn. App. 1027, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2526 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought judicial review of a order entered by the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) granting respondent property owners' motion for summary judgment on liability and dismissing the city's affirmative defenses of the business judgment rule, discretionary governmental immunity, and that the property owners' claims under Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 were barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court rejected the city's claim that the property owners were required to personally serve the amended complaint since it stated a new and different cause of action. The property owners' original complaint was for a writ of mandamus. The amended complaint made claims for damages. The trial court ruled that the damage claims in the amended complaint were based on the same set of facts set forth in the original mandamus action and that personal service was not required. Since the trial court had jurisdiction, the property owners' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim was not barred by the three year statute of limitations. However, the property owners' claim for damages under Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40 was barred because the amended complaint was filed more than 30 days after they had exhausted their administrative remedies. The 30-day period in Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40.030 had to be strictly complied with. The fact that the amended complaint related back to the original complaint did not save the § 64.40 claim since the property owners had not exhausted their administrative remedies when the original complaint was filed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed in all respects, except the appellate court reversed the denial of summary judgment on the property owners' state law claim and common law breach of contract claim. The appellate court adhered to its decision in the first appeal and remanded for a trial on damages.

 

1952 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Ziegenfuss


No. 51145-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


118 Wn. App. 110; 74 P.3d 1205; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1851



August 25, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Ziegenfuss, 151 Wn.2d 1016, 88 P.3d 965, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 277 (Wash., Apr. 6, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine, and her sentence included a financial obligation. At sentencing, she sought a waiver of all legal financial obligations on grounds that she was disabled, had never been employed, and was unlikely ever to have the means to satisfy any such obligations. The Superior Court, King County, Washington, waived all obligations except the victim's penalty assessment, which was mandatory. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute and regulations governing violation hearings did not provide adequate procedural safeguards to ensure she would not be punished if she was unable to pay and that therefore her due process rights were violated. Because she had not yet failed to pay her legal financial obligations, nor been incarcerated or otherwise sanctioned for violating the terms of her community custody, the court held that her due process rights had not been violated and her argument was not yet ripe for review. The court nevertheless noted that, if the defendant was accused of violating the terms of her community custody, she would be entitled to the procedural due process safeguards due in parole revocation hearings and that the regulations governing community custody violation hearings appeared to meet these requirements. The court disagreed with the argument that a hearing officer could invoke sanctions without considering ability to pay, noting that imposition of sanctions without such an inquiry would violate due process and Wash. Const. art. I, § 17. The regulation permitted a hearing officer to elicit any facts necessary and was consistent with due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1953 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hills


No. 50428-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1806



August 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-1-09360-2. Date filed: 05/03/2002.
State v. Hills, 118 Wn. App. 1011, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2433 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicting him of promotion of prostitution in the second degree after offering two female undercover police officers protection and logistical support for half of their prostitution profits.


OVERVIEW: The two female officers were posing as prostitutes as part of an undercover operation for the police department. According to the two female officers, they had a lengthy discussion with defendant during which he allegedly offered to find them customers, provide them with clothing, and other logistical aide in exchange for a 50-50 split of the profits. Defendant argued that the statutes prohibiting the promotion of prostitution were overbroad, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.88.080 and 9A.88.060. The appellate court ruled that defendant's argument was without merit, as the statutes could only be overbroad if they swept within their grasp constitutionally protected speech, and the Washington Supreme Court had previously held that the promotion of prostitution statutes did not prohibit any constitutionally protected speech. Furthermore, a rational trier of fact could have found that the testimony of the two female officers was sufficient evidence to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1954 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Luby v. DaSilva (In re Brown)


No. 50681-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


118 Wn. App. 71; 74 P.3d 674; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1823



August 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by Luby v. DaSilva (In re Brown), 151 Wn.2d 1025, 94 P.3d 959, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 425 (2004)
Affirmed by Luby v. Da Silva (In re Brown), 153 Wn.2d 646, 105 P.3d 991, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 185 (Wash., Feb. 10, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant paternal grandmother challenged a judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which granted custody of the child to respondent godmother as being in the best interests of the child.


OVERVIEW: The child lived with the paternal grandmother for six years until the grandmother was arrested for growing a large quantity of marijuana. The child was removed from the grandmother's home, and custody of the child was granted to the godmother. The grandmother appealed, arguing that, because she was the child's effective parent, the court was required to find actual detriment to the child before removing her from the grandmother's household. Although the child resided with the grandmother, she was not a parent under any statutory definition, so she was not afforded the presumption of parental fitness under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.10.030. Next, the grandmother claimed that, even under a best interest of the child standard, there was insufficient nonhearsay evidence to change the child's residential placement. However, the court properly determined placement based on the preponderance of the evidence. Continuing to reside with the grandmother was not in the child's best interest because the grandmother consistently used poor judgment when making decisions regarding the child by allowing boarders with untreated mental disorders and alcohol problems to reside in her home.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.

 

1955 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Personal Restraint Petition of Charles


No. 49570-4-I, consolidated with Nos. 49575-5-I, 49580-1-I, 49590-9-I, 49594-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1824



August 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Date first document (petition, etc) was filed in Court of Appeals: 11/27/2001.
In re Pers. Restraint of Charles, 118 Wn. App. 1010, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2430 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Petitions were dismissed for all petitioners except Ervin whose petition was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates were given an exceptional sentence above the standard range for their offense, but below the maximum sentence allowed by the legislature. The inmates filed writs of mandamus concerning the constitutionality of their exceptional sentences.


OVERVIEW: The inmates argued that their sentences violated due process and their right to a jury trial. The appellate court found that the imposition of an exceptional sentence by a judge based on facts not found by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt was constitutional. The inmates had no procedural due process rights to a standard range sentence, as their liberty interest was qualified. They could not assert that their procedural due process rights were violated by operation of the statute. The inmates had petitions that were time barred under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1), where none of the inmates contested any increase in the mandatory minimum of their sentencing ranges. All of the inmates, except one, filed their petitions more than one year after their direct appeals were mandated. No precedents existed for the claim that the exceptional sentence itself amounted to another crime, preventing the time bar of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100 from applying. There was no basis to equitably toll the time bar, where the inmates failed to produce evidence of bad faith, deception, or false assurances by the State or of lack of due diligence on the part of their appellate counsel.


OUTCOME: The inmates' petitions were dismissed as untimely, where they were not exempt from the statutory time bar; the one inmate with a timely petition was denied relief.

 

1956 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Smith


No. 49843-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


117 Wn. App. 846; 73 P.3d 386; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1683



July 28, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by In re Pers. Restraint of Smith, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2769 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 18, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and attempted robbery in the first degree, in the Superior Court of King County, Washington. Defendant filed a personal restraint petition, asserting his convictions should have been reversed and remanded for a new trial, because the accomplice liability instruction given to his jury was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Each of the victims testified that defendant initially had the gun, that defendant hit one of the four victims with a gun while at a gas station, got into the driver's seat of the victims' car, and pointed the gun at each of them while demanding their valuables. All of the victims testified that defendant drove to a lake where three of the victims were locked naked in the trunk of the car. Defendant's co-defendant then raped the fourth victim. The issue on appeal was that the accomplice liability instruction erroneously stated that a person was liable as an accomplice, if the person had knowledge that his actions would facilitate commission of "a" crime (as opposed to "the" crime). The appellate court held that defendant did not establish that the error had any actual substantial influence on the jury's verdict. The State presented overwhelming evidence that defendant was a principal in each of the crimes charged. While defendant testified at trial that he was merely present while the crimes took place, wearing, as he put it, "mental blinders," he effectively confessed to active participation in several phases of the ongoing kidnappings and robberies with which he was charged.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1957 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Oakley


No. 50782-6-I, NO. 50783-4-I (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


117 Wn. App. 730; 72 P.3d 1114; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1562



July 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Nault, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 154 (Wash., Mar. 2, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed writs of certiorari with the Superior Court, King County (Washington), which denied the writs and ruled in favor of defendants that the State was not granted the right to demand a jury trial over a defendant's objection.


OVERVIEW: The State demanded jury trials for each of the misdemeanor defendants involved in the action. The district court denied each demand because defendants waived their rights to a jury trial and elected instead to proceed with a bench trial. The State filed writs of certiorari with the superior court, which denied the writs, ruling that Washington statutes and court rules did not grant the State the right to demand a jury trial over a defendant's objection. The court reversed, stating that Washington statutes unambiguously required district courts to hold a jury trial when the State demanded one, Wash. Rev. Stat. §§ 3.66.010, 10.04.050. And those statutes were not unconstitutional because the Washington Constitution only guaranteed defendants a jury trial, not the right to demand a bench trial. The district court acted contrary to the procedures authorized by the State Legislature, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 10.04.050, 3.66.010. The superior court should have granted the State's writ and ordered jury trials for all three defendants. Accordingly, the court reversed, granted the writ, and remanded all cases for a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, granted the writs, and remanded each defendant's case for a jury trial.

 

1958 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Simmons


No. 28654-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


117 Wn. App. 682; 73 P.3d 380; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1511



July 15, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Simmons, 151 Wn.2d 1001, 87 P.3d 1184, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 132 (2004)
Affirmed by State v. Simmons, 152 Wn.2d 450, 98 P.3d 789, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 660 (Wash., Oct. 7, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with persistent prison misbehavior in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070. Defendant's motion to dismiss on grounds that the statute was unconstitutional was denied. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, found defendant guilty as charged. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant reasserted his contention that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070 was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that, although § 9.94.070 and Wash. Rev. Code § 72.09.130 did not require the department of corrections to follow the rulemaking procedures under the Washington Administrative Procedure Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.010 et seq., the department did so when it repromulgated its disciplinary code. Because of the presence of the procedural safeguards, defendant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating the Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070's unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, treating inmates who could not be motivated to obey internal prison rules by the possible loss of early release credit differently from inmates who had potential earned early release credits was justified. Because the latter faced the loss of credit if they committed infractions, they had an incentive to follow prison rules and were less in need of the additional motivation of felony criminal sanctions. Thus, § 9.94.070 was rationally related to maintaining prison discipline despite its inability to deter inmates serving mandatory life sentences from disobeying prison rules.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1959 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Daly v. Snyder


No. 50964-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


117 Wn. App. 602; 72 P.3d 780; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1408



July 14, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Snyder, 151 Wn.2d 1005, 87 P.3d 1184, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 141 (Wash., Mar. 2, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought to enforce a child support order against defendant father. A court commissioner found the father in contempt for failing to pay support arrearages and ordered him to report to jail unless he paid toward the arrearage. The father appealed, and the Superior Court, King County (Washington) found that absent a continuing obligation, incarceration was not available for enforcing payment of child support arrearages. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State unsuccessfully sought to enforce a child support order against the father before the child reached the age of majority. However, the contempt finding was entered after the child had entered the age of majority. The superior court held that incarceration was not an available remedy under the court's contempt powers to enforce the payment of child support arrearages because there was no current, ongoing support obligation. On appeal, the court disagreed. The court noted that U.S. Const. amend. XIII, § 1, and Wash. Const. art. I, § 17, prohibited incarceration for failure to pay a debt in actions at law in personam. However, the court held that the child support order was an equitable remedy in which the father was ordered to do an act: to pay child support. Because the child support order was an equitable remedy, the constitutional provisions did not bar incarceration as an enforcement tool. The court also noted that Wash. Rev. Code §§ 26.18.040 and 26.18.050(5) jurisdiction over the father was retained even though the child had reached the age of majority. Therefore, the court reversed the superior court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment and remanded the case.

 

1960 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arnett


No. 20814-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1380



July 8, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Arnett, 117 Wn. App. 1053, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2014 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 01-1-01215-1. Judge signing: KATHLEEN O'CONNOR. Date filed: January 10, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence reversed, and case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first-degree rape. The child victim blacked out during the attack and was uncertain whether penetration occurred. Thus, at trial, at the close of the evidence, the State amended the charge to attempted rape in the first degree. A jury in the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant on the latter offense. Defendant appealed, attacking the amended information, and his sentencing conditions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, in the case of rape, the definition of attempt included an essential element, intent, that the completed crime did not. He asserted that amending the information in the middle of the trial denied him notice of the intent element, in violation of due process. He contended that denied him the opportunity to present a voluntary intoxication diminished capacity defense to negate the essential element of intent. The appellate court agreed with the State that, because of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.61.003, making attempt a lesser-included offense of every crime, the information put defendant on notice that a jury could convict him of any lesser-included offense of first-degree rape, including attempted first-degree rape. Further, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.61.010, either the State or defendant could have requested a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of attempted rape under the original information. It could not be said that the trial court abused its discretion by allowing the amendment. However, the trial court imposed conditions of community custody not authorized by the Washington Sentencing Reform Act of 1981 (SRA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.94A.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. However, his sentence was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1961 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Chino


No. 21186-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


117 Wn. App. 531; 72 P.3d 256; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1391



July 8, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction and sentences by the Superior Court, Yakima County (Washington), of intimidating a witness and assault in violation of a protection order, following the denial of his motion for a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of two jury instructions. The appellate court held that the information differed from the instruction given on the intimidation of a witness. The information alleged that defendant attempted to induce the witness to not give truthful information, but this means of committing the crime was not in the jury instruction. The error was not harmless. The assault instruction was proper, as the first- and second-degree assault exception was not a necessary element for the purposes of a "to convict" instruction alleging assault in violation of a protective order.


OUTCOME: The intimidation of a witness conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Taylor


No. 28360-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1356



July 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Taylor, 117 Wn. App. 1046, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1992 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 01-1-04265-5. Date filed: 01/11/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted him of two counts of unlawful display of a weapon in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.270.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought treatment at a chiropractic clinic, but was refused treatment unless he paid in advance for the costs. He returned with a gun and asked again for treatment. When one of the employees refused, he lifted up his shirt and pulled a gun out of the top of his pants. He pointed the gun directly at her and another employee and put the gun on the counter, saying "850 deposit." Defendant was subsequently convicted of two counts of unlawful display of a weapon in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.270. On appeal he argued that he wanted to use the gun as collateral, that the gun's safety latch was on, that he did not point it at anyone, and that he did not mean to frighten anyone. The court affirmed the decision however, stating that his actual intent was not relevant under § 9.41.270. Further, defense counsel's decision to propose a lesser-included instruction with a legitimate tactical decision and as such could not be considered grounds for a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1963 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. PDC v. WEA


No. 28264-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


117 Wn. App. 625; 71 P.3d 244; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1225; 173 L.R.R.M. 2232



June 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State ex rel. Wash. State Pub. Disclosure Comm'n v. Wash. Educ. Ass'n, 150 Wn.2d 1032, 84 P.3d 1229, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 85 (2004)
Later proceeding at, Sub nomine at Davenport v. Wash. State Educ. Ass'n, 84 P.3d 1229, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 90 (Wash., 2004)
Affirmed by State ex rel. Wash. State Pub. Disclosure Comm'n v. Wash. Educ. Ass'n, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 260 (Wash., Mar. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
State ex rel. Evergreen Freedom Found. v. Wash. Educ. Ass'n, 111 Wn. App. 586, 49 P.3d 894, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 647 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Washington Education Association (WEA) sought review of the decision of the superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which found in favor of plaintiff State in the State's action alleging that the WEA had violated Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.760 by using non-union employees' agency fees to make political expenditures.


OVERVIEW: The State sued the WEA alleging that it had violated Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.760 by using non-union employees' (nonmembers) agency fees to make political expenditures without their affirmative authorization. The court reversed and held that § 42.17.760 was unconstitutional based on U.S. Supreme Court caselaw that mandated a balancing between members' and nonmembers' First Amendment free speech and association rights, and approved of a procedure that requires nonmembers to exercise their rights by objecting or "opting out." Thus, § 42.17.760 was unconstitutional because, by requiring an "opt in" procedure, it presumed that nonmembers objected to the use of their fees for political purposes. Section 42.17.760's affirmative authorization requirement unduly burdened unions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded to determine costs and attorney's fees.

1965 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Retired Pub. Emples. Council v. State


No. 29016-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1233



June 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No:98-2-02283-1. Date filed: 01/17/2002.
Retired Pub. Emples. Council v. State, 117 Wn. App. 1036, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1952 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1998, plaintiff retired state employees sued defendant Washington Department of Retirement Systems, alleging that the Department denied them the opportunity to elect to receive cost-of-living benefits under the old cost-of-living statute, which had been amended in 1995. The Thurston County Superior Court, Washington, dismissed the action, as it was filed more than three years after the 1995 statute became law. The retirees appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1995, the legislature repealed all existing cost-of-living adjustment statutes for certain retired employees and enacted a new law, which took effect in July 1995. The 1995 law allowed the Department to pay cost-of-living raises under the repealed statute. The retirees argued that the three-year statute of limitations did not start to run until they were harmed, sometime after 1996 when they first would have received more benefits under the old cost-of-living statute than the new one. They also contended that the discovery rule applied and that the limitations statute did not start to run until they learned, again after 1996, that the Department denied them the right to elect their cost-of-living benefits. The instant court held that the three-year statute of limitations started to run no later than July 1995. Thus, the retirees' claims were barred. All elements of the retirees' claims, including harm, existed at the time the new statute took effect in July 1995. Even if the discovery rule applied, it would not have delayed the running of the statute of limitations, because the retirees knew all the essential facts of their claims in 1995 when the statute took effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1966 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Edmonds Shopping Ctr. v. Edmonds


No. 50815-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


117 Wn. App. 344; 71 P.3d 233; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1224



June 23, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action, plaintiffs, a limited partnership, a restaurant, and the owners of the restaurant, appealed a summary judgment of the Snohomish County Superior Court, Washington, granted substantially in favor of defendant city concerning its adoption of an ordinance banning card rooms. The city cross-appealed the trial court's ruling that certain portions of the ordinance were invalid.


OVERVIEW: Section 1 of the ordinance prohibited the conduct or operation of social card games as commercial stimulants. Section 2 of the ordinance regulated existing social card games and provided that all such games had to cease operation five years after the enactment of the ordinance. The restaurant owners operated a restaurant, bar, and card room facility located in the city. The restaurant had a gambling permit from the Washington Gambling Commission. The owners argued, inter alia, that the ordinance conflicted with Wash. Const. art. XI, § 11, because it was not a reasonable exercise of the city's police power. The instant court concluded that § 1 was a proper exercise of the city's police power. The city's exercise of its police power divested the owners of the claimed vested right to operate a card room. The ordinance did not operate to take property in the constitutional sense, and there were no violations of substantive or procedural due process rights. However, state law preempted the entirety of § 2 because it regulated, rather than prohibited gambling outright. Any regulation pertaining to the scope of gambling activities was under the sole authority of the Gambling Commission.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the summary judgment order in part and reversed in part. The instant court affirmed the trial court's decision as to the first section of the ordinance, but it reversed the decision to the extent that it validated portions of the second section.
