State v. Rodriguez


No. 28109-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1165



June 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Rodriguez, 117 Wn. App. 1021, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3173 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 00-1-03534-1. Date filed: 11/26/2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted him of kidnapping, robbery, and assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant persuaded a real estate agent to come to his home. While she was there, he robbed and assaulted her before stealing her vehicle. After he was convicted of kidnapping, robbery, and assault, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that there was sufficient evidence presented to support the jury's finding of criminal intent, despite the fact that defendant was intoxicated at the time of the crime. There was direct and circumstantial evidence that defendant acted with specific intent. Defendant lured the victim to the home, turned up the volume on his stereo, and had rope, duct tape, and a bandana handy. Moreover, the evidence showed that defendant was mentally aware. The court determined that defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel. There was no reason to argue merger, as the doctrine did not apply to kidnapping and robbery. Finally, the court determined that the trial court was not required to submit defendant's prior offenses to a jury before using them to enhance his sentence. Prior offenses were specifically excluded from facts that required submission to a jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1968 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bradshaw


NO. 50610-2-I LINKED WITH: NO. 50611-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1142



June 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 00-1-01082-9. Date filed: 05/28/2002.
State v. Bradshaw, 117 Wn. App. 1019, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3165 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the judgment of the Whatcom County Superior Court (Washington) which convicted defendants, in separate trials, of possession of more than 40 grams of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the consolidated cases, defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to require the State to prove defendants knowingly possessed a controlled substance, and that the evidence was insufficient to prove actual or constructive possession. The appellate court rejected defendants' arguments. The court found that prior case law interpreting Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(d) held that knowledge or intent were not essential elements of unlawful possession of a controlled substance. Instead, "unwitting possession" was an affirmative defense that defendants must prove by a preponderance of the evidence. As for defendants' challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, both defendants were driving alone in vehicles where drugs were found, which established dominion and control of the "premises" sufficient to prove they constructively possessed drugs found inside.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1969 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Bennett v. State


No. 29173-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


117 Wn. App. 483; 70 P.3d 147; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1108



June 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals July 8, 2003.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Modifying Opinion July 8, 2003.
Review denied by Bennett v. State, 151 Wn.2d 1004, 87 P.3d 1185, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 157 (Wash., Mar. 2, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sued defendant State, contending that H.B. 3901 (Wash. 1997), which implemented congressional welfare reform provisions, violated the Washington Constitution's single subject and subject in title requirements. The Thurston County Superior Court, Washington, dismissed plaintiff's suit on summary judgment. The Washington Supreme Court denied plaintiff's petition for direct review and transferred his appeal to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: When the State took steps toward suspending plaintiff's driver's license for failure to pay child support, plaintiff filed this action. Plaintiff argued that the bill violated constitutional requirements that a bill contain only one subject and that its title express that subject. He contended that the bill included multiple subjects and that these subjects did not share a rational unity. The instant court noted that the bill, when read in its entirety, broadly encompassed the topic of implementing a specific piece of federal legislation dealing with public assistance. Thus, the bill had a general title. The provisions of the bill were germane to its title and to one another in that they all concerned implementing the federal legislation. Even if the instant court were to view the bill's title as restrictive, it was enforceable because its provisions were "fairly within" the subject of the title. The title's subject referred to the implementation of the legislation and each of the bill's provisions operated to accomplish that purpose. The bill did not violate the single subject requirement. The bill's title also sufficiently stated the single subject matter of the bill.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment dismissing plaintiff's cause of action.

State v. Lee


No. 27609-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1109



June 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Lee, 117 Wn. App. 1012, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 3136 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 00-1-00061-0. Date filed: 06/29/2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted him of second-degree murder, three counts of second-degree assault, and four counts of second-degree unlawful possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was at a party when he killed another person at the party and threatened several others. He was subsequently convicted of second-degree murder, three counts of second-degree assault, and four counts of second-degree unlawful possession of a firearm. The court affirmed, stating that his counsel was not deficient for failing to impeach the victim's niece with a prior inconsistent statement, as the statements were fully consistent and conveyed the same meaning. Further, counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a manslaughter instruction, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.070, because the only evidence indicating that the shots were unintentional was defendant's testimony. From that evidence alone, no rational jury could have determined that defendant was reckless or negligent. A motion for severance was not warranted in part because the trial court likely would have denied severance out of a proper concern for judicial economy. Defendant did not prove Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310(3)(e) unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt, and an aggressor instruction was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1971 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Born v. Thompson


No. 49384-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


117 Wn. App. 57; 69 P.3d 343; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 968



May 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by Born v. Thompson, 150 Wn.2d 1025, 82 P.3d 242, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 4 (2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by, Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Born v. Thompson, 154 Wn.2d 749, 117 P.3d 1098, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 660 (Wash., Aug. 4, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the Superior Court for King County, Washington, challenging his confinement for evaluation of his competency to stand trial on a misdemeanor charge. The trial court denied the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with threatening to punch a bus driver who asked defendant to leave the bus at a terminal. The trial court ordered a competency evaluation under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.060. Following the evaluation, defendant was committed for mental health treatment under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.090. Defendant argued that the commitment was improper because the State did not prove the need for civil commitment by clear cogent, and convincing evidence. The appellate court considered the case even though the civil commitment had ended and the charge had been dismissed, because the statutory scheme governing civil commitment was a matter of continuing and substantial public interest. The appellate court then held that the State had the burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that defendant had committed a violent act sufficient to justify a civil commitment under the statute. Defendant's actions in threatening the bus driver for no apparent reason was sufficient to show the commission of a violent act. The term "violent act" in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.010 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1972 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cunningham


No. 21189-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 967



May 15, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: GRANT. Docket No(s): 02-1-00139-7. Judge signing: EVAN SPERLINE. Date filed: May 14, 2002.
State v. Cunningham, 116 Wn. App. 1075, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1481 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court for Grant County (Washington) of possession of a firearm, maintaining a drug house, a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.402(a)(6), and use of drug paraphernalia, a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.412. He was sentenced to 10 months on each of the 2 felony counts, with the sentences to run concurrently, and a 90-day suspended sentence on the misdemeanor count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was sufficient evidence for a rational trier of fact to conclude that defendant unlawfully kept or maintained a dwelling for the purpose of storing controlled substances. Inter alia, defendant was renting the residence and no one else was living there, letters addressed to defendant were found, and he admitted that he owned three of the four vehicles parked there. However, the appellate court held that there was insufficient evidence to establish that he maintained the dwelling for the purpose of selling controlled substances. During their search of the dwelling and its surroundings, officers uncovered all of the items necessary to produce methamphetamine, the presence of methamphetamine and the 151 compound consistent with the production of methamphetamine, an electronic scale, and baggies. Officers detected the odor associated with manufacturing methamphetamine. In short, the evidence was sufficient to establish that drugs were kept and measured on the premises, but not that they were sold. Because the record contained insufficient evidence that defendant maintained the residence to sell drugs, the jury was not entitled to convict under that prong of the statute.


OUTCOME: The conviction for maintaining a drug house was reversed. The case was remanded for retrial on whether defendant maintained or kept the residence for illegal drug activity. The convictions for possession of a firearm and use of drug paraphernalia were affirmed.

 

1973 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Blunt


No. 27785-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


118 Wn. App. 1; 71 P.3d 657; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 960



May 13, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Lewis County. Docket No: 01-1-00144-7. Date filed: 08/23/2001.

Released for Publication June 24, 2003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Lewis County, Washington, convicted defendant of vehicular homicide upon defendant's guilty plea. Defendant appealed his enhanced sentence, which was based on prior driving while under the influence convictions.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the State did not present sufficient evidence for the trial court to conclude that he had the three prior driving under the influence (DUI) convictions used as enhancements. The appellate court disagreed, finding the State's evidence bore minimum indicia of reliability, which, especially in the absence of any challenge, proved defendant's three prior DUIs. Thus, the facts proven by the State were deemed acknowledged by defendant. As the purpose of defendant's sentencing hearing was to establish his prior convictions, not to make any factual determinations respecting the circumstances and details of the vehicular homicide, the trial court did not improperly infringe on defendant's right to remain silent by summarizing the evidence and noting defendant's failure to challenge it. Nor did Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.370(2) (recodified at Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.530(2)), the statute allowing the trial court to infer such acknowledgment, infringe on defendant's right to remain silent. Rather, it simply allowed unchallenged, minimally reliable evidence of prior convictions to preponderate toward proof of a prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1974 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Childs v. King County


No. 50272-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 923



May 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Childs v. King County, 116 Wn. App. 1067, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1449 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 00-2-16855-1. Date filed: 03/08/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual sued defendants, county, deputies and municipalities, for civil rights violations, conspiracy to violate civil rights, defamation, malicious prosecution, false arrest, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The county moved for summary judgment dismissing all defendants, and the Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted the motion. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the individual was being arrested, after assaulting two deputies, he was dragged out of his home in handcuffs because he refused to walk. The individual's naked lower body was exposed because his sweatpants came down. The individual subsequently was convicted of assaulting the deputies. The trial court granted the county's summary judgment motion on the grounds that the individual's claims were barred by the individual's conviction and the statute of limitations. The appellate court affirmed the grant of summary judgment. The appellate court held that the findings in the underlying criminal action that the police had not acted with excessive force barred the individual's civil rights claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and barred his claims for the tort of outrage. The individual's claims for false arrest, defamation and assault or excessive force were barred by the two year limitation in Wash. Rev. Code § 4.16.100(1) as the individual was arrested in April 1997 and did not file suit until June 2000.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cramm


No. 48438-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 929



May 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Cramm, 116 Wn. App. 1065, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1438 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 00-1-01051-1. Date filed: 04/23/2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.030(1)(b) and one count of second-degree unlawful possession of a firearm in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of two counts of first degree murder under circumstances manifesting an extreme indifference to human life in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.030(1)(b), and one count of second-degree unlawful possession of a firearm in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(b). He claimed that the murder by extreme indifference statute was unconstitutionally void as applied to him, but the court disagreed and affirmed. Defendant argued that the statute must have been found to be unconstitutionally vague as applied to him because it gave no guidance to one deciding whether to shoot, or if he had to let another shoot at him and others. Defendant claimed that he was subjectively unaware of the alleged aggravated recklessness of his acts, but the court stated that defendant's argument was one for the trier of fact. He ignored the fact that he was arguing specific defenses to specific charges and that it was an issue for the jury to resolve. Further, the amended information was not defective because it inferred that more than mere conduct was required; it inferred that there was a mental element as well.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1976 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Treatment of Mays


No. 50222-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


116 Wn. App. 864; 68 P.3d 1114; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 933



May 12, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual was involuntarily committed by the Superior Court of King County, Washington, for 60 days of alcoholism treatment under Wash Rev. Code § 70.96A.140(1) because he had been admitted to a detoxification facility at least twice in the preceding 12 months and was found to be in need of a more sustained treatment program. The individual appealed and challenged the constitutionality of § 70.96A.140(1).


OVERVIEW: The State committed the individual pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 70.96A.140(1) because the individual was either gravely disabled or had twice previously been admitted for detoxification during the past 12 months and was in need of a more sustained treatment program. The trial court ruled that the State had not proved that the individual was gravely disabled, but did order the individual to be committed for 60 days because twice previously been admitted for detoxification during the past 12 months and was in need of a more sustained treatment program. The individual argued that § 70.96A.140(1) was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The appellate court agreed with the individual and vacated the order of commitment. The appellate court held that § 70.96A.140(1) was (1) unconstitutionally overbroad as the statute was not narrowly drawn to ensure that only alcoholics with a substantial risk of serious injury in the near future were detained, and (2) unconstitutionally vague because the statute did not provide any guidance as when or why "a more sustained treatment program" was needed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order of commitment was vacated and the petition was dismissed.

 

1977 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Johnson


No. 43625-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


116 Wn. App. 851; 68 P.3d 290; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 935



May 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Johnson, 150 Wn.2d 1021, 81 P.3d 119, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 823 (Wash., Dec. 2, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence in the Superior Court of King County, Washington, for delivery and possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for delivery and possession of cocaine. Because the delivery of the cocaine occurred within 1,000 feet of a school bus stop, defendant was sentenced to a standard range sentence of 132 months, which included a mandatory 24 months for the school bus zone sentence enhancement. Defendant argued on appeal that the jury was improperly instructed as to accomplice liability, that the judge made improper comments to the jury, and the 24 month sentence enhancement under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435 was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. The appellate court held that (1) although the accomplice liability instruction was improper, it was a harmless error as it did not affect the outcome as the State did not argue that the accomplice liability for delivery could be based on defendant's possession; (2) the judge's response to the jury's inquiry was not improper was it was a correct statement of the law; and (3) § 69.50.435 was not unconstitutional as defendant could have learned the location of the school bus stop before his drug transaction.


OUTCOME: The conviction and the sentence imposed were affirmed.

 

1978 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Country Doctor Cmty. Clinic


No. 50408-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 946



May 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Johnson v. Country Doctor Cmty. Clinic, 116 Wn. App. 1069, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1455 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No:00-2-07567-7. Judgment or order under review. Date filed:08/15/2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient filed suit against respondents, doctor and clinic, after experiencing an allergic reaction to a prescription. The patient claimed that the doctor failed to notify her about the drug manufacturer's warnings, thereby failing to obtain the patient's informed consent to the treatment. The King County Superior Court (Washington) granted the doctor and clinic summary judgment. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the patient failed to produce expert testimony supporting her informed consent claim. On appeal, the patient argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 7.70.050(3)(d) was unconstitutional because the statute required the patient to prove the scope and breach of a duty to obtain informed consent by expert testimony. The patient contended that requiring her to present expert testimony to determine whether a patient had a right to receive a warning about the potential risks associated with taking a drug undermined her constitutional right to determine his or her own treatment. The appellate court rejected the argument. The statute did not govern the private relations between a doctor and patient, or the right of the patient to receive information about the known risks of medical procedures specifically. It merely addressed the necessary elements of proof in an action for damages. It was patient's failure to provide expert testimony, and not any constitutional infirmity of the statute, that required dismissal of her claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1979 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bady


No. 49529-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 719



May 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 00-1-05771-3. Date filed: 11/13/2001.
State v. Bady, 116 Wn. App. 1059, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1417 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed in part and vacated in part, remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Superior Court for King County, Washington, of attempted second degree murder and first degree assault. The trial court merged the convictions for sentencing purposes and sentenced defendant as a persistent offender to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told his former girlfriend he was going to kill her, burned her with a cigarette, and stuffed plastic bags down her throat until she passed out. The victim regained consciousness and defendant was about to resume the assault when the victim's 10 year old son interrupted. Both the victim and her son told police what happened, but recanted their statements at trial. Defendant was convicted despite the recantations. The appellate court held that letting the assault conviction stand violated double jeopardy. It was not enough to merge the offenses for sentencing purposes. As to defendant's other claims of error, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the attempted murder conviction. The prosecutor's reference to the testimony of the victim and her son was not a personal opinion and did not constitute prosecutorial misconduct. The victim's statements to police on the date of the incident were properly admitted under Wash. R. Evid. 803 as excited utterances. The Persistent Offender Accountability Act did not violate defendant's right to due process or trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The second degree assault conviction was vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1980 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Maddox


No. 27455-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


116 Wn. App. 796; 67 P.3d 1135; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 667



April 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals May 20, 2003.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Amending Opinion May 20, 2003.
Review pending at State v. Maddox, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 867 (Wash., Dec. 2, 2003)
Review granted by State v. Maddox, 150 Wn.2d 1031, 84 P.3d 1230, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 5 (2004)
Affirmed by State v. Maddox, 152 Wn.2d 499, 98 P.3d 1199, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 740 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Maddox, 2009 Wash. App. LEXIS 419 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 18, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress, the Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, convicted defendant of two counts of possessing a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the police unlawfully searched his home, as there was no probable cause to believe that methamphetamine would be found in his home, there was no probable cause to believe that evidence of methamphetamine dealing would be found in his home, and the warrant purported to authorize a search for books and records not related to methamphetamine dealing, and, thus, was "overbroad." Given both the informant's track record and independent corroboration by the police, the appellate court determined that the magistrate had discretion to credit the informant's assertions, to find that defendant probably had methamphetamine in his house, and to issue a warrant for the house. However, the appellate court agreed with defendant that the warrant was overbroad, as it authorized the police to search for items for which there was no probable cause. Nonetheless, in applying the severability doctrine, the appellate court determined that the warrant's overbreadth did not require suppression of the items admitted at trial. Although defendant said he was out of methamphetamine, the police were not required to return to the magistrate to redetermine probable cause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1981 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Powell


NO. 49838-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 699



April 28, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Powell, 116 Wn. App. 1049, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1269 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-1-02727-8 KNT. Date filed: 12/17/2001. Judge signing: Jay V. White. Date entered: August 23, 2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in par and, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court for King County (Washington), which convicted him of taking a motor vehicle without permission, harassment, third-degree assault, and second-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his girlfriend got into an argument regarding their relationship. Allegedly, defendant pushed the victim over a balcony, broke a picture frame over her head, and threatened to cut her throat with a piece of glass. He also forced her to ride in her car, which he had permission to use in the past. After defendant was convicted of various crimes, he filed an appeal. On review, the court reversed defendant's second-degree assault conviction. The court determined that defense counsel improperly requested a jury instruction that contained the words "to wit." Moreover, the failure to object prejudiced defendant, as it caused the trial court to impermissibly comment on the evidence. Moreover, it effectively removed an essential element of the crime from the jury's consideration. As a result, defendant received ineffective assistance of counsel. However, there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.070, as the evidence showed that defendant no longer had permission to use the victim's car. Defendant only had permission to use the car during the parties' relationship, which had just ended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for second-degree assault. The rest of the convictions were affirmed.

 

1982 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. E.A.J.


No. 49890-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


116 Wn. App. 777; 67 P.3d 518; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 638



April 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. E.A.J., 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1135 (Wash. Ct. App., June 9, 2003)
Review denied by State v. Jacobson, 150 Wn.2d 1028, 82 P.3d 243, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 21 (Wash., Jan. 7, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile pleaded guilty in the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, to first- degree rape of a child, second-degree assault, and unlawful imprisonment. The trial court ordered that the defendant be confined until his 21st birthday. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 14 years old, lured a 5 year old girl into a secluded place, choked her until she lost consciousness, and sexually assaulted her by sticking his finger into her vagina. Defendant and the State reached a plea agreement, which defendant alleged required the State to recommend that defendant be eligible for release when he was between 20 and 21. At the dispositional hearing, the State indicated it concurred with the probation report's recommendation that defendant be confined until age 21. Defendant argued on appeal that the State breached the plea agreement. The appellate court held that the agreement was ambiguous and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to conduct a hearing to determine the exact terms of the agreement and whether the State breached it or not. If the trial court determined that the agreement had been breached, defendant was to receive a new dispositional hearing in front of a different judge. If the agreement was not breached, the original sentence could be affirmed. The "unusually cruel" aggravator applied by the trial court was not unconstitutionally vague and was properly applied to defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to conduct a hearing to determine whether the State breached the terms of the plea agreement. The trial court was then to proceed as instructed by the appellate court and either order a new dispositional hearing or affirm the sentence imposed.

 

1983 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Woods v. Bailet


No. 50484-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


116 Wn. App. 658; 67 P.3d 511; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 641



April 21, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sued appellees, her doctors, for operating on her without her informed consent. The Superior Court for King County (Washington) granted the doctors' motion for summary judgment, finding that the patient failed to comply with former Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.010, which required plaintiffs suing local government entities to have first filed a claim with the entity's governing body. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first issue was whether the clinic that employed the doctors was a "local government entity" as defined by former § 4.96.010. The appellate court held that it was. The statute defined "local government entity" as including "quasi-municipal corporations," and the clinic fell squarely within the common-law definition of that term. As a quasi-municipal corporation, the clinic was a local government entity subject to the claim filing requirements of former § 4.96.010. Therefore, the patient was required to file a claim before suing sued the entity or its employees acting within the scope of their employment. The appellate court also held that the application of the claim-filing statute did not violate due process in the case at bar, as the patient was on inquiry notice of the clinic's status as a local government entity and the proper claim filing procedure. Finally, the appellate court concluded that statutory amendments requiring local government entities to have appointed agents to have received claims should not have been applied retroactively to the case at bar, because, to have done so, would not have furthered their remedial purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Burke


No. 50411-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 646



April 21, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Burke, 116 Wn. App. 1044, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1247 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No:01-1-07059-9. Date filed:05/06/2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, convicting him of one count of possession of methamphetamine and one count of criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from his entry into a home that was under a decontamination order as a suspected methamphetamine lab. A notice of a decontamination order was posted on the home prohibiting its use and occupancy. Defendant argued that his presence in the home did not furnish probable cause for the arrest. The appellate court ruled that, because the police informed defendant that the order meant he was not to be in the home, and they observed defendant in the basement, the police had probable cause to believe a misdemeanor was being committed in their presence. As there was probable cause to arrest defendant, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant also argued that there was insufficient evidence to conclude that he used or occupied the home in violation of the notice and order. To convict, the jury had to determine whether defendant knowingly entered or remained unlawfully in the home. There was evidence that a detective told defendant the order meant he had to stay out of the home and that defendant admitted he knew he was not supposed to be there.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1985 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Noble


No. 48423-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 651



April 21, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Noble, 116 Wn. App. 1043, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1242 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No:00-1-01381-3. Date filed:04/13/2001.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which convicted defendant of five counts of second-degree robbery and sentenced defendant to life in prison without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that his conviction should be reversed due to the trial court's failure to timely enter written findings of fact and conclusions of law. Defendant also claimed that the trial court erred in admitting a gun and defendant's statements about the gun and its use, because the evidence was improper as propensity evidence under Wash. R. Evid. 404(b). The appellate court rejected defendant's arguments. The court found that the trial court issued a clear and comprehensive oral opinion that permitted the appellate court to determine how or whether the dispositive factual issues were decided by the trial court. Although the findings and conclusions were entered after defendant's appellate brief was filed, those findings and conclusions mirrored the rulings of the trial court. The court found that the evidence of the gun and defendant's statements was admitted for a showing of intent and plan, not flight. Defendant's statements and the use of a gun indicated his approach or method used for bank robbery and was highly relevant. Therefore, it was more relevant than prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Furfaro v. City of Seattle


No. 43409-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 523



April 7, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Furfaro v. City of Seattle, 116 Wn. App. 1032, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1644 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No:96-2-02226-8. Date filed:02/10/1998.
Furfaro v. City of Seattle, 144 Wn.2d 363, 27 P.3d 1160, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 541 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington Supreme Court remanded the claim for equitable relief to the court for further proceedings. The action involved appellants, individuals and corporation, and respondent city and the violation of the city's standards of conduct ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The basic ruling on appeal was the trial court's judgment of dismissal entered after a jury verdict for the city. The dismissal encompassed the individuals' and corporation's claims for injunctive and declaratory relief under both the federal and state constitutions. The court previously reversed the judgment of dismissal and remanded for a new trial on the individuals' and corporation's claims for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court had held that the United States Constitution required police to obtain a warrant before arresting nude dancers for violation of the city's standards of conduct ordinance. The supreme court remanded the claim for equitable relief to the court and the court declined the invitation to make a substantive determination about the availability of equitable relief. It remained an open question whether the individuals and corporation were entitled to declaratory and injunctive relief under the state constitution, independently of what the result could be under the federal constitution. The trial court could consider the argument that the warrantless arrests of nude dancers constituted a prior restraint that was invalid under Wash. Const. art. 1, § 5.


OUTCOME: The court reversed without prejudice the dismissal of the claims for injunctive and declaratory relief and to permit the individuals and corporation to place those claims before the trial court and argued them anew.

 

1987 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Stephenson v. Lehman


No. 51471-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 488



March 31, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Walla Walla County. Docket No: 01-2-00766-2. Date filed: 01/01/1800.
Stephenson v. Lehman, 116 Wn. App. 1029, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1634 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Superior court ruling denying petition for writ of habeas corpus affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of three counts of intimidating a judge. On appeal, his convictions were affirmed. The Superior Court of Walla Walla County (Washington) denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus, seeking relief from his convictions. Petitioner appealed, asserting in-part, that he had no "criminal intent" in filing the subject administrative claims, and therefore, was not guilty of intimidating a judge.


OVERVIEW: The basis of petitioner's convictions was that he filed a document entitled "certification of administrative foreign judgment" with a county auditor's office. The document named individuals, including three judges, and claimed that defendant was entitled to make a claim against them for over $ 500,000 in damages. Several of petitioner's claims were raised on direct appeal, and therefore, the appellate court declined to revisit those issues. Petitioner contended that the prosecutor improperly charged him with a crime in retaliation for exercising his First Amendment right to redress his grievances. The appellate court disagreed. Petitioner failed to demonstrate that the First Amendment gave him the right to file false liens and "certifications of administrative foreign judgment," as a means of threatening a judge. Nor did petitioner point to anything in the record showing that the prosecutor's motive in filing the charges was to retaliate against him for engaging in lawful conduct. Petitioner's claims that he had no "criminal intent" to intimidate a judge was rejected, as any rational trier of fact could have inferred that petitioner intended to communicate a threat to his victims.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, that petitioner was not entitled to habeas corpus relief, was affirmed.

State v. Wentz


No. 50172-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 494



March 31, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 01-1-01567-9. Date filed: 03/12/2002.
State v. Wentz, 116 Wn. App. 1026, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1621 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with rape of a child in the first degree, and, in the alternative, attempted rape of a child in the first degree. Following a bench trial in the Superior Court of King County (Washington), defendant was found guilty of attempted rape of a child in the first degree, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.44.073(1) and 9A.28.020. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly admitted child hearsay statements to, inter alia, the victim's mother, as the statements did not describe any act or attempted act of sexual contact, as required in Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120. Before trial, he argued that the child hearsay statements did not describe sexual contact, as there was no evidence that defendant touched the victim with his penis or touched her mouth for the purpose of gratifying sexual desire. The appellate court held that, given the victim's description of the taste test, the discovery of the condoms, defendant's admissions regarding his actions and purpose, and the lack of any other reasonable purpose besides sexual gratification, even with his version that he filled condoms with shampoo and placed them in the mouth of a blindfolded 9-year-old child, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the statements involved an act or attempted act of sexual contact and admitting the hearsay statements. The appellate court also held that a rational fact finder could have found from the evidence that defendant had taken a substantial step toward committing first degree child rape.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1989 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Suggs v. Hamilton


No. 27141-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 440



March 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Marriage of Suggs, 150 Wn.2d 1009, 79 P.3d 446, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 752 (2003)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by In re Marriage of Suggs, 152 Wn.2d 74, 93 P.3d 161, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 459 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 92-3-00648-5. Date filed: 03/08/2001.
Suggs v. Hamilton, 116 Wn. App. 1016, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1049 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Cowlitz County, Washington, granted appellee husband an anti-harassment protection order against appellant, his former wife, and also found the wife in contempt of court for violating a prior protection order. The wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife argued that the trial court erred when it issued an anti-harassment protection order against her, and punished her for violating the "no investigation" order. Former Wash. Rev. Code § 10.14.020(1) (1999) defined unlawful harassment as knowing and willful course of conduct directed at a specific person which seriously alarmed, annoyed, harassed, or was detrimental, and which served no legitimate or lawful purpose. The appellate court found that the wife intentionally made unfounded accusations about the husband designed to create a hostile environment and served no legal purpose. Wash. Rev. Code § 10.14.080(4) allowed for extended anti-harassment orders where the harassment was likely to resume when the order expired. An order of civil contempt had to contain a purge clause under which a contemnor had the ability to avoid a finding of contempt and/or incarceration for non-compliance. The wife had no ability to purge her contempt. The contempt penalty was punitive and not coercive and was, therefore, not a sanction available. The wife was not entitled to attorney fees where evidence supported the finding that the wife's behavior was intended to harm the husband.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the anti-harassment order and reversed as to the contempt order.

State v. Reed


No. 21028-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


116 Wn. App. 418; 66 P.3d 646; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 415



March 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish Opinion April 10, 2003.
Reported at State v. Reed, 116 Wn. App. 1014, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1040 (2003)
Review denied by State v. Reed, 150 Wn.2d 1013, 79 P.3d 447, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 763 (Wash., Nov. 4, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted defendant of second degree possession of stolen property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it: (1) denied her motion to suppress; and (2) added one point to her offender score for sentencing purposes by finding the current offense was committed while she was on community placement for a prior drug crime. The instant court found no evidence of trial court error. It agreed with defendant that the trial court's findings incorrectly stated that she did not make any type of statement prior to receiving her constitutional warnings. The record revealed that defendant told the officers how to find an allegedly stolen vehicle, although it was disputed whether the so-called statement was verbal or nonverbal. Nevertheless, the trial court's ultimate conclusion, regarding lack of threat or coercion regarding defendant's statement, was supported by the record. Regarding defendant's offender score, the parties agreed that defendant had, at a minimum, a score of seven. Defendant was under community placement at the time of the current offense, as she was subject to the conditions of the community custody ordered in her Drug Offender Sentencing Alternative sentence. As a result, defendant's offender score was properly calculated as eight.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1991 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Joyce v. Dep't of Corr.


No. 26499-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


116 Wn. App. 569; 75 P.3d 548; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 400



March 11, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Joyce v. State, 150 Wn.2d 1032, 84 P.3d 1229, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 72 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Joyce v. State, 155 Wn.2d 306, 119 P.3d 825, 2005 Wash. LEXIS 789 (Wash., Sept. 15, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: While under community supervision by the department of corrections (DOC), defendant caused an automobile accident that killed the decedent. Respondent family of the decedent sued the DOC, alleging, inter alia, negligent community supervision. Following a jury trial court, Pierce County Superior Court (Washington) awarded the family $ 22,453,645 in damages. The DOC appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the DOC argued, inter alia, that the facts did not support finding that the DOC's duty to control the defendant extended to the decedent or that its supervision of the defendant was the proximate cause of the decedent's death. The appellate court rejected these arguments. The family's evidence showed that, while under the DOC's supervision, defendant completely failed to fulfill his court ordered supervision requirements. Defendant had mental health problems that caused his behavior to be erratic and violent, and, while under community supervision, defendant was convicted of possession of stolen property after being pulled over for speeding in a stolen vehicle. This was sufficient evidence for a jury to find it foreseeable that defendant would continue to exercise poor or no judgment, continue to break the law, drive without a valid license, and potentially endanger the lives of others. Further, there was a special duty on the part of the DOC to control the defendant, as there was a clear public policy for imposing liability on the DOC for lax supervision of offenders. Thus, there was sufficient evidence for a jury to find proximate cause and cause in fact.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1992 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



City of Tacoma v. Cornell


No. 27422-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


116 Wn. App. 165; 64 P.3d 674; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 394



March 11, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City of Tacoma, Washington, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, dismissing the charge against defendant for violation of a protection order.


OVERVIEW: On September 14, a superior court commissioner issued a temporary order of protection order (TRO) against defendant for his former girlfriend. On September 16, the girlfriend filed a police report alleging that defendant had violated the TRO. On September 28, a superior court commissioner entered a permanent restraining order against defendant, and he sought revision and dismissal. The superior court found that the girlfriend's petition and supporting affidavit did not set forth the required allegations, and both the temporary and permanent protection orders were vacated on October 13. The city did not appeal the order vacating the temporary and permanent protection orders, and 11 days after the orders were vacated, the city charged defendant with violating the TRO on September 16. The appellate court ruled that the city had no underlying basis to charge defendant, as the city could not charge defendant for violating an order after the order had been vacated, even if the alleged violation occurred while the order was in effect. In other words, the city might have prevailed had it charged defendant for violating the order before it was vacated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1993 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Schoonover v. State


No. 27519-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


116 Wn. App. 171; 64 P.3d 677; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 395



March 11, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executed a durable power of attorney, authorizing his attorney to file a tort claim against respondent State of Washington on his behalf. The attorney filed the claim. The Thurston County Superior Court, Washington, granted the State's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, finding that appellant failed to personally verify his complaint as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.92.100. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The State placed appellant, who was mildly retarded, in foster care from the ages of 7 to 16 years old. During that time, he suffered repeated instances of mental, physical, and sexual abuse. The attorney prepared, verified, signed, and filed the claim against the State, but appellant did not personally verify the information in the claim form. Appellant argued that: (1) § 4.92.100 did not require that he personally verify his tort claim against the State; (2) the State was equitably estopped from raising the claim filing deficiency defense because it provided an outdated claim form and instructions; and (3) the personal verification requirement violated his right to equal protection. Strictly construing the statutory filing requirements, the instant court concluded that the attorney's verification was deficient. The power of attorney did not confer on the attorney any more authority than that of appellant's agent. Appellant failed to present sufficient evidence of his incapacitation to meet the incapacitation exception. Equitable estoppel did not apply because the interpretation of the statute was a legal matter. Appellant did not present an adequate equal protection challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1995 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Gladden


No. 20804-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


116 Wn. App. 561; 66 P.3d 1095; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 369



March 6, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published April 22, 2003.
Reported at State v. Gladden, 116 Wn. App. 1007, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1013 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Douglas County, Washington, convicted defendant of communication with a minor for immoral purposes under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090, which required proof of a prior conviction for a felony sex offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting evidence of his prior conviction for a felony sex offense when he was willing to stipulate to that element to avoid having the evidence introduced to the jury. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred by rejecting his proposed jury instruction as to the definition of "immoral purposes" under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090. The appellate court found that the trial court properly admitted the judgment and sentence related to the prior conviction because defendant did not offer to stipulate that he had a prior conviction for a felony sex offense. Instead, defendant offered to delete any reference to a statutory element that required proof of a prior conviction for a felony sex offense. Sexual misconduct was a sufficient context for the "immoral purposes" contemplated by the communications with a minor under § 9.68A.090. Defendant's counsel's failure to object to certain evidence was a legitimate trial tactic. Defense counsel's questioning of defendant's wife did not result in any prejudice to defendant. Defendant did not submit affidavits from exculpatory witnesses detailing their testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1996 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Everette


No. 20687-4-III CONSOLIDATED WITH 21034-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 370



March 6, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 01-1-01806-1. Judge signing: MICHAEL DONOHUE. Date filed: November 9, 2001. Proceedings Originating in Court of Appeals: April 12, 2002. Nature of Proceedings: PERSONAL RESTRAINT PETITION.
State v. Everette, 116 Wn. App. 1006, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1009 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the conviction and denied the personal restraint petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington), which arrested him on a bench warrant and convicted him of first-degree escape, pursuant to former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.110 (1982).


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to report to begin serving his sentence for a felony conviction, but was arrested on a bench warrant and charged with first-degree escape under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.110 (1982). A jury convicted him, but, on appeal, he contended that a court-ordered extension of the trial date violated the speedy trial rule. Additionally, he argued that he should have been charged with the more specific crime of failure to return from furlough. He raised additional issues in his consolidated personal restraint petition. The court affirmed, stating that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in granting a five-day trial extension, as he did not argue prejudice. Consequently, he failed to show that the trial court abused its discretion in granting the extension based on the deputy prosecutor's surgery, Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.3(d)(8). Further, because he was not released on furlough while in custody, he could not be charged with failure to return from furlough. The court concluded that he was not denied due process of law, as he failed to show any prejudice resulting from an allegedly defective bench warrant on the conviction for first-degree escape.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1997 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gonzalez


No. 20070-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 334



March 4, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: ADAMS. Docket No(s): 00-1-00093-6. Judge signing: RICHARD MILLER. Date filed: March 19, 2001.
State v. Gonzalez, 116 Wn. App. 1001, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 991 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Adams Superior Court County (Washington), which convicted him of escape, burglary, and theft. Specifically, defendant challenged his convictions, the denial of his motion to dismiss the escape charge, and the imposition of an exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was being moved to a holding cell in a police department, he escaped. After defendant was charged with several crimes, he filed a motion to dismiss the escape charge. Defendant was convicted, and the trial court imposed an exceptional sentence. In affirming, the court determined that the motion to dismiss was properly denied because a police department constituted a detention facility under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.010(2). Moreover, there was sufficient evidence presented to sustain his conviction on the escape charge. The State was not required to present a witness to testify that the police department was a detention facility. In addition, the trial court did not err in imposing an exceptional sentence. The standard sentencing range would have been "clearly too lenient" based on defendant's high offender score. The trial court was also not required to submit the underlying factual determinations to a jury before imposing the sentence. The court noted that defendant's convictions did not violate double jeopardy because burglary and theft were separate offenses. Finally, the court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.050 was not an unconstitutional bill of attainder.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1998 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guerrero


No. 50648-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 329



March 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Guerrero, 115 Wn. App. 1057, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 900 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 011089974. Date filed: 06/21/2002. Judge signing: Hon. Charles W. Mertel.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of King County (Washington), of possession of heroin, delivery of cocaine, and possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. The trial court applied the school bus route stop enhancement contained in Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(a) in imposing sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested along with a female co-defendant, after they sold crack cocaine to an undercover police officer. In a search incident to arrest, a plastic baggie containing 2.44 grams of crack cocaine was found in defendant's underwear and a bindle of heroin weighing .4 grams in his sock. The jury also entered special verdicts finding that the cocaine possession and delivery offenses occurred within 1000 feet of a school bus route stop. Defendant argued on appeal that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, that Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(a) was unconstitutionally vague, and that the trial erred in applying the school bus stop enhancement. The appellate court held that the circumstances of the crime and the amount of drugs involved supported the inference that defendant possessed the drugs with intent to deliver. The constitutionality of the statute had been upheld in Coria. Testimony of an official of the school district established that the crime occurred within 1000 feet of an identifiable school bus stop and that defendant could readily determine that fact.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1999 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lillard


No. 49224-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 330



March 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 001023329. Date filed: 08/17/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth Cowsert.
State v. Lillard, 115 Wn. App. 1054, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 885 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) of seven counts of forgery and one count of first degree theft. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain convictions for forgery. The court of appeals disagreed. The checks defendant wrote bore the business's account number and were from the business's bank. Any rational fact-finder could have concluded from that that the checks were drawn from the same account, regardless of which city or bank branch was written on the checks. Even assuming that the accounts were different, defendant admitted that he did not open either of the checking accounts. Mildly stated, his claim -- that to satisfy a debt, a friend had opened two separate checking accounts in defendant's name, deposited money in them, and then gave defendant blank checks bearing his name and address -- strained credulity. The jury was entitled to reject that claim and find that defendant was unauthorized to write checks on either of the two accounts and that he forged the checks. Viewed in the light most favorable to the State, there was sufficient evidence to prove forgery.


OUTCOME: The first degree theft conviction was reversed and remanded for entry of a second degree theft conviction. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

2000 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Johnson


No. 20858-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


115 Wn. App. 890; 64 P.3d 88; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 306



February 27, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted defendant of malicious harassment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threatened a female police officer, using vicious, vile invectives directed at the officer. The trial judge found that defendant did it because the officer was a woman. Defendant argued that the State did not show that he selected the officer because of her gender. Although defendant conceded that the terms he used were offensive and vulgar, he argued that their meanings did not provide a basis for the trial court's finding that defendant's "method of attack" and threats were made because the officer was a woman. The appellate court concluded that the trial court's determination that defendant threatened to mutilate the officer's sexual organs was supported by substantial evidence. The officer testified and the trial court entered an unchallenged finding that defendant stated that he would slit the officer from her genitalia to her throat. Although defendant argued that because this threat was one of disembowelment rather than mutilation of female genitalia, it was not supported by substantial evidence. A fair-minded, rational person could have easily concluded otherwise. Defendant did not hurl abuse at a male transit officer at the time of the incident.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
